Ruling of the Absolute Command: Immediate or Delayed? (Usul al-Fiqh)
Determining whether absolute commands obligate immediate or delayed action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on whether an absolute command obligates immediate or delayed action, explain the key proofs for tarakhi, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The absolute command obligates delayed performance, not immediate, unless a time is specified.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi tackles a foundational question in Hanafi legal theory: does a command without a time restriction require immediate obedience? The school's established position (mufta bihi) is that it permits delay (tarakhi), as long as the act is completed within one's lifetime. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the intra-madhhab dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position on absolute command: performance is obligatory with delay (tarakhi), provided it is not missed in one's lifetime.
Contrast with the view of those who say fawr (immediate).
2
Understand the dispute
Note that some Hanafis (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in one report) held fawr, but the relied-upon view is tarakhi.
The opposing school is the majority of 'our companions' and hadith scholars.
3
Examine the proofs
Analyze the three main arguments for tarakhi: a) command seeks future occurrence, b) ease/facilitation, c) consequence of fawr leading to qada' being counted as ada' (contrary to consensus).
Also note the condition based on ghalabat al-zann.
4
Apply to examples
Zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, and 'ushr are absolute commands; delay does not incur sin unless missed entirely.
If the nisab is lost, the obligation falls.
5
Note the condition
The permissibility of delay is conditional on the obligation not being missed in one's lifetime, determined by ghalabat al-zann.
Sudden death is a rarity upon which rulings cannot be based.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المأمور به وحكم المطلق: أن يكون الأداء واجباً على التراخي بشرط أن لا يفوته في العمر. وعلى هذا قال محمد رحمه الله في الجامع الكبير: لو نذر أن يعتكف شهرا فله أن يعتكف أي شهر شاء. ولو نذر أن يصوم شهراً فله أن يصوم أي شهر شاء. وفي الزكاة وصدقة الفطر والعشر المذهب المعلوم: أنه لا يصير بالتأخير مفرطاً. وحكم المطلق إلخ: جواب سوال وهو أن كل المأمور به يؤدي في وقت فكيف يكون المأمور به منقسماً إلى خلاف المطلق عن الوقت وإلى المقيد به وحاصل الجواب أن المراد بالمطلق عدم التعين بالوقت وبالمقيد تعيينه. واجباً على التراخي: أي جاز تأخيره في أي وقت يأتي المأمور بذلك المأمور به المطلق، وهذا مذهب جمهور أصحابنا أنه على الفور، وهو قول عامة أهل الحديث وبعض المعتزلة، وذكر أبو سهل الزجاجي أنه عند أبي يوسف بحاله على الفور، وعند محمد والشافعي حملها على التراخي، وروي عن أبي حنيفة عليه أنه على الفور كذا قيل، والصحيح ما قلنا؛ لأن الأمر لطلب إيقاع المصدر في المستقبل، وخصوص الوقت إنما هو بخصوص المادة كما في اشتر اللحم بناء على أن له ضرورة إلى أكله اليوم، وطلب إيقاع فعل مطلق، فيجعل الامتثال به بإيقاعه في أي جزء كان في المستقبل، ولو كان على الفور كان مقيداً بالوقت ولم يبق مطلقاً وهو المفروض، ولأن إطلاق الأمر عن قيد الوقت للتيسر والتسهيل فلو حمل على الفور لعاد على موضوعه بالنقض؛ لأنه على هذا يكون أعسر وأصعب من المقيد أيضاً، فيزول اليسر إلى أشد العسر والحرج، ولأن لو كان محمولاً على الفور ويراد الفور من الأمر كان الفعل المأمور به بعد الفور غير مأمور به بل مثله؛ لأنه ليس على وفق الأمر فيلزم أن يكون قضاء لأداء، وهو خلاف الإجماع كذا في الحصول. بشرط أن لا يفوته إلخ جواب سوال وهو: أن المرء لا يعلم عمر نفسه، فيكون تعليق جواز التأخير بشرط عدم الفوات في العمر تعليقا بشرط لا يمكن الوقوف عليه وهو باطل، وحاصل الجواب : أن ذلك يعلم باعتبار غلبة الظن بأن يؤخره إلى زمان لم يغلب على ظنه فواته وغلبة تفيد العلم والموت مفاجاة نادر لا يصلح لابتناء الأحكام عليه. لا يصير إلخ لإطلاق الأمر بالزكاة، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وآتوا الزكاة﴾، وبصدقة الفطر، وهو قوله عليه السلام: أدوا عن كل حر وعبد، وبالعشر وهو قوله عليه السلام: ما سقته السماء ففيه العشر، وكل واحد منها مطلق عن الوقت، فلهذا لا يصير بالتأخير مفرطاً أي مقصراً كذا في الفصول. فإنه لو هلك النصاب سقط الواجب، والحانث إذا ذهب ماله وصار فقيراً كفر بالصوم. لسقوط الواجب وعلى هذا لا يجب قضاء الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة؛ لأنه لما وجب مطلقاً وجب القضاء كاملاً، فلا يخرج عن العهدة بأداء الناقص، فيجوز العصر عند الإحمرار أداء ولا يجوز قضاء. وعن الكرخي له أن موجب الأمر المطلق الوجوب على الفور، والخلاف معه في الوجوب، ولا خلاف في أن المسارعة إلى الائتمار مندوب إليها. وأما الموقت فنوعان: نوع يكون الوقت ظرفاً للفعل، حتى لا يشترط استيعاب كل الوقت، ولا يفضل المظروف عنه يسمى معياراً كوقت الصوم. وفي حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: وتفسير الظرف أن يكون الفعل واقعاً فيه لا مقدماً به أي: يكون وقته الذي وقته له الشارع يسعه ويسع غيره من جنسه، ويسمى الظرف موسعا.
Chapter on the Commanded Action. The ruling of the absolute (command): that the performance is obligatory with delay (tarakhi), on condition that it is not missed in one's lifetime. And upon this, Muhammad (r) said in al-Jami' al-Kabir: If one vows to perform i'tikaf for a month, he may perform i'tikaf in any month he wishes. And if one vows to fast a month, he may fast any month he wishes. With regard to zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, and 'ushr, the known madhhab is that one does not become negligent by delaying. 'And the ruling of the absolute...' etc. is an answer to a question, namely: every commanded action is performed at a time, so how can the commanded action be divided into absolute with respect to time and restricted to it? The summary of the answer is that by absolute is meant not being specified to a time, and by restricted is meant its specification. 'Obligatory with delay' means it is permissible to delay it to any time the person performs that absolute commanded action. And this is the madhhab of the majority of our companions, that it is immediate; and it is the statement of the general people of hadith and some Mu'tazila. Abu Sahl al-Zajjaji mentioned that according to Abu Yusuf it remains immediate, and according to Muhammad and al-Shafi'i it is carried upon delay. And it is reported from Abu Hanifa (r) that it is immediate, it was said thus. But the correct is what we said, because the command is to request the occurrence of the verbal noun in the future, and the particularity of time is only due to particularity of the matter, as in 'buy meat' based on his need to eat it today. And the request to perform an absolute act, so compliance with it is achieved by performing it in any future part. If it were immediate, it would be restricted by time and would not remain absolute, which is the presupposed. And because freeing the command from the restriction of time is for ease and facility; if it were interpreted as immediate, it would contradict its subject, because then it would be more difficult and harder than the restricted, removing ease into extreme difficulty and hardship. And because if it were interpreted as immediate and immediacy were intended from the command, then the commanded act after the immediate time would not be commanded but like it; because it is not in accordance with the command, leading to a substitute being a performance, which is contrary to consensus, as in al-Husul. 'On condition that it is not missed' etc. is an answer to a question: that one does not know his own lifespan, so tying the permissibility of delay to the condition of not missing it in one's lifetime is a condition that cannot be ascertained, which is invalid. The summary of the answer: that it is known by considering overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann) that he delays to a time when he does not have an overwhelming probability of missing it, and overwhelming probability yields knowledge, and sudden death is a rarity upon which rulings cannot be based. 'One does not become' etc. due to the absoluteness of the command for zakat, which is His statement (Exalted): 'And give zakah,' and for sadaqat al-fitr, which is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Give on behalf of every free person and slave,' and for 'ushr, which is his statement (peace be upon him): 'What the sky waters has one-tenth.' Each of these is absolute with respect to time, so for this one does not become negligent by delaying, i.e., falling short, as in al-Fusul. Thus if the nisab is lost, the obligation falls, and if one who has broken an oath loses his wealth and becomes poor, he expiates by fasting. 'For the falling of the obligation' and upon this, the make-up of prayer is not obligatory in the disliked times; because when it became obligatory absolutely, the make-up became obligatory completely, so one does not fulfill the responsibility by performing an incomplete performance. So the afternoon prayer at the time of redness is valid as an on-time performance, but not as a make-up. From al-Karkhi he has that the necessitation of the absolute command is obligation on the spot (fawr), and the dispute with him is about the obligation, and there is no dispute that hastening to comply is recommended. As for the time-bound (muwaqqat), it is of two types: a type where the time is a vessel (zarf) for the act, such that encompassing all the time is not required, and a type where the time is a standard (mi'yar) such that the act does not exceed it, as in the time of fasting. In the Hashiyah of al-Shaykh Akram al-Nadawi: The interpretation of zarf is that the act occurs within it, not preceding it: i.e., its time that the Lawgiver has assigned to it accommodates it and accommodates other acts of its kind, and it is called an expansive vessel (zarf musawwa').
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of an absolute command (al-amr al-mutlaq) in Hanafi usul. The author begins by stating the ruling: the performance of an absolute command is obligatory with delay (tarakhi), meaning it is permissible to postpone it to any time within one's lifetime, provided that one does not miss it entirely. This is contrasted with a restricted command (muqayyad) that specifies a particular time. The author provides examples from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Kabir: a vow to perform i'tikaf or fast for a month may be fulfilled in any month, because the command is absolute. Similarly, obligations like zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, and 'ushr are absolute in time, so delaying them does not make one negligent. The author then addresses a potential objection: how can a commanded action be divided into absolute and restricted? The answer is that 'absolute' here means not specified to a particular time, while 'restricted' means specified. The author clarifies that the view of the majority of our companions (جمهور أصحابنا) is that the absolute command is on delay (tarakhi), but he notes that there is a report from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that it is immediate (fawr). However, the correct position (الصحيح) is tarakhi, supported by several rational proofs. First, the command seeks the occurrence of the act in the future; specificity of time is only due to the specific context of the matter. If it were immediate, the command would be restricted and would not remain absolute. Second, freeing the command from time restriction is for ease; interpreting it as immediate would make it harder than even restricted commands, defeating the purpose of facilitation. Third, if it were immediate, the act performed after the immediate time would not be commanded, leading to the absurdity that a make-up (qada') would be considered a performance (ada'), contrary to consensus. The passage then addresses the condition 'provided it is not missed in one's lifetime', explaining that the permissibility of delay is based on overwhelming probability (ghalabat al-zann), not certainty, since death is rare. Further evidence is cited from Quran and Hadith that zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, and 'ushr are absolute commands, so delaying does not incur sin. Practical examples are given: if the nisab is lost after the year, zakat is waived, and an oath-breaker who becomes poor may expiate by fasting instead of financial expiation. Finally, the passage discusses time-bound acts (muwaqqat), distinguishing between time as a vessel (zarf) where the act does not require full time, and time as a standard (mi'yar) where the act must fill the entire time, like fasting.

Key Terms
المطلق (al-mutlaq): ما لم يتقيد بوقت معين في الأمر
التراخي (al-tarakhi): جواز تأخير الفعل المأمور به إلى أي وقت من أوقات الإمكان في العمر
الفور (al-fawr): وجوب تعجيل الأداء في أول وقت الإمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on an absolute command?
A) Immediate obligation if possible
B) Delayed obligation conditional on not missing it in lifetime
C) Immediate obligation with option of delay
D) No obligation until a time is fixed

Key Takeaway
The absolute command in Hanafi usul obligates delayed performance, not immediate, as long as the act is completed before death.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
12 min
Absolute Command: Immediacy vs. Delay and Time-Bound Obligations
Commentary on the commanded act: fawr dispute and time classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether an absolute command implies immediate performance and distinguish between time as a container and time as a measure, deriving the respective rulings.

Core Idea
An absolute command does not require immediacy; time either contains or measures the act, determining rules of intention and competition.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi tackles two foundational questions in Hanafi usul: what does a bare command really demand, and how does the nature of time shape the obligation? By working through concrete fiqh examples—zakat and expiation—the author demonstrates that delay is not sinful, contrary to a minority view. Then, moving to time-bound acts, the text introduces a powerful distinction between time as a container (like prayer time) and time as a measure (like fasting day), each carrying its own rules about competing acts and the need for specific intention. Understanding this unlocks the logic behind many practical rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Find the core question: does an absolute command (amr mutlaq) oblige immediate action (fawr) or permit delay (tarakhi)? Note that the text states the Hanafi position that delay is permissible, and contrasts it with the view of al-Karkhi.
The dispute is only about obligation, not recommendation.
2
Examine the proofs
Work through the two examples: (a) zakat: if nisab is destroyed after the year, the obligation falls with no sin for delay; (b) expiation: an oath-breaker who delays financial expiation while rich, then becomes poor, may fast—if delay were sinful, fasting wouldn't suffice. This proves delay does not incur sin.
These are dalil naqli (transmitted evidence) from Quranic verses.
3
Apply the classification of time
The text divides time-bound commands into two types. Identify each: (1) time as a container (zarf) – the act occurs within it but does not fill it; prayer is the example. (2) time as a measure (mi'yar) – the act occupies the entire time; fasting is the example.
The terms 'zarf' and 'mi'yar' are technical in Hanafi usul.
4
Derive the rulings for container time
For container time: (a) the obligation of one act does not forbid another similar act (e.g., supererogatory prayers in Dhuhr time), (b) the commanded act requires a specific intention (niyyah mu'ayyanah) because other acts are legally possible; even when time is tight, intention is needed because competition remains in principle.
The intention must specify the act person- or type-specifically.
5
Derive the rulings for measure time
For measure time: (a) no other act of the same kind can be performed in that time (e.g., no voluntary fast during Ramadan), (b) the time is determined by the Lawgiver and cannot be changed; a vow to fast in Ramadan is not binding because the time is already occupied by the obligatory fast.
The measure type leaves no room for substitution.

First research on the Book of Allah. Chapter on the commanded act. If the nisab is destroyed, the obligation falls. And a person who breaks an oath, if his wealth is gone and he becomes poor, he expiates by fasting. For the fall of obligation. And accordingly, the making up of prayer in disliked times is not obligatory; because when it was obligatory absolutely, the full making up becomes obligatory, so one does not discharge the duty by performing a deficient act. Thus, the afternoon prayer at the time of redness is permissible as performance but not as make-up. [commentary]: From Karkhi: He holds that the requirement of an absolute command is obligation immediately. The disagreement with him is about obligation, and there is no disagreement that hastening to comply is recommended. Immediately. As for time-bound commands, there are two types: one type where time is a container for the act, so that it is not necessary to occupy the entire time [with the act]; it is not a measure. The explanation: 'If the nisab is destroyed etc.' is proof that the obligated person does not become negligent by delaying. Because if the nisab is destroyed after the completion of the year before paying zakat, the obligation falls from the liability and he does not sin. And if he were negligent in delaying or paying zakat, the obligation would remain on the liability and he would sin for the delay, as in 'al-Ma'din'. 'If his wealth is gone': That the oath-breaker is commanded with a financial expiation first when wealth is present, and fasting when he lacks it. His saying, Allah Almighty: 'Then its expiation is feeding ten needy persons from the average of what you feed your own families, or clothing them, or freeing a slave. But whoever cannot find [or afford] it, then a fast of three days.' The command for financial expiation is absolute. So if he delays it while possessing wealth, he is not negligent. Then if his wealth goes and he becomes poor, he expiates by fasting and is not taken for the financial expiation; because he was not negligent by delaying. And if the absolute command were for immediacy, he would be taken for the financial expiation and it would not suffice as expiation by fasting, and he would be negligent in delaying, as in some footnotes. The disliked times: sunrise until it rises and becomes white to the extent of a spear or two, and the sun's zenith until it declines and inclines from the middle of the sky toward the west, and the sun's yellowing and weakening until the eye can face it. [al-Shafi, p. 138]. 'Immediately': i.e., instantly without delay, and the interpretation of immediacy is that performance must be hastened after the command arises in the first possible time of performance, so he sins by delaying from the first possible time, but his sin is dependent on performance, so if he performs afterward, that sin is removed, as in 'al-Ma'din'. 'Container for the act': i.e., for performing the commanded act. Then 'container' in language is a general noun that includes both a container that is larger than its contents and a container that is not larger, but in the terminology of the Imams of usul, this term is specific to every container that is larger than its contents; what does not have the contents larger than it is called a 'measure' like the time of fasting, as in 'al-Ma'din'. And in the 'Hashiyah of Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi, p. 104: The interpretation of 'container' is that the act occurs within it, not that it is advanced by it, i.e., its time that the Lawgiver specified for it accommodates it and accommodates other acts of its kind, and it is called an expanded container. [PAGE_093] First research on the Book of Allah. Chapter on the commanded act. Time for the act like prayer. [commentary]: 'The obligatory' and among the rulings of this type is that the obligation of the act in it does not negate the obligation of another act of its kind in it, so that if he vows to pray such-and-such rak'ahs in the time of Dhuhr, it is incumbent. 'The time', 'the vower', 'the obligated'. And among its rulings: that the obligation of prayer in it does not negate the validity of another prayer in it, so that if he occupies the entire time of Dhuhr with other than Dhuhr, it is permissible. Its ruling: that the commanded act is only performed with a specific intention; because other acts are prescribed in the time, and from the commanded act, valid, it is not determined by the act itself even if the time is tight; because the consideration of intention is due to the competition, and competition remains when time is tight. The second type: where time is a measure for it, such as fasting; for it is measured by time, which is the day. Its ruling: that if the Lawgiver specifies a time for it, no other act is obligatory in that time, and it is not permissible to perform other acts in it, so that a healthy resident, if he performs his abstention in Ramadan for another obligation, it falls for [that other]? [commentary]: 'His abstention'... The evidence for its being a container is that it is not necessary to occupy the entire time with prayer. The interpretation of the container nature of time here: that it occurs with the possibility of surplus beyond the performance of the act, except with a specific intention: i.e., except with an intention of specifying the commanded act person-specifically or type-specifically so that the intended object applies only to this commanded act, and it is not necessary to specify the number of rak'ahs or observe the meaning of performance or residence or travel and the like. Rather, specification in intention is obligatory because the container nature accommodates other acts, and specification in intention pushes away the possible competitor for valid legal existence. This remains until the end of time, even if it becomes tight and becomes a measure in reality not by the Lawgiver. So the validity of the existence of the competitor, i.e., other than the commanded act, remains; because if he prays something else, the prayer would be valid, so specification is also obligatory. 'It remains etc.': i.e., competition from other acts, which is the validity of the time-bound act with it; because it is not specified for the commanded act even if the choice of the servant falls due to tight time. 'Measure for it': i.e., the act measure; the measure of a thing is what it is measured by. What is meant here is the time that the act occupies and does not leave surplus, and it is measured, so it lengthens with the length of time and shortens with its shortness, as in 'al-Ma'din'. 'No other act is obligatory in that time', so that if he vows to fast in Ramadan, it is not obligatory to perform it, and therefore it is not permissible in it; because the time does not accommodate two fasts, and it is not for him to change the Law, so it is determined by what is obligated legally, and no other is obligatory, as in 'al-Ma'din'.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter 'Al-Ma'mur Bih' (The Commanded Act) from Usul al-Shashi. It addresses two key usul topics: (1) whether an absolute command (amr mutlaq) implies immediate performance (fawr) or allows delay (tarakhi), and (2) the classification of time-bound commands (muwaqqat) into two types: time as a container (zarf) and time as a measure (mi'yar).

The discussion begins with fiqh examples: if the zakatable nisab is destroyed before payment, the obligation falls, proving that delay is not sinful. Similarly, an oath-breaker who delays financial expiation while wealthy, then becomes poor, may expiate by fasting; this would be invalid if the command required immediacy. These examples demonstrate that the absolute command does not obligate immediate action, contrary to the view of al-Karkhi. The passage clarifies that the dispute with Karkhi is only about obligation (wujub), not about the recommendation (nadb) of hastening—all agree that quickly complying is recommended.

Then the text moves to time-bound commands. The first type is where time is a container (zarf): the act occurs within the time, but the time can accommodate other similar acts. Prayer is the example—its time is a container. Rulings: (a) the obligation of one prayer does not negate the validity of another prayer in the same time (e.g., supererogatory prayers during Dhuhr time), (b) the commanded act requires a specific intention (niyyah mu'ayyana) because the container nature allows competing acts; even when time becomes tight, the intention remains necessary because the possibility of another valid act persists in principle.

The second type is where time is a measure (mi'yar): the act fills the time entirely, leaving no room for another. Fasting is the example—its time is the entire day. Ruling: in such a time, no other act of the same kind can be performed; e.g., during Ramadan, one cannot fast for a vow unless it coincides with the Ramadan obligation. The time is determined by what the Lawgiver has prescribed, and no substitute is allowed.

The commentary stays strictly within Hanafi usul, referencing authoritative works like 'al-Ma'din' and al-Shafi. The key takeaway is that understanding the nature of time vis-à-vis the commanded act determines rules of intention, competition, and obligation.

Key Terms
الأمر المطلق (al-amr al-mutlaq): A command that does not contain any indication of time or condition requiring immediate or delayed performance.
الفور (al-fawr): Immediate performance at the first possible moment after the command; delaying is sinful.
التراخي (al-tarakhi): Delay is permissible; the command can be performed at any time within the legally allowed period.
الوقت الظرف (al-waqt al-zarf): Time that acts as a container for an act, permitting the act to be performed within it and also allowing other similar acts.
الوقت المعيار (al-waqt al-mi'yar): Time that acts as a measure for an act, fully occupied by the act such that no other similar act can be performed in the same time.
النِّيَّةُ الْمُعَيَّنَةُ (al-niyyah al-mu'ayyanah): A specific intention that distinguishes the commanded act from other legally valid acts that could be performed in the same time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidence that an absolute command does not require immediate performance?
A) The example of zakat: if the nisab is destroyed after a year but before payment, the obligation falls and the person does not sin.
B) The Prophet said 'Do not hasten' in a hadith.
C) Consensus of the companions that commands are not immediate.
D) All absolute commands are actually recommendations.

Key Takeaway
An absolute command does not obligate immediate action; time-bound commands are either containers (allowing other acts with specific intention) or measures (excluding other acts).

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Definition of Fasting and the Necessity of Intention
Defining fasting and the essential role of intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fasting and explain why intention is a condition for its validity.

Core Idea
Fasting is intentional refraining; without intention, it is mere hunger, not worship.

The text begins by clarifying a key principle: when the time for an obligation is fixed by Sharia (like Ramadan), specification of intention (ta'yin) is not required, but the original intention (niyyah) is still essential. It then defines fasting as an act of worship that inherently requires intention, and addresses a special case for travelers and the sick, highlighting the flexibility of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Determine what act is being defined (fasting) and its legal classification (obligatory worship). Note that the passage is part of Usul al-Fiqh, so the definition establishes the legal meaning of the term.
Fasting is a commanded act (ma'mur bihi) classified under acts of worship.
2
Extract the legal definition from the text
Locate the precise phrasing: 'الصوم شرعاً هو الإمساك عن الأكل والشرب والجماع نهارا مع النية'. This is the Hanafi definition. Notice the inclusion of intention as a defining element.
The definition has two components: physical restraint (imsak) and intention (niyya).
3
Analyze the role of intention
The text states that refraining (imsak) does not become fasting (sawm) except with intention. Intention distinguishes worship from custom (adah). Determine whether intention is a condition (shart) or a pillar (rukn) – here it is a condition for validity.
Hanafi: niyya is a shart, not a rukn; it must be present at the beginning of the act.
4
Note the exception for traveler and sick
The passage adds a qualification: for a traveler or sick person, if they intend another obligation during Ramadan, it counts as what they intended, not Ramadan. This shows that the ruling is restricted to the healthy resident (muqim sahih).
This is based on Abu Hanifa's view; the Sahibayn may differ, but the text follows Abu Hanifa.

البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في المأمور به

رمضان لا عما نوى، وإذا اندفع المزاحم في الوقت سقط اشتراط التعيين فإن ذلك لقطع المزاحمة، ولا يسقط أصل النية؛ لأن الإمساك لا يصير صوماً إلا بالنية، فإن الصوم شرعاً هو الإمساك عن الأكل والشرب والجماع نهارا مع النية. لا عما نوى: لأن الشرع لما عين للمعيار صوماً بصفة، فإذا أراد المكلف تغيير صفة لم يقدر عليه، وهذا كمن آجر نفسه في وقت معين للخياطة فخاط له ثم قصد التبرع في ذلك الوقت لم يكن تبرعا بل يكون إجازة، وإنما قيد بالصحيح المقيم احترازاً عن المسافر والمريض على قول أبي حنيفة محله؛ فإنه عنده إذا نوى المريض أو المسافر في رمضان عن واجب آخر يقع عما نوى؛ لأنه لما ثبت لهما الترخص لمصالح البدن وهو الفطر، فلأن يثبت لمصالح الدين وهي قضاء ما عليه من الدين أولى كذا في "الفصول". وإذا اندفع إلخ : وهو غير هذا الصوم بأن لا يجوز في الوقت وفسر بعدم الجواز؛ لئلا يتوهم أن المراد بقوله: وإذا اندفع المزاحم المزاحم في الأولوية. سقط إلخ وعند الشافعي له: يشترط التعيين؛ لأنه وجد من الشارع فلابد أن من يتعين من جهة العبد ليكون مختارا في ذلك لا مجبورا، قلنا: إطلاق العبد في مثل هذا التعيين؛ لأنه في أصل الصوم مختار، فهو مخاطب في هذا اليوم بالصوم لا بالتعيين؛ لأنه قد حصل من الشارع، فلا حاجة إلى تعيين العبد فاحفظه. اشتراط التعيين: أي لما كان اشتراط التعيين لقطع المزاحم في الوقت، فلما اندفع المزاحم سقط اشتراط التعيين؛ لأنه لما تعين في رمضان أصيب لمطلق الاسم، وبالخطاء في الوصف كالمتعين في مكان ينال باسم الجنس والنوع كما يزال باسم العلم، فإن زيدا لو نوى ينال إنسان أو يا رجل وهو منفرد في الدار كان كما قيل: يا زيد وينال بالخطاء في الوصف كما لو نوى الرجل الأبيض وهو منفرد في الدار بيد أيها الرجل الأسود وينال بهذا؛ لأن الأسود بطل فبقي اسم الجنس الذي يصلح اسما له كذا قيل. وهكذا تعيين الصوم بأن يضاف الصوم إلى رمضان بأن يقول المكلف: نويت صوم رمضان ولا يسقط إلخ جواب سوال، وهو: أنه لما تعين الوقت لصوم رمضان فينبغي أن يسقط أصل النية ويتأدى بلا نية من الصحيح المقيم. هو الإمساك إلخ الأحسن أن يقال: هو الإمساك عن الأكل والشرب والجماع حقيقة أو حكما عمدا من طلوع الفجر إلى غروب الشمس؛ لئلا يرد أكل الناسي وشربه وجماعه وأكل السمسم وما في الأسنان أقل من الحمص وأمثلهما عكسا، والاستمناء باليد والتفخيذ وأمثالهما، والإمساك من طلوع الشمس لا قبله طردا؛ لأنه عرفا من طلوعها إلى غروبها، والمأخوذ في الحدود المعاني العرفية المتبادر إلا أن يقال: المعتبر في الصناعات الشرعية المعاني الشرعية، والنهار الشرعي من طلوع الفجر إلا أن نهاريته ليس بعام؛ فإن وقت الفجر إنما يعد من النهار في حق الصوم خاصة دون الصلاة حتى لم يكن صلاته عجماء بل جهرية وقد ورد صلاة النهار عجماء كذا في "الفصول".

البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في المأمور به

وإن لم يعين الشرع له وقتا، فإنه لا يتعين الوقت له بتعيين العبد، حتى لو عين العبد أياما لقضاء رمضان لا تتعين هي للقضاء، ويجوز فيها صوم الكفارة والنفل، ويجوز قضاء تلك الأيام في رمضان فيها وغيرها.
ومن حكم هذا النوع: أنه يشترط تعيين النية لوجود المزاحم، ثم للعبد أن يوجب شيئا على نفسه مؤقتا أو غير موقت وليس له تغيير حكم الشرع. مثاله: إذا نذر أن يصوم يوما بعينه لزمه ذلك، ولو صامه عن قضاء رمضان أو عن كفارة يمينه جاز؛ لأن الشرع جعل القضاء مطلقا، مع النية: لأنه عبادة، ولا عبادة بدون النية؛ ليمتاز عن العادة؛ ولأن العبادة لابد فيها من الإخلاص، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أُمِرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مُخْلِصِينَ لَهُ الدِّينَ﴾ الآية، والإخلاص لا يكون إلا بالنية كذا في "المعدن".
وإن لم يعين الشرع إلخ : هذا بيان القسم الثاني من نوعي المعيار أي ما لم يعين الشرع له وقتا كقضاء فإنه ليس له وقت معين؛ لإطلاق الأيام في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ﴾، فإنه لا يتعين الوقت له بتعيين العبد؛ لأنه تغيير حكم الشرع من الإطلاق إلى التقييد ليس ذلك للعبد، وتشترط فيه نية التعيين أي يشترط في هذا القسم من الوقت نية التعيين بأن يقول: نويت للقضاء أو المنذور، ولا يتأدى بمطلق النية، ولا بنية النفل أو واجب آخر فافهم.
لا يتعين إلخ لأنه تغير حكم الشرع من الإطلاق إلى التقييد وليس ذلك للعبد. تعيين النية: بأن ينوي قضاء رمضان مثلا، ولا يكفيه نية مطلق صوم الفرض أو مطلق القضاء. لوجود المزاحم: بعدم تعيين الوقت له شرعا، وشرعية كل صوم من الواجب والنفل في كل يوم من الأيام غير الأيام الممنوعة والحيض والنفاس. ثم للعبد إلخ هذا اعتراض ومحصوله : أن للعبد أن يوجب على نفسه شيئا لم يكن واجبا، فكيف لا يكون له أن يعين على نفسه بعض الواجبات بوقت مع أن التعيين دون الإيجاب؛ لأن إثبات الوصف أدنى من إثبات الأصل، فأجاب المصنف بأن تعيين بعض الأوقات تغيير حكم الشرع وليس للعبد ذلك وإن كان له إيجاب شيء على نفسه، والأقرب أن يجعل قوله ثم للعبد كالتفريع على الأول، وتقديره: إذا تحققت أنه لا يتعين الوقت بتعيين العبد فاعلم بعد ذلك أن للعبد أن يوجب شيئا على نفسه، وإذا تعلق بما أوجب عليه حكم الشرع ليس له تغييره كذا في "الفصول".
The first research in the Book of Allah. Section on the commanded act. Ramadan, not what he intended. And when the competing obligation is removed in the time, the requirement of specification falls away, because that is to remove competition. And the original intention does not fall away, because refraining does not become fasting except with intention. For fasting in Sharia is refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse during the day with intention. 'Not what he intended': because when Sharia specified for the standard a fast with a description, if the obligated person wants to change the description, he cannot, and this is like one who hires himself at a specific time for sewing, and sews for him, then intends charity in that time, it is not charity but rather a hire. And it is only restricted to the healthy resident to exclude the traveler and the sick according to Abu Hanifa's opinion in its place; for according to him, if the sick or traveler intends in Ramadan for another obligation, it occurs for what he intended, because since they have been granted concession for bodily interests, which is breaking the fast, then to establish it for religious interests—which is fulfilling what he owes of religious duties—is more appropriate. As in al-Fusul. 'And when the competing obligation is removed, etc.': And it is other than this fast in that it is not permissible in the time and is interpreted as non-permissibility, lest one imagine that what is meant by his saying 'and when the competing obligation is removed' is competition in priority. 'It falls away, etc.' And according to al-Shafi'i, specification is required, because it exists from the Lawgiver, so it is necessary that the specification come from the slave so that he is voluntary in that, not compelled. We say: the slave is unrestricted in such specification, because in the original fast he is voluntary, so he is addressed in this day regarding the fast, not regarding specification, because it has been obtained from the Lawgiver, so there is no need for specification by the slave. So memorize it. 'Requirement of specification': meaning, when the requirement of specification was to remove the competing obligation in the time, when the competing obligation was removed, the requirement of specification falls away. Because when it was specified in Ramadan, it is attained by the absolute name, and by error in the description, like the specified in a place is attained by the genus and species name just as it is removed by the proper name. For if Zaid intended to attain a human or O man, and he is alone in the house, it is as if he said: O Zaid, and is attained by error in the description, as if he intended the white man while he is alone in the house, and said O black man, he is attained by this, because the black is invalid, so the genus name which is suitable as a name for him remains. As was said. And likewise the specification of the fast by adding the fast to Ramadan, such that the obligated person says: I intend to fast Ramadan. 'And it does not fall away, etc.' is the answer to a question, which is: when the time was specified for the fast of Ramadan, then the original intention should fall away and it should be performed without intention from the healthy resident. 'It is refraining, etc.' It is better to say: it is refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse literally or legally intentionally from the dawn to sunset, so that the eating, drinking, and intercourse of the forgetful, and eating of sesame and what is in the teeth less than a chickpea and their likes are not included by converse, and masturbation by hand and by thigh and their likes, and refraining from sunrise not before it, by way of exclusion, because customarily it is from its rising to its setting. And what is taken in definitions are the customary meanings that come to mind, except that it is said: what is considered in legal crafts are the legal meanings, and the legal daytime is from the break of dawn, except that its being daytime is not general, for the time of dawn is only counted as daytime in regard to fasting specifically, not prayer, so that his prayer is not silent but rather audible, and it has been reported that the daytime prayer is silent. As in al-Fusul. The first research in the Book of Allah. Section on the commanded act. And if Sharia has not specified a time for it, then the time is not specified by the slave's specification, such that if the slave specifies days for making up Ramadan, they are not specified for the make-up, and the fast of expiation and supererogatory is permissible in them, and it is permissible to make up those days in Ramadan and other than it. And one of the rulings of this type is that specification of intention is required due to the existence of a competing obligation. Then the slave can obligate something upon himself limited or unlimited, and he does not have the power to change the ruling of Sharia. Example: if he vows to fast a specific day, that is binding on him, and if he fasts it for making up Ramadan or for expiation of an oath, it is permissible, because Sharia has made the make-up absolute. With intention: because it is worship, and no worship without intention, to distinguish it from custom, and because worship must have sincerity. Allah says: 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion' (the verse), and sincerity is only through intention. As in al-Ma'din. 'And if Sharia has not specified, etc.': This is an explanation of the second category of the two types of standard, i.e., what Sharia has not specified a time for, like make-up, for it has no specified time, due to the absoluteness of the days in His saying: 'then a number of other days,' so the time is not specified by the slave's specification, because it is a change of the ruling of Sharia from absoluteness to restriction, and that is not for the slave. And specification of intention is required in it, meaning specification of intention is required in this type of time, so he says: I intend for make-up or for the vowed fast, and it is not fulfilled by absolute intention, nor by intention of supererogatory or another obligatory. So understand. 'It is not specified, etc.' because it is a change of the ruling of Sharia from absoluteness to restriction, and that is not for the slave. 'Specification of intention': by intending make-up of Ramadan, for example, and mere intention of absolute obligatory fast or absolute make-up is not sufficient for him. 'Due to the existence of a competing obligation': by the time not being specified by Sharia, and the legality of every fast, obligatory and supererogatory, in every day except the prohibited days and menstruation and postnatal bleeding. 'Then the slave, etc.' This is an objection and its gist: that the slave can obligate something upon himself that was not obligatory, so why can he not specify some obligations with a time, while specification is less than obligation, because establishing a description is lower than establishing the essence? So the author replied that specifying some times is a change of the ruling of Sharia, and the slave does not have that, even though he has the power to obligate something upon himself. And the closest is to make his saying 'then for the slave' as a branch upon the first, and its estimation: if you realize that the time is not specified by the slave's specification, then know after that that the slave can obligate something upon himself, and when it pertains to what he has obligated, the ruling of Sharia applies, he cannot change it. As in al-Fusul.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi examines the relationship between time specification and intention in commanded acts of worship, focusing on fasting. The author categorizes acts into two types: those with a time specified by the Lawgiver (like Ramadan) and those without (like make-up or vows). For the first type, specification of intention is not required because the time itself removes any competition from other obligations; the mere intention to fast suffices, as the fast is already identified by its time. The author uses an analogy: a hired tailor cannot turn his work into charity because the time is fixed. A dispute with al-Shafi'i is presented: Shafi'i requires specification because the command to fast is general and the slave must specify to avoid being compelled. The Hanafi response: since the slave is already free in choosing to fast in Ramadan, and the time is fixed by the Lawgiver, specification is redundant. For the second type (e.g., qada), because Sharia left the time open (as per Quran 2:184), the slave cannot fix it by his own choice; doing so would change the ruling from unrestricted to restricted, which is not in his authority. Here, specification of intention is necessary because multiple obligations (e.g., qada, kaffarah, nadhr) compete on the same day. The passage also defines fasting as intentional refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse from dawn to sunset, with refinements for forgetfulness, minor residues, and the difference between legal and customary daytime. Finally, the author addresses an objection: if the slave can create new obligations (vows), why can't he specify times? The answer: specification of time alters the divine ruling, while creating a new obligation does not—once the slave obligates himself, he must follow the existing rules, not invent new ones.

Key Terms
نية (niyya): Intention; the resolve to perform an act of worship, distinguishing it from custom and ensuring sincerity.
إمساك (imsak): Refraining; the physical abstention from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in Usul al-Shashi, what transforms mere refraining (imsak) into valid fasting (sawm)?
A) The time of day
B) The intention (niyyah)
C) The abstention from food only
D) The soundness of the body

Key Takeaway
Intention (niyyah) is a condition for fasting; without it, the act lacks legal validity as worship.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Time-Specified vs Unspecified Acts: When Specification of Intention is Required
Classifying commanded acts by time specification and the resultant requirement for intention specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between acts with time specified by Sharia and those without, and apply the rule that specification of intention is required only when multiple obligations compete on the same time slot.

Core Idea
When Sharia fixes the time, intention needs no specification; when time is open, specification is required due to competition.

The passage divides commanded acts (ma'mur bihi) into two types: those with a specified time by the Lawgiver (like Ramadan) and those left unspecified (like qada). For the first, the time itself removes any conflict, so the absolute intention suffices. For the second, because multiple obligations can occupy the same day, the worshipper must specify which obligation he intends. This section also addresses the objection that a slave can create obligations (vows) but cannot specify times, explaining the difference between creating a new ruling and altering an existing one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of commanded acts based on time
From the text: 'إن لم يعين الشرع له وقتا' and implicitly the first category where time is specified. Recognize that the key is whether Sharia has fixed a time for the act (e.g., Ramadan for the obligatory fast) or left it open (e.g., qada, nadhr, kaffarah).
The first category is discussed in the earlier part; the second is explicitly introduced here.
2
State the ruling on intention for each category
First category: specification of intention (ta'yin) is not required; absolute intention (e.g., 'I intend to fast') suffices. Second category: specification is required because of the existence of a competing obligation (muzahim).
The competing obligation arises because multiple valid fasts (qada, nadhr, kaffarah, nafil) can be performed on the same day.
3
Explain the reason for the difference
For the first category, the time is specified by Sharia, so the fast is identified by its time; there is no competition from other obligations because only that specific act is valid in that time. For the second, Sharia left the time open, so any day can host multiple obligations; specification is needed to distinguish which one is intended.
The text uses the term 'muzahim' for competing obligations.
4
Analyze the objection and response about the slave's authority
An objection is raised: if a slave can obligate himself to a new act (nadhr), why can he not specify a time for an existing obligation? The answer: creating a new obligation does not change Sharia's ruling, but specifying a time for an existing obligation (where Sharia left it open) would change the ruling from absolute to restricted, which is not in the slave's authority.
This shows the limit of human authority in legislation: we can add obligations but cannot modify divine rulings.

رمضان لا عما نوى، وإذا اندفع المزاحم في الوقت سقط اشتراط التعيين فإن ذلك لقطع المزاحمة، ولا يسقط أصل النية؛ لأن الإمساك لا يصير صوماً إلا بالنية، فإن الصوم شرعاً هو الإمساك عن الأكل والشرب والجماع نهارا مع النية. لا عما نوى: لأن الشرع لما عين للمعيار صوماً بصفة، فإذا أراد المكلف تغيير صفة لم يقدر عليه، وهذا كمن آجر نفسه في وقت معين للخياطة فخاط له ثم قصد التبرع في ذلك الوقت لم يكن تبرعا بل يكون إجازة، وإنما قيد بالصحيح المقيم احترازاً عن المسافر والمريض على قول أبي حنيفة محله؛ فإنه عنده إذا نوى المريض أو المسافر في رمضان عن واجب آخر يقع عما نوى؛ لأنه لما ثبت لهما الترخص لمصالح البدن وهو فصل في المأمور به

وإن لم يعين الشرع له وقتا، فإنه لا يتعين الوقت له بتعيين العبد، حتى لو عين العبد أياما لقضاء رمضان لا تتعين هي للقضاء، ويجوز فيها صوم الكفارة والنفل، ويجوز قضاء تلك الأيام في رمضان فيها وغيرها.
ومن حكم هذا النوع: أنه يشترط تعيين النية لوجود المزاحم، ثم للعبد أن يوجب شيئا على نفسه مؤقتا أو غير موقت وليس له تغيير حكم الشرع. مثاله: إذا نذر أن يصوم يوما بعينه لزمه ذلك، ولو صامه عن قضاء رمضان أو عن كفارة يمينه جاز؛ لأن الشرع جعل القضاء مطلقا، مع النية: لأنه عبادة، ولا عبادة بدون النية؛ ليمتاز عن العادة؛ ولأن العبادة لابد فيها من الإخلاص، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أُمِرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مُخْلِصِينَ لَهُ الدِّينَ﴾ الآية، والإخلاص لا يكون إلا بالنية كذا في "المعدن".
وإن لم يعين الشرع إلخ : هذا بيان القسم الثاني من نوعي المعيار أي ما لم يعين الشرع له وقتا كقضاء فإنه ليس له وقت معين؛ لإطلاق الأيام في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ﴾، فإنه لا يتعين الوقت له بتعيين العبد؛ لأنه تغيير حكم الشرع من الإطلاق إلى التقييد ليس ذلك للعبد، وتشترط فيه نية التعيين أي يشترط في هذا القسم من الوقت نية التعيين بأن يقول: نويت للقضاء أو المنذور، ولا يتأدى بمطلق النية، ولا بنية النفل أو واجب آخر فافهم.
لا يتعين إلخ لأنه تغير حكم الشرع من الإطلاق إلى التقييد وليس ذلك للعبد. تعيين النية: بأن ينوي قضاء رمضان مثلا، ولا يكفيه نية مطلق صوم الفرض أو مطلق القضاء. لوجود المزاحم: بعدم تعيين الوقت له شرعا، وشرعية كل صوم من الواجب والنفل في كل يوم من الأيام غير الأيام الممنوعة والحيض والنفاس. ثم للعبد إلخ هذا اعتراض ومحصوله : أن للعبد أن يوجب على نفسه شيئا لم يكن واجبا، فكيف لا يكون له أن يعين على نفسه بعض الواجبات بوقت مع أن التعيين دون الإيجاب؛ لأن إثبات الوصف أدنى من إثبات الأصل، فأجاب المصنف بأن تعيين بعض الأوقات تغيير حكم الشرع وليس للعبد ذلك وإن كان له إيجاب شيء على نفسه، والأقرب أن يجعل قوله ثم للعبد كالتفريع على الأول، وتقديره: إذا تحققت أنه لا يتعين الوقت بتعيين العبد فاعلم بعد ذلك أن للعبد أن يوجب شيئا على نفسه، وإذا تعلق بما أوجب عليه حكم الشرع ليس له تغييره كذا في "الفصول".
The first research in the Book of Allah. Section on the commanded act. Ramadan, not what he intended. And when the competing obligation is removed in the time, the requirement of specification falls away, because that is to remove competition. And the original intention does not fall away, because refraining does not become fasting except with intention. For fasting in Sharia is refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse during the day with intention. 'Not what he intended': because when Sharia specified for the standard a fast with a description, if the obligated person wants to change the description, he cannot, and this is like one who hires himself at a specific time for sewing, and sews for him, then intends charity in that time, it is not charity but rather a hire. And it is only restricted to the healthy resident to exclude the traveler and the sick according to Abu Hanifa's opinion in its place; for according to him, if the sick or traveler intends in Ramadan for another obligation, it occurs for what he intended, because since they have been granted concession for bodily interests, which is breaking the fast, then to establish it for religious interests—which is fulfilling what he owes of religious duties—is more appropriate. As in al-Fusul. 'And when the competing obligation is removed, etc.': And it is other than this fast in that it is not permissible in the time and is interpreted as non-permissibility, lest one imagine that what is meant by his saying 'and when the competing obligation is removed' is competition in priority. 'It falls away, etc.' And according to al-Shafi'i, specification is required, because it exists from the Lawgiver, so it is necessary that the specification come from the slave so that he is voluntary in that, not compelled. We say: the slave is unrestricted in such specification, because in the original fast he is voluntary, so he is addressed in this day regarding the fast, not regarding specification, because it has been obtained from the Lawgiver, so there is no need for specification by the slave. So memorize it. 'Requirement of specification': meaning, when the requirement of specification was to remove the competing obligation in the time, when the competing obligation was removed, the requirement of specification falls away. Because when it was specified in Ramadan, it is attained by the absolute name, and by error in the description, like the specified in a place is attained by the genus and species name just as it is removed by the proper name. For if Zaid intended to attain a human or O man, and he is alone in the house, it is as if he said: O Zaid, and is attained by error in the description, as if he intended the white man while he is alone in the house, and said O black man, he is attained by this, because the black is invalid, so the genus name which is suitable as a name for him remains. As was said. And likewise the specification of the fast by adding the fast to Ramadan, such that the obligated person says: I intend to fast Ramadan. 'And it does not fall away, etc.' is the answer to a question, which is: when the time was specified for the fast of Ramadan, then the original intention should fall away and it should be performed without intention from the healthy resident. 'It is refraining, etc.' It is better to say: it is refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse literally or legally intentionally from the dawn to sunset, so that the eating, drinking, and intercourse of the forgetful, and eating of sesame and what is in the teeth less than a chickpea and their likes are not included by converse, and masturbation by hand and by thigh and their likes, and refraining from sunrise not before it, by way of exclusion, because customarily it is from its rising to its setting. And what is taken in definitions are the customary meanings that come to mind, except that it is said: what is considered in legal crafts are the legal meanings, and the legal daytime is from the break of dawn, except that its being daytime is not general, for the time of dawn is only counted as daytime in regard to fasting specifically, not prayer, so that his prayer is not silent but rather audible, and it has been reported that the daytime prayer is silent. As in al-Fusul. The first research in the Book of Allah. Section on the commanded act. And if Sharia has not specified a time for it, then the time is not specified by the slave's specification, such that if the slave specifies days for making up Ramadan, they are not specified for the make-up, and the fast of expiation and supererogatory is permissible in them, and it is permissible to make up those days in Ramadan and other than it. And one of the rulings of this type is that specification of intention is required due to the existence of a competing obligation. Then the slave can obligate something upon himself limited or unlimited, and he does not have the power to change the ruling of Sharia. Example: if he vows to fast a specific day, that is binding on him, and if he fasts it for making up Ramadan or for expiation of an oath, it is permissible, because Sharia has made the make-up absolute. With intention: because it is worship, and no worship without intention, to distinguish it from custom, and because worship must have sincerity. Allah says: 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion' (the verse), and sincerity is only through intention. As in al-Ma'din. 'And if Sharia has not specified, etc.': This is an explanation of the second category of the two types of standard, i.e., what Sharia has not specified a time for, like make-up, for it has no specified time, due to the absoluteness of the days in His saying: 'then a number of other days,' so the time is not specified by the slave's specification, because it is a change of the ruling of Sharia from absoluteness to restriction, and that is not for the slave. And specification of intention is required in it, meaning specification of intention is required in this type of time, so he says: I intend for make-up or for the vowed fast, and it is not fulfilled by absolute intention, nor by intention of supererogatory or another obligatory. So understand. 'It is not specified, etc.' because it is a change of the ruling of Sharia from absoluteness to restriction, and that is not for the slave. 'Specification of intention': by intending make-up of Ramadan, for example, and mere intention of absolute obligatory fast or absolute make-up is not sufficient for him. 'Due to the existence of a competing obligation': by the time not being specified by Sharia, and the legality of every fast, obligatory and supererogatory, in every day except the prohibited days and menstruation and postnatal bleeding. 'Then the slave, etc.' This is an objection and its gist: that the slave can obligate something upon himself that was not obligatory, so why can he not specify some obligations with a time, while specification is less than obligation, because establishing a description is lower than establishing the essence? So the author replied that specifying some times is a change of the ruling of Sharia, and the slave does not have that, even though he has the power to obligate something upon himself. And the closest is to make his saying 'then for the slave' as a branch upon the first, and its estimation: if you realize that the time is not specified by the slave's specification, then know after that that the slave can obligate something upon himself, and when it pertains to what he has obligated, the ruling of Sharia applies, he cannot change it. As in al-Fusul.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi examines the relationship between time specification and intention in commanded acts of worship, focusing on fasting. The author categorizes acts into two types: those with a time specified by the Lawgiver (like Ramadan) and those without (like make-up or vows). For the first type, specification of intention is not required because the time itself removes any competition from other obligations; the mere intention to fast suffices, as the fast is already identified by its time. The author uses an analogy: a hired tailor cannot turn his work into charity because the time is fixed. A dispute with al-Shafi'i is presented: Shafi'i requires specification because the command to fast is general and the slave must specify to avoid being compelled. The Hanafi response: since the slave is already free in choosing to fast in Ramadan, and the time is fixed by the Lawgiver, specification is redundant. For the second type (e.g., qada), because Sharia left the time open (as per Quran 2:184), the slave cannot fix it by his own choice; doing so would change the ruling from unrestricted to restricted, which is not in his authority. Here, specification of intention is necessary because multiple obligations (e.g., qada, kaffarah, nadhr) compete on the same day. The passage also defines fasting as intentional refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse from dawn to sunset, with refinements for forgetfulness, minor residues, and the difference between legal and customary daytime. Finally, the author addresses an objection: if the slave can create new obligations (vows), why can't he specify times? The answer: specification of time alters the divine ruling, while creating a new obligation does not—once the slave obligates himself, he must follow the existing rules, not invent new ones.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the type or time of an act of worship in the intention (e.g., specifying Ramadan vs. qada).
مزاحم (muzahim): A competing obligation that could conflict with the intended worship (e.g., another obligatory fast on the same day).
مطلق (mutlaq): Absolute; no restriction or qualification. In usul, a mutlaq text applies to all its instances without specification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is specification of intention required for the second category of commanded acts (e.g., qada)?
A) Because the Lawgiver commanded it explicitly.
B) Because there is a competing obligation (muzahim) that requires distinction.
C) Because the slave cannot change the ruling.
D) Because the time is fixed by Sharia.

Key Takeaway
For acts with unspecified time by Sharia, specification of intention is required because multiple obligations compete for the same time slot.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Specification of Intention for Ramadan
Presenting and rebutting the Shafi'i objection on specification for Ramadan fasting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the requirement of specification (ta'yin) for the fast of Ramadan, explain each proof, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Hanafi: time itself specifies; Shafi'i: the slave must specify to exercise choice.

In the beginning of the passage, the author presents a dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i regarding whether a person must specify in his intention that he is fasting Ramadan, or whether a general intention to fast suffices. The Hanafi position is that specification is not required because the time is fixed by Sharia and removes any competition. Al-Shafi'i argues that the command to fast is general, so the slave must specify to avoid being compelled. The Hanafi response emphasizes that the slave is already free in the original fast; the Lawgiver's specification is enough. This lesson dissects that dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on specification for Ramadan
The Hanafi school holds that specification (ta'yin) is not required for the fast of Ramadan. The mere intention to fast, without specifying that it is for Ramadan, suffices.
This is based on the principle that the time itself identifies the obligation.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its rationale
Imam al-Shafi'i requires specification in intention for Ramadan. His reasoning: the command to fast is general (the Quranic command is absolute), so the slave must specify which fast he intends to exercise his choice and not be compelled.
The Shafi'i school views intention as a pillar (rukn) that must explicitly identify the act.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i argument
The Hanafi response: the slave is already free in choosing to fast in Ramadan; the Lawgiver's specification of the time suffices. The address is to fast, not to specify. The slave is addressed for the fast, not for specification.
The analogy of the hired tailor is used: if hired for a specific time, the act is bound by that time, not by the worker's intention.
4
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
In the Hanafi school, if a person intends a general fast in Ramadan (e.g., 'I intend to fast'), it counts as the Ramadan fast. In the Shafi'i school, it would not count unless he specifies 'Ramadan' in his intention.
This difference affects validity in cases where the intention is ambiguous.

رمضان لا عما نوى، وإذا اندفع المزاحم في الوقت سقط اشتراط التعيين فإن ذلك لقطع المزاحمة، ولا يسقط أصل النية؛ لأن الإمساك لا يصير صوماً إلا بالنية، فإن الصوم شرعاً هو الإمساك عن الأكل والشرب والجماع نهارا مع النية. لا عما نوى: لأن الشرع لما عين للمعيار صوماً بصفة، فإذا أراد المكلف تغيير صفة لم يقدر عليه، وهذا كمن آجر نفسه في وقت معين للخياطة فخاط له ثم قصد التبرع في ذلك الوقت لم يكن تبرعا بل يكون إجازة، وإنما قيد بالصحيح المقيم احترازاً عن المسافر والمريض على قول أبي حنيفة محله؛ فإنه عنده إذا نوى المريض أو المسافر في رمضان عن واجب آخر يقع عما نوى؛ لأنه لما ثبت لهما الترخص لمصالح البدن وهو الفطر، فلأن يثبت لمصالح الدين وهي قضاء ما عليه من الدين أولى كذا في "الفصول". وإذا اندفع إلخ : وهو غير هذا الصوم بأن لا يجوز في الوقت وفسر بعدم الجواز؛ لئلا يتوهم أن المراد بقوله: وإذا اندفع المزاحم المزاحم في الأولوية. سقط إلخ وعند الشافعي له: يشترط التعيين؛ لأنه وجد من الشارع فلابد أن من يتعين من جهة العبد ليكون مختارا في ذلك لا مجبورا، قلنا: إطلاق العبد في مثل هذا التعيين؛ لأنه في أصل الصوم مختار، فهو مخاطب في هذا اليوم بالصوم لا بالتعيين؛ لأنه قد حصل من الشارع، فلا حاجة إلى تعيين العبد فاحفظه. اشتراط التعيين: أي لما كان اشتراط التعيين لقطع المزاحم في الوقت، فلما اندفع المزاحم سقط اشتراط التعيين؛ لأنه لما تعين في رمضان أصيب لمطلق الاسم، وبالخطاء في الوصف كالمتعين في مكان ينال باسم الجنس والنوع كما يزال باسم العلم، فإن زيدا لو نوى ينال إنسان أو يا رجل وهو منفرد في الدار كان كما قيل: يا زيد وينال بالخطاء في الوصف كما لو نوى الرجل الأبيض وهو منفرد في الدار بيد أيها الرجل الأسود وينال بهذا؛ لأن الأسود بطل فبقي اسم الجنس الذي يصلح اسما له كذا قيل. وهكذا تعيين الصوم بأن يضاف الصوم إلى رمضان بأن يقول المكلف: نويت صوم رمضان ولا يسقط إلخ جواب سوال، وهو: أنه لما تعين الوقت لصوم رمضان فينبغي أن يسقط أصل النية ويتأدى بلا نية من الصحيح المقيم. هو الإمساك إلخ الأحسن أن يقال: هو الإمساك عن الأكل والشرب والجماع حقيقة أو حكما عمدا من طلوع الفجر إلى غروب الشمس؛ لئلا يرد أكل الناسي وشربه وجماعه وأكل السمسم وما في الأسنان أقل من الحمص وأمثلهما عكسا، والاستمناء باليد والتفخيذ وأمثالهما، والإمساك من طلوع الشمس لا قبله طردا؛ لأنه عرفا من طلوعها إلى غروبها، والمأخوذ في الحدود المعاني العرفية المتبادر إلا أن يقال: المعتبر في الصناعات الشرعية المعاني الشرعية، والنهار الشرعي من طلوع الفجر إلا أن نهاريته ليس بعام؛ فإن وقت الفجر إنما يعد من النهار في حق الصوم خاصة دون الصلاة حتى لم يكن صلاته عجماء بل جهرية وقد ورد صلاة النهار عجماء كذا في "الفصول".

وإن لم يعين الشرع له وقتا، فإنه لا يتعين الوقت له بتعيين العبد، حتى لو عين العبد أياما لقضاء رمضان لا تتعين هي للقضاء، ويجوز فيها صوم الكفارة والنفل، ويجوز قضاء تلك الأيام في رمضان فيها وغيرها.
ومن حكم هذا النوع: أنه يشترط تعيين النية لوجود المزاحم، ثم للعبد أن يوجب شيئا على نفسه مؤقتا أو غير موقت وليس له تغيير حكم الشرع. مثاله: إذا نذر أن يصوم يوما بعينه لزمه ذلك، ولو صامه عن قضاء رمضان أو عن كفارة يمينه جاز؛ لأن الشرع جعل القضاء مطلقا، مع النية: لأنه عبادة، ولا عبادة بدون النية؛ ليمتاز عن العادة؛ ولأن العبادة لابد فيها من الإخلاص، قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أُمِرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُوا اللَّهَ مُخْلِصِينَ لَهُ الدِّينَ﴾ الآية، والإخلاص لا يكون إلا بالنية كذا في "المعدن".
وإن لم يعين الشرع إلخ : هذا بيان القسم الثاني من نوعي المعيار أي ما لم يعين الشرع له وقتا كقضاء فإنه ليس له وقت معين؛ لإطلاق الأيام في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ﴾، فإنه لا يتعين الوقت له بتعيين العبد؛ لأنه تغيير حكم الشرع من الإطلاق إلى التقييد ليس ذلك للعبد، وتشترط فيه نية التعيين أي يشترط في هذا القسم من الوقت نية التعيين بأن يقول: نويت للقضاء أو المنذور، ولا يتأدى بمطلق النية، ولا بنية النفل أو واجب آخر فافهم.
لا يتعين إلخ لأنه تغير حكم الشرع من الإطلاق إلى التقييد وليس ذلك للعبد. تعيين النية: بأن ينوي قضاء رمضان مثلا، ولا يكفيه نية مطلق صوم الفرض أو مطلق القضاء. لوجود المزاحم: بعدم تعيين الوقت له شرعا، وشرعية كل صوم من الواجب والنفل في كل يوم من الأيام غير الأيام الممنوعة والحيض والنفاس. ثم للعبد إلخ هذا اعتراض ومحصوله : أن للعبد أن يوجب على نفسه شيئا لم يكن واجبا، فكيف لا يكون له أن يعين على نفسه بعض الواجبات بوقت مع أن التعيين دون الإيجاب؛ لأن إثبات الوصف أدنى من إثبات الأصل، فأجاب المصنف بأن تعيين بعض الأوقات تغيير حكم الشرع وليس للعبد ذلك وإن كان له إيجاب شيء على نفسه، والأقرب أن يجعل قوله ثم للعبد كالتفريع على الأول، وتقديره: إذا تحققت أنه لا يتعين الوقت بتعيين العبد فاعلم بعد ذلك أن للعبد أن يوجب شيئا على نفسه، وإذا تعلق بما أوجب عليه حكم الشرع ليس له تغييره كذا في "الفصول".

And when the competing obligation is removed in the time, the requirement of specification falls away, because that is to remove competition. For fasting in Sharia is refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse during the day with intention. 'Not what he intended': because when Sharia specified for the standard a fast with a description, if the obligated person wants to change the description, he cannot, and this is like one who hires himself at a specific time for sewing, and sews for him, then intends charity in that time, it is not charity but rather a hire. So memorize it. 'Requirement of specification': meaning, when the requirement of specification was to remove the competing obligation in the time, when the competing obligation was removed, the requirement of specification falls away. Because when it was specified in Ramadan, it is attained by the absolute name, and by error in the description, like the specified in a place is attained by the genus and species name just as it is removed by the proper name. For if Zaid intended to attain a human or O man, and he is alone in the house, it is as if he said: O Zaid, and is attained by error in the description, as if he intended the white man while he is alone in the house, and said O black man, he is attained by this, because the black is invalid, so the genus name which is suitable as a name for him remains. As was said. And likewise the specification of the fast by adding the fast to Ramadan, such that the obligated person says: I intend to fast Ramadan. 'And it does not fall away, etc.' is the answer to a question, which is: when the time was specified for the fast of Ramadan, then the original intention should fall away and it should be performed without intention from the healthy resident. 'It is refraining, etc.' It is better to say: it is refraining from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse literally or legally intentionally from the dawn to sunset, so that the eating, drinking, and intercourse of the forgetful, and eating of sesame and what is in the teeth less than a chickpea and their likes are not included by converse, and masturbation by hand and by thigh and their likes, and refraining from sunrise not before it, by way of exclusion, because customarily it is from its rising to its setting. And what is taken in definitions are the customary meanings that come to mind, except that it is said: what is considered in legal crafts are the legal meanings, and the legal daytime is from the break of dawn, except that its being daytime is not general, for the time of dawn is only counted as daytime in regard to fasting specifically, not prayer, so that his prayer is not silent but rather audible, and it has been reported that the daytime prayer is silent. As in al-Fusul. The first research in the Book of Allah. Section on the commanded act. And if Sharia has not specified a time for it, then the time is not specified by the slave's specification, such that if the slave specifies days for making up Ramadan, they are not specified for the make-up, and the fast of expiation and supererogatory is permissible in them, and it is permissible to make up those days in Ramadan and other than it. And one of the rulings of this type is that specification of intention is required due to the existence of a competing obligation. Then the slave can obligate something upon himself limited or unlimited, and he does not have the power to change the ruling of Sharia. Example: if he vows to fast a specific day, that is binding on him, and if he fasts it for making up Ramadan or for expiation of an oath, it is permissible, because Sharia has made the make-up absolute. With intention: because it is worship, and no worship without intention, to distinguish it from custom, and because worship must have sincerity. Allah says: 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion' (the verse), and sincerity is only through intention. As in al-Ma'din. 'And if Sharia has not specified, etc.': This is an explanation of the second category of the two types of standard, i.e., what Sharia has not specified a time for, like make-up, for it has no specified time, due to the absoluteness of the days in His saying: 'then a number of other days,' so the time is not specified by the slave's specification, because it is a change of the ruling of Sharia from absoluteness to restriction, and that is not for the slave. And specification of intention is required in it, meaning specification of intention is required in this type of time, so he says: I intend for make-up or for the vowed fast, and it is not fulfilled by absolute intention, nor by intention of supererogatory or another obligatory. So understand. 'It is not specified, etc.' because it is a change of the ruling of Sharia from absoluteness to restriction, and that is not for the slave. 'Specification of intention': by intending make-up of Ramadan, for example, and mere intention of absolute obligatory fast or absolute make-up is not sufficient for him. 'Due to the existence of a competing obligation': by the time not being specified by Sharia, and the legality of every fast, obligatory and supererogatory, in every day except the prohibited days and menstruation and postnatal bleeding. 'Then the slave, etc.' This is an objection and its gist: that the slave can obligate something upon himself that was not obligatory, so why can he not specify some obligations with a time, while specification is less than obligation, because establishing a description is lower than establishing the essence? So the author replied that specifying some times is a change of the ruling of Sharia, and the slave does not have that, even though he has the power to obligate something upon himself. And the closest is to make his saying 'then for the slave' as a branch upon the first, and its estimation: if you realize that the time is not specified by the slave's specification, then know after that that the slave can obligate something upon himself, and when it pertains to what he has obligated, the ruling of Sharia applies, he cannot change it. As in al-Fusul.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi examines the relationship between time specification and intention in commanded acts of worship, focusing on fasting. The author categorizes acts into two types: those with a time specified by the Lawgiver (like Ramadan) and those without (like make-up or vows). For the first type, specification of intention is not required because the time itself removes any competition from other obligations; the mere intention to fast suffices, as the fast is already identified by its time. The author uses an analogy: a hired tailor cannot turn his work into charity because the time is fixed. A dispute with al-Shafi'i is presented: Shafi'i requires specification because the command to fast is general and the slave must specify to avoid being compelled. The Hanafi response: since the slave is already free in choosing to fast in Ramadan, and the time is fixed by the Lawgiver, specification is redundant. For the second type (e.g., qada), because Sharia left the time open (as per Quran 2:184), the slave cannot fix it by his own choice; doing so would change the ruling from unrestricted to restricted, which is not in his authority. Here, specification of intention is necessary because multiple obligations (e.g., qada, kaffarah, nadhr) compete on the same day. The passage also defines fasting as intentional refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse from dawn to sunset, with refinements for forgetfulness, minor residues, and the difference between legal and customary daytime. Finally, the author addresses an objection: if the slave can create new obligations (vows), why can't he specify times? The answer: specification of time alters the divine ruling, while creating a new obligation does not—once the slave obligates himself, he must follow the existing rules, not invent new ones.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of the type or time of an act of worship in the intention (e.g., specifying Ramadan vs. qada).
مختار (mukhtar): Voluntary; exercising free choice. In the dispute, al-Shafi'i argues that specification ensures the slave is mukhtar, not compelled.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in the text, why is specification of intention not required for the Ramadan fast?
A) Because the Prophet did not specify his intention.
B) Because the time is fixed by Sharia and removes competition.
C) Because intention is not required for obligatory acts.
D) Because the Shafi'i argument is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require specification of intention for the Ramadan fast because the fixed time removes any competing obligation.
