The Definition and Ruling of Acts Good in Themselves (Hasan bi Nafsihi)
Classification and ruling of acts good in themselves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of hasan bi nafsihi, identify its two subtypes, and explain why its goodness is a legal ruling (shar'i) rather than a rational one (aqli).

Core Idea
An act good in itself is legally good because of the command, not because reason deems it good.

In this passage, Al-Shashi introduces the first major category of commanded acts: those that are good in themselves (hasan bi nafsihi). Understanding this category is essential for grasping how obligations are established and how they can be dropped. The author also engages with the Mutazila, defending the Hanafi view that legal goodness is determined by revelation, not reason.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of commanded acts
Identify the two broad categories mentioned at the beginning: good in itself and good for another. Focus on the first type for this lesson.
The second type (good for another) will be covered separately.
2
List examples of hasan bi nafsihi
Note the examples given: iman, gratitude, truthfulness, justice, prayer. These are inherently good acts of worship or moral virtues.
3
Analyze the ruling: obligations that can and cannot be dropped
The text states that some obligations (like faith) cannot be dropped under any circumstance, while others (like prayer or zakat) can be dropped by performance or by a legal impediment. Identify the key conditions for each.
Dropping by impediment is a specific concession from the Lawgiver.
4
Understand why goodness is legal, not rational
The passage argues that if goodness were rational, it could not be abrogated or dropped. Since we observe abrogation and dropping, goodness must be a legal ruling. This is the Hanafi rebuttal of the Mutazila position.
This is a foundational usul principle: husn and qubh are shar'i, not aqli.
5
Distinguish between tasdiq and iqrar
The text clarifies that faith (tasdiq) is essential and cannot be dropped, while declaration (iqrar) can be dropped under coercion. This illustrates the principle within a specific case.
This distinction is important for understanding the limits of obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في حسن المأمور به
ثم المأمور به في حق الحسن نوعان: ۱- حسن بنفسه ٢- وحسن لغيره. فالحَسَنُ بنفسه: مثل الإيمان بالله تعالى، وشكر المنعم، والصدق، والعدل، والصلاة ونحوها من العبادات الخالصة.
فحكم هذا النوع : أنه إذا وجب على العبد أداؤه لا يسقط إلا بالأداء، وهذا فيما لا يحتمل السقوط مثل الإيمان بالله تعالى وصفاته.
وأما ما يحتمل السقوط فهو يسقط بالأداء أو بإسقاط الآمر. كالزكاة عند هلاك النصاب
وعلى هذا قلنا: إذا وجبَت الصَّلاةُ في أول الوقت سقط الواجب بالأداء، أو باعتراض الجنون والحيض والنفاس في آخر الوقت باعتبار أن الشرع أسقطها عنه عند هذه العوارض، ولا يسقط بضيق الوقت وعدم الماء، واللباس ونحوه.
حتى يجب القضاء إذا فات الصلاة
الشيء مما يثاب بفعله ويعاقب بتركه؛ لأن هذا حكم شرعي لا عقلي، فلا يكون العقل موجباً، ولأنه يجوز ورود النسخ على حسن المأمور به ولو كان حسنها بعقل لما جاز ذلك؛ لأن حسن العقل لا يرد عليه الفسخ كحسن شكر المنعم والعدل والإحسان كذا في "المعدن". في حق الحسن أي في ذات الحسن، وأما في كيفية الحسن، فأربعة أنواع؛ لأن الحسن بنفسه نوعان: ۱- حسن لا يحتمل السقوط -۲ وحسن يحتمله، وكذا الحسن لغيره نوعان: ۱- ما يحصل ذلك بفعل المأمور به -٢- وما يحصل بفعل مقصود كذا في "المعدن". والصلاة: أي الصلاة حسن في نفسها؛ لأنها من أولها إلى آخرها تعظيم للرب تعالى بالأقوال والأفعال، وثناء عليه وخشوع له، وقيام بين يديه وجلسة لحضوره وإن كانت الكميات وتعداد الركعات، والأوقات والشرائط لا يستقل بمعرفتها العقل، فكان محتاجاً إلى الشريعة الغراء. مثل الإيمان: ههنا التصديق، فإنه ركن أصلي لا يحتمل السقوط بحال، بخلاف الإقرار، فإنه ركن إما زائد أو شرط إجراء الأحكام في الدنيا على حسب الاختلاف بين العلماء، فإنه يسقط بقدر الإكراه كذا في "المعدن". في أول الوقت فيه إشارة إلى أن نفس الوجوب يثبت بأول جزء من الوقت وجوباً موسعاً عند المصنف كما هو المذهب الصحيح.
ولا يسقط بضيق إلخ بتفريطه فيأثم، أو بغير تفريطه فلا يأثم وعلى كل تقدير يجب القضاء، وفي عدم اللباس
The First Inquiry: Regarding the Book of Allah. Chapter on the Goodness of the Commanded Act. Then the commanded act, in terms of goodness, is of two types: 1. Good in itself, and 2. Good for another. Good in itself: such as faith in Allah Most High, gratitude to the Benefactor, truthfulness, justice, prayer, and similar pure acts of worship. The ruling of this type: if it becomes obligatory upon the servant to perform it, it is not dropped except by performance. This applies to that which does not admit of being dropped, like faith in Allah Most High and His attributes. As for that which admits of being dropped, it is dropped by performance or by the command-giver's dropping it, like zakat when the nisab is destroyed. Based on this we said: if prayer becomes obligatory at the beginning of its time, the obligation is dropped by performance, or by the occurrence of insanity, menstruation, or postnatal bleeding at the end of the time, because the Lawgiver has dropped it due to these impediments. It is not dropped by the scarcity of time, lack of water, clothing, and the like. It (the act) is something for which one is rewarded if performed and punished if abandoned, because this is a legal ruling, not a rational one; reason does not make it obligatory. Also, abrogation can occur regarding the goodness of the commanded act; if its goodness were by reason, that would not be permissible, because the goodness of reason is not subject to annulment, like the goodness of gratitude to the Benefactor, justice, and beneficence. As stated in al-Ma'din. 'In terms of goodness' means regarding the essence of goodness. As for the modality of goodness, it is four types: because good in itself is two types: 1. Good that does not admit of being dropped, and 2. Good that admits of being dropped. Likewise, good for another is two types: 1. That which occurs by the commanded act itself, and 2. That which occurs by a purposeful act. As in al-Ma'din. 'Prayer': meaning prayer is good in itself because from beginning to end it is magnification of the Lord through words and actions, praise of Him, humility before Him, standing before Him, and sitting in His presence. Even though the quantities, number of rak'ahs, times, and conditions cannot be independently known by reason, so it needed the radiant Shariah. 'Like faith': here it means affirmation (tasdiq), which is the essential pillar that does not admit of being dropped at all, unlike declaration (iqrar), which is either an additional pillar or a condition for applying rulings in this world according to scholarly disagreement, and it is dropped under coercion. As in al-Ma'din. 'At the beginning of the time' contains an indication that the obligation itself is established at the first part of the time as a broad obligation according to the author, as the correct school. 'It is not dropped by scarcity' etc.: if due to his negligence, he sins; if without negligence, he does not sin. In either case, he must make up (qada). And regarding lack of clothing: he is given a choice between praying standing and completing ruku' and sujud, or praying sitting and performing them by gesture.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage from Al-Shashi's Usul defines the first type of commanded acts: those good in themselves (hasan bi nafsihi). It opens by stating the two broad categories. The author then gives examples such as iman, gratitude, truthfulness, justice, and prayer. The key ruling: if an act good in itself becomes obligatory, it cannot be dropped except by performance, unless it admits of being dropped by the Lawgiver's concession (e.g., zakat upon loss of nisab). The text elaborates on prayer: obligation is at the beginning of time, but certain impediments (insanity, menstruation, postnatal bleeding) can drop it. It emphasizes that the obligation is a legal (shar'i) ruling, not a rational one. The passage then subdivides hasan bi nafsihi into two: good that does not admit of being dropped (like faith) and good that does admit of being dropped (like prayer under certain impediments). It also clarifies that prayer is good in itself because its actions are inherently acts of worship, though its details rely on revelation. A brief discussion on faith distinguishes between tasdiq (which cannot be dropped) and iqrar (which can be dropped under coercion). This is a foundational usul concept for understanding how obligations are established and terminated.

Key Terms
حسن بنفسه (hasan bi nafsihi): An act whose goodness is inherent, e.g., faith, prayer, gratitude.
لا يحتمل السقوط (la yahtamil al-suqut): An obligation that cannot be dropped under any circumstance, e.g., faith (tasdiq).
يحتمل السقوط (yahtamil al-suqut): An obligation that can be dropped by performance or by a legal impediment (e.g., prayer due to menstruation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in the passage, what is the basis for the goodness (husn) of an act?
A) The act is good inherently and reason can make it obligatory.
B) The act is good because the Lawgiver commands it, and the obligation is a legal ruling.
C) The act's goodness is determined by its consequences.
D) The act is good only if it is mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
An act good in itself (hasan bi nafsihi) is legally good because of the command, and its obligation can be absolute or conditional depending on whether the Lawgiver allows it to be dropped.

Acts Good for Another: Definition and Ruling
Definition and ruling of acts good due to an external purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'hasan li ghayrihi', distinguish it from 'hasan li 'aynihi', and apply the rule that the obligation of the means is contingent on the obligation of the end.

Core Idea
A means act is obligatory only when its end is obligatory — if the end drops, the means drops.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi introduces the second category of commanded acts: those that are good because they serve an external purpose (hasan li ghayrihi). Understanding this classification is essential for determining when acts like wudu or walking to Friday prayer are obligatory. You will learn the core rule that the obligation of the means depends on the obligation of its end, and explore edge cases like hudud that seem similar but behave differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the definition in the Arabic text: 'ما يكون حسناً بواسطة الغير'. Note the examples: السعى إلى الجمعة (walking to Friday prayer) and الوضوء للصلاة (wudu for prayer). These acts are good not in themselves but because they lead to another good act.
The definition hinges on the intermediary (wasita).
2
State the ruling of contingency
Find the phrase 'يسقط بتلك الواسطة'. The obligation of the means drops when the intermediary (the end act) is not obligatory. For example, walking is not obligatory on one for whom Friday prayer is not obligatory, such as a traveler.
This is the key legal effect: the means is not independently obligatory.
3
Apply to interruption scenarios
Study the examples: if one walks to Friday prayer but is forced away, he must walk again. If one makes wudu then breaks it before prayer, he must repeat wudu. However, if already in a state of wudu when prayer becomes obligatory, no renewal is needed.
The means must be intact at the time of the end act.
4
Analyze the borderline category
Examine the discussion of 'القريب من هذا النوع' (close to this type) referring to hudud, qisas, and jihad. These are not dropped by impediments, so they are not purely 'good for another'. The text argues they are closer to 'good in themselves' but not identical.
This nuance helps avoid overgeneralization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الثاني: ما يكون حَسَناً بواسطة الغير، وذلك مثلَ السَّعى إلى الجمعة، والوضوء للصلاة، فإن السَّعي حَسَنٌ بواسطة كونه مفضيًّا إلى أداء الجمعة، والوضوء حَسَنُ بواسطة كونه مفتاحاً للصلاة.
وحكمُ هذا النوع أنه يسقُط تلك الواسطة، حتى أن السعي لا يجب على من لا جمعة عليه كالمريض والمسافر، ولا يجب الوضوء على من لا صلاة عليه كالحائض والنفساء، ولو سَعَى إلى الجمعة فحمل مكرها إلى غير الجامع قبل إقامة الجمعة يجب عليه السعي ثانياً، ولو كان معتكفا في الجامع يكون السعي ساقطا عنه.
وكذلك لو توضأ فأحدث قبل أداء الصلاة يجب عليه الوضوء ثانياً، ولو كان متوضياً عند وجوب الصلاة لا يجب عليه تجديد الوضوء، والقريب من هذا النوع الحدود، والقصاص، والجهاد، تجب عرياناً، ولا تسقط في حين من الأحيان، فعلم أن مطلق العوارض غير مسقط للوجوب بل بعضها الذي اعتبره الشارع في باب الحرج والضرورة البالغة إلى حد معتبر عند الشرع مسقط للوجوب، فافهم كذا في "المعدن". واللباس: حتى خير بين أن يصلي قائماً ويتم الركوع والسجود، وبين أن يصلي قاعداً ويؤديهما بالإيماء. والوضوء إلخ: فإن الوضوء تبريد وتنظيف الأعضاء وإضاعة الماء، وذلك ليس بحسن في ذاته أو ليس فيه معنى العبادة إنما حسن لأجل أداء الصلاة.
والقريب وفيه كلام وهو: أن قريب الشيء يلزم أن يكون غيره، فيلزم أن يكون الحدود ونحوها حسناً لعينه؛ إذ لا واسطة بين الحسن لغيره وبين الحسن لعينه، فإذا كان قريباً لما هو حسن لغيره يلزم أن يكون غيره، وغيره ليس إلا الحسن لعينه، بناء على انتفاء الواسطة وكون الحدود وأمثالها من الحسن لعينه بديهي البطلان كذا في بعض الحواشي. من يحصل بفعل المأمور، بخلاف هذا القسم أي الحدود والقصاص والجهاد؛ فإن الغير يحصل بفعل المأمور به.
The second type: that which is good by means of another, such as walking to Friday prayer and ablution for prayer. For walking is good by means of leading to the performance of Friday prayer, and ablution is good by means of being a key to prayer. The ruling of this type: it drops with the dropping of that intermediary, such that walking is not obligatory upon one for whom Friday is not obligatory, like the sick and the traveler; and ablution is not obligatory upon one for whom prayer is not obligatory, like the menstruating woman and the woman with postnatal bleeding. If one walks to Friday prayer and is carried against his will outside the mosque before the Friday prayer is established, he must walk a second time. If he was in retreat (i'tikaf) in the mosque, walking is dropped from him. Similarly, if he performs ablution and then invalidates it before performing prayer, he must perform ablution a second time. If he was already in a state of ablution when prayer became obligatory, he does not have to renew the ablution. Close to this type are [the punishments of] hudud, qisas, and jihad; they are to be performed as originally required and are not dropped at any time. Thus it is known that mere impediments do not remove obligation, but rather some impediments that the Lawgiver considered in the context of hardship and necessity reaching a recognized limit in Shariah remove the obligation. So understand. As in al-Ma'din. 'Clothing': [the person] is given a choice between praying standing and completing the bowing and prostration, or praying sitting and performing them by gesture. 'Ablution, etc.': because ablution is cooling and cleaning of limbs and wasting water, and that is not good in itself or has no meaning of worship; it is only good for the sake of performing prayer. 'Close' [to this type] and there is discussion regarding it: because 'close' to something must be other than it, so it would require that hudud and the like are good in themselves; for there is no intermediate between 'good for another' and 'good in itself'. If it is close to what is good for another, it must be other than it, and that other is nothing but good in itself, based on the absence of an intermediate. But that hudud and the like are good in themselves is obviously false. As in some glosses. [The difference is that] in the first section [walking and ablution], the end is obtained by the mandated act itself, unlike this section [hudud, qisas, jihad]; for the end is obtained by the mandated act.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage continues the classification of commanded acts, now discussing acts that are good not in themselves but for something else (hasan li ghayrihi). Examples given are walking to Friday prayer and performing ablution for prayer. The ruling: these acts become obligatory only if the end (the Friday prayer or prayer itself) is obligatory. If the end is not obligatory (e.g., one is sick or traveling for Friday, or a menstruating woman for prayer), the means is not obligatory either. Furthermore, if one performs the means and then the end is delayed or invalidated, the means must be repeated. For example, if one walks to Friday prayer but is forcibly taken out of the mosque, he must walk again; if one makes ablution but breaks it before prayer, he must repeat ablution. However, if one is already in a state of ablution when prayer becomes obligatory, renewal is not required. The passage then discusses acts 'close' to this type, like hudud, qisas, and jihad. These are said to be obligatory in themselves and never dropped, leading to a discussion about whether they are truly 'good for another' or 'good in themselves'. The text argues that they cannot be 'good for another' because they do not lose their obligation with the drop of an intermediary; they are inherently required. Yet they are also not 'good in themselves' in the sense of being inherently virtuous acts like faith. This nuance is clarified by noting that in the first section (walking, ablution), the end is obtained by the mandated act, while in the second (hudud, etc.), the end (deterrence, justice) is also obtained by the act itself, making them closer to 'good in themselves' but not identical. The passage emphasizes that only certain impediments (recognized by Shariah as hardship) can lift obligation, not general difficulties.

Key Terms
بواسطة الغير (bi wasitat al-ghayr): An act is good because it leads to another good act, e.g., wudu leads to prayer.
يسقط بتلك الواسطة (yasqut bi tilka al-wasita): The obligation of the means drops when the end is dropped.
القريب من هذا النوع (al-qarib min hadha al-naw'): Acts like hudud, qisas, jihad that are similar to 'good for another' but closer to 'good in themselves' because they are not dropped.
الحسن لغيره (al-hasan li ghayrihi): An act that is good because of an external end it serves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler (musafir) walks to Friday prayer (jumu'ah), what is the ruling regarding his walking?
A) It is obligatory, because walking is always required for Friday prayer.
B) It is not obligatory, because Friday prayer is not obligatory on a traveler.
C) It is recommended (sunnah) but not obligatory.
D) It is obligatory only if he intends to pray.

Key Takeaway
A means act (wasila) is obligatory only when its end (ghaya) is obligatory; if the end drops, the means drops, except for acts like hudud which are inherently obligatory.

Definition of Ada' (Performance) and Qada' (Make-up)
Defining two categories of commanded acts: performance and make-up.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada' and qada' in Hanafi usul, identify the hadith evidence for qada', and distinguish between the two categories.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a wajib act is either ada' (performed on time) or qada' (made up after being missed).

This passage from Usul al-Shashi lays the foundation for understanding two key categories of commanded acts: performance (ada') and make-up (qada'). The matn states simply that the obligatory by virtue of a command is of two types. The subsequent commentary clarifies that ada' is when the act is done at its proper time with the presence of its cause, while qada' is when the act is done after its time has lapsed due to having been missed. The hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) 'Let him pray it when he remembers it' serves as the primary evidence for the obligation of qada'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the matn: 'The obligatory by virtue of command is of two types: performance and make-up.' Recognize that these are the two subdivisions of wajib.
This is a foundational binary classification in Hanafi usul.
2
Define ada' (performance)
From the text: ada' is the occurrence of an act that has become obligatory by its cause, performed initially without prior lapse. Example: praying zuhr when the sun passes its zenith.
The key is 'initial occurrence' and 'proper time'.
3
Define qada' (make-up)
From the text: qada' is the occurrence of an act that has previously lapsed. Example: making up a missed prayer when remembered.
The hadith 'faliyasllaha idha dhakara' is the proof.
4
Connect to the hadith evidence
The commentary cites the hadith 'Let him pray it when he remembers it' as the basis for qada'. Understand that this hadith establishes that missed obligatory acts must be made up.
This is a key proof (dalil) for the obligation of qada'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأداء والقضاء:
الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان: أداء وقضاء.
بواسطة الزجر إلخ باعتبار ذاته، فإن الحد عقوبة وتعذيب للعباد، وليس ذلك حسن بنفسه، وإنما حسن بواسطة الزجر أي منع المرء عن الجناية كالزنا وشرب الخمر والقصاص مثل الحد، وإنما حسن بواسطة زجر القتل فافهم. بواسطة دفع شر إلخ لا باعتبار نفسه فإن الجهاد فيه تخريب البلاد وتعذيب الناس وليس ذلك حسنا بنفسه، قال عليه: الآدمي بنيان الرب ملعون من هدم بنيان الرب، وإنما حسن بواسطة كفر الكافر، فإن الكفرة أعداء الله تعالى والمسلمين، فلذلك حسن لدفع شرهم وإعلاء كلمة الحق. إلى الحراب إنما قال: "إلى الحراب" ولم يقل إلى شر الكفرة؛ بينهما على أن المراد بشر الكفرة: الحراب، وإنما قال: لو فرضنا؛ لأنه خلاف الخبر، وهو قوله عليه: "الجهاد ماض إلى يوم القيامة"، وإنما قال: والقريب من النوع مع أن الحسن في هذه الثلاث أيضاً بواسطة للفرق بين هذه الثلاث وبين السعي والوضوء، فإن حسن السعي والوضوء بواسطة الجمعة والصلاة وهما لا يتأديان بالسعي والوضوء، بل بأفعال مقصودة وأقوال معلومة، بخلاف الحدود والقصاص والجهاد فإن حسن هذه الثلاث بواسطة الزجر عن الجناية، وقتل النفس المعصومة، وإعلاء كلمة الله وهذه الوسائط تتأدى بنفس الحد والقصاص والجهاد، ولأن بنفس الحد والقصاص يحصل الزجر، وبنفس الجهاد يحصل الإعلاء، أو يقال: إنما قال: والقريب من هذا النوع؛ لأن القسم الأول أي السعي والوضوء كاملاً في كونه حسناً لغيره؛ لأن الغير لا يحصل بفعل المأمور به بخلاف هذا القسم أي الحدود والقصاص والجهاد؛ فإن الغير يحصل بفعل المأمور به على ما بين آنفاً كذا في "المعدن". لا يجب عليه الجهاد والمعنى أنه لو تصور إسلام الخلق عن آخرهم لا تبقى فرضية الجهاد ويسقط فرض القتال، وإن كان ذلك خلاف الخبر في الظاهر، فإن النبي ﷺ قال: "لن يبرح هذا الدين قائماً تقاتل عليه عصابة من المسلمين حتى تقوم الساعة"، وعن عمران بن حصين رضي الله عنه قال: قال رسول الله ﷺ: "لا تزال طائفة من أمتي يقاتلون على الحق ظاهرين على من ناوأهم حتى يقاتل آخرهم المسيح الدجال". [الشافي: ص ١٤٤]
نوعان إلخ: يعني أن الأمر قد يرد لطلب إيقاع فعل وجب في ذمته بوجود سببه ابتداء من غير سبق فواته كالأمر بإقامة الصلاة، وقد يرد لإيقاع ما سبق فواته كقوله عليه: "فليصلها إذا ذكرها"، فسمى الإيقاع الأول أداء، والثاني قضاء.
Chapter on Performance and Make-up:
The obligatory by virtue of command is of two types: performance and make-up.
[Commentary continues:] By means of deterrence etc. considering itself: for the hadd is a punishment and torment for servants, and that is not good in itself; rather it is good by means of deterrence, i.e., preventing a person from crime like adultery and wine drinking. Qisas is like the hadd, rather it is good by means of deterrence from killing, so understand. By means of repelling evil etc., not considering itself, for jihad involves destruction of lands and torment of people, and that is not good in itself. He said: 'The human is the building of the Lord; cursed is he who demolishes the building of the Lord.' Rather it is good by means of the disbelief of the disbeliever, for the disbelievers are enemies of Allah and Muslims. Therefore it is good to repel their evil and raise the word of truth. 'To war' he only said 'to war' and did not say 'to the evil of the disbelievers'; between them is that what is meant by 'evil of the disbelievers' is war. He only said 'if we suppose' because it contradicts the report, and that is his saying: 'Jihad continues until the Day of Judgment.' And he said: 'close to the type' even though the goodness in these three is also by means of [another], due to the difference between these three and walking and wudu: for the goodness of walking and wudu is by means of Friday prayer and prayer, and these two are not attained by walking and wudu themselves, but by intended actions and known words; unlike hudud, qisas, and jihad, for the goodness of these three is by means of deterrence from crime, killing a protected soul, and raising the word of Allah. These intermediaries are attained by the very hadd, qisas, and jihad; because by the very hadd and qisas, deterrence is achieved, and by jihad, elevation is achieved. Or it is said: He only said 'close to this type' because the first category, i.e., walking and wudu, is complete in being good by another; because the other is not attained by the act of the commanded, unlike this category, i.e., hudud, qisas, and jihad; for the other is attained by the act of the commanded as explained above, as in 'al-Ma'din'. Jihad is not obligatory upon him, meaning that if one imagines all people embracing Islam, the obligation of jihad would not remain and the obligation of fighting would fall, although that apparently contradicts the report: for the Prophet ﷺ said: 'This religion will remain established; a group of Muslims will fight for it until the Hour is established.' And from 'Imran ibn Husayn that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'A group of my community will continue to fight for the truth, dominant over those who oppose them, until the last of them fights the Dajjal.' [al-Shafi: p. 144]
'Two types' etc.: meaning that the command may come to demand the occurrence of an act that has become obligatory in one's responsibility by the existence of its cause initially without prior lapse, like the command to establish prayer; and it may come to demand the occurrence of what has previously lapsed, like his saying: 'Let him pray it when he remembers it.' So he called the first occurrence 'performance' and the second 'make-up'.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an usul definition of two types of wajib: ada' (performance) and qada' (make-up). The matn states simply that the obligatory by virtue of command is of two types. The subsequent commentary, which appears to be from a sharh, expands on the preceding discussion about hasan li ghayrihi, reiterating the distinction between hudud, qisas, jihad and acts like walking and wudu. It then concludes with the definition: ada' is doing an act when its cause is present without prior lapse, like praying on time; qada' is doing it after it has been missed, like making up a missed prayer when remembered. The hadith 'faliyasllaha idha dhakara' (let him pray it when he remembers it) is the basis for qada' in prayer. This classification is fundamental in Hanafi fiqh for understanding when an act is considered performed or made up.

Key Terms
أداء (ada'): Performance of a commanded act at its proper time without prior lapse.
قضاء (qada'): Performance of a commanded act after its initial time has passed due to having been missed.
الواجب بحكم الأمر (al-wajib bi hukm al-amr): The obligatory by virtue of a command, as opposed to wajib by other means.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what distinguishes ada' from qada'?
A) The presence of the cause (sabab) for the act
B) Whether the act was performed on time or after its time lapsed
C) The intention of the performer
D) Whether the act is obligatory or recommended

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, every wajib act falls into one of two categories: ada' (on-time performance) or qada' (make-up after being missed), with the hadith 'pray it when you remember' as the evidence for qada'.

Definitions of Ada and Qada in Hanafi Usul
Defines ada' and qada' and divides ada' into kamil and qasir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada' and qada' according to the Hanafi usul and distinguish between complete and deficient ada'.

Core Idea
Ada' is delivering the very obligation; qada' is delivering its like; completeness varies by rights fulfilled.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, understanding how obligations are discharged is fundamental. This passage from Usul al-Shashi introduces two key categories: ada' (performance) and qada' (make-up), and further divides ada' into complete and deficient. These definitions shape how we classify the fulfilment of commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The text states that the obligatory (wajib) by virtue of command is of two types: ada' and qada'. Note the key terms 'ayn al-wajib' and 'mithl al-wajib'.
The definition uses 'mustahaq' (due recipient) to emphasize delivery to the right party.
2
Compare ada' and qada'
Ada' delivers the exact obligation (ayn), while qada' delivers a similar obligation (mithl). This is because the original time for ada' has passed, so a precise repetition is impossible.
3
Analyze the subdivision of ada'
Ada' is divided into kamil (complete) and qasir (deficient). Complete ada' fulfills all rights; deficient ada' misses some, yet both discharge the obligation.
Examples: prayer in time with congregation vs. prayer without congregation.
4
Understand the commentary additions
The phrase 'to its due recipient' is emphasized because delivery to the wrong person is not ada'. For qada', the 'like' is necessary because the original act's time is unique.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a missed fajr prayer, describe the qada' and explain why it is a 'mithl' and not the 'ayn'.
Consider that the qada' prayer differs in time intention and possibly conditions (e.g., if missed due to travel, qasr may apply).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الأداء والقضاء: الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان: ۱- أداء -۲ وقضاء. فالأداء: عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه. والقضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه. ثم الأداء نوعان: ۱- كامل ۲ وقاصر. فالكامل: مثل أداء الصلاة في وقتها بالجماعة، أو الطواف متوضياً، وتسليم المبيع سليماً كما اقتضاه العقدُ إلى المشتري، وتسليم الغاصب العين المغصوبة كما غصبها. أداؤه وتفويضه عن مالكها وحكم هذا النوع أن يُحكم بالخروج عن العهدة به. بخروج المأمور تسليم عين الواجب إلخ تسليم عين الواجب والمثل في الأفعال والأعراض إيجادها والإتيان بها، فإن العبادة حق الله تعالى، فالعبد يؤديها ويسلمها إليه ولم يعتبر التقييد بالوقت ليعم أداء الزكاة والأمانات والمنذورات والكفارات، والمراد بالواجب ههنا : ما يعم الفرض أيضاً. إلى مستحقه إنما زاد هذا اللفظ مع أنه متروك في عبارة كثير من المشايخ؛ لأنه من تمام حقيقة المحدود؛ إذ التسليم لابد من تمامه وتمامه بوجود المسلم إليه كيف وإنما المأمور به إذا سلم دراهم دين إلى غير رب الدين لا يكون ذلك التسليم أداء كذا في بعض الحواشي. والقضاء إلخ : أي القضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب لا عينه أي تسليم ذلك الواجب الذي وجب أولاً في غير ذلك الوقت، وكان ينبغي أن يقيده بقوله: "من عنده" ليخرج أداء الظهر أي ظهر اليوم عن ظهر أمسه؛ لأنه ليس من عنده بل عنده بل كلاهما الله تعالى، وإنما لم يقيده بشهرة أمره وكونه مدلولاً عليه بالالتزام كذا في "نور الأنوار". فالكامل إلخ هو أداء المأمور به على وجه شرع عليه مع إيفاء جميع حقوقه، ولو استوفى بعض حقوقه دون بعض فهو كامل ذلك الوجه قاصر من هذا الوجه كأداء الصلاة بالجماعة إذا أديت في وقت مكروه، أو بإمامة من الفاسق، وبترك واجب، أو سنة من داخلها أو خارجها، فالكامل المطلق ما لا يترك فيه حق من حقوق الأداء وغيره عن النقصانات كلها والكامل الإضافي ما استوفى فيه بعضها دون بعض وهو يجامع القاصر. أداء الصَّلاة: المراد بها الصلاة المكتوبة؛ لأن الجماعة فيما عداها صفة قصور بمنزلة الإصبع الزائدة، فلو أريد بها مطلق الصلاة فلم يطابق المثال بالمثل كما لا يخفى بالجماعة: فإن الصلاة بالجماعة قد فضلت على صلاة المنفرد بخمس وعشرين درجة كما نطق به الحديث. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ٩٤] أو الطواف إلخ: لقوله عليه: "الطواف بالبيت صلاة"، والصلاة بدون الطهارة لا تجوز، لكنه يجزئ بدون الطهارة أيضاً؛ لإطلاق النص، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَطُوفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتيق
Section on Performance and Make-up: The obligatory by virtue of command is of two types: 1. Performance (ada') 2. Make-up (qada'). Ada' is the delivery of the very obligation to its due recipient. Qada' is the delivery of the like of the obligation to its due recipient. Then ada' is of two types: 1. Complete (kamil) 2. Deficient (qasir). The complete is like performing prayer in its time with congregation, or tawaf with wudu', and delivering the sold item soundly as required by the contract to the buyer, and the delivery by the usurper of the usurped item as it was usurped... [commentary] ... The ruling of this type is that one is judged to have discharged the responsibility. [Commentary on 'delivery of the very obligation']: Delivery of the very obligation and the like in actions and accidents is to bring them into existence and perform them, for worship is a right of Allah, so the servant performs it and delivers it to Him, and the restriction to time was not considered so that it includes the performance of zakat, trusts, vows, and expiations. 'Obligation' here includes what is fard as well. 'To its due recipient' – this phrase was added even though it is omitted in the expression of many scholars, because it is part of the complete reality of the defined term; for delivery must be complete, and its completion is by the existence of the recipient. How? If the commanded person delivers dirhams of a debt to someone other than the creditor, that delivery is not ada'. So in some glosses. 'Qada' etc.': i.e., qada' is the delivery of the like of the obligation, not the very thing – that is, the delivery of that obligation which was first obligatory at a different time. He should have restricted it by saying 'from him' to exclude the performance of zuhr – i.e., today's zuhr from yesterday's zuhr – because it is not from him but rather both belong to Allah. However, he did not restrict it due to the fame of his command and it being indicated implicitly. So in 'Nur al-Anwar'. 'The complete etc.': It is the performance of the commanded act in the manner prescribed with fulfillment of all its rights. If one fulfills some rights and not others, it is complete in that aspect and deficient in this aspect, like performing prayer with congregation but at a disliked time, or with an imam who is a fasiq, or leaving a wajib or sunnah inside or outside. So the absolute complete is that in which no right of performance or other is omitted from all deficiencies, and the relative complete is that in which some rights are fulfilled and others not, and it coexists with the deficient. 'Performance of prayer': what is meant is the obligatory prayer; because congregation in other than it is a deficient attribute like an extra finger. If one meant absolute prayer, then the example would not match the example. By congregation: indeed prayer with congregation is superior to prayer of an individual by twenty-five degrees as the hadith states. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 94] 'Or tawaf etc.': because of his statement عليه: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer', and prayer without purification is not permissible, but tawaf is valid without purification too due to the absolute text, which is His statement تعالى: ﴿and let them circumambulate the Ancient House﴾.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage defines the key terms ada' (performance) and qada' (make-up) in Hanafi usul. Ada' is delivering the exact obligation (like praying zuhr in its time) to its rightful recipient (Allah for worship, the buyer for sale). Qada' is delivering a similar obligation (like making up a missed prayer at a later time). The passage then divides ada' into complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). Complete ada' fulfills all conditions and rights, e.g., praying on time with congregation. Deficient ada' misses some aspects, e.g., praying on time but at a disliked time. The commentary elaborates: the definition of ada' includes the phrase 'to its due recipient' to exclude cases where delivery is to the wrong person. For qada', it notes that the obligation is a 'like' of the original (e.g., similar prayer but not the exact same moment). The passage also provides examples from fiqh: sale (delivery of sound goods), usurpation (return of the exact item), prayer (with congregation), and tawaf (with or without wudu'). It cites hadith for the superiority of congregational prayer and the hadith that 'tawaf is prayer' with a note that tawaf does not require wudu' unlike prayer. This lesson is foundational for understanding how obligations are discharged in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الأداء (al-ada'): The performance of an obligation exactly as first required, delivering the very same obligation to its due recipient (e.g., praying zuhr in its time).
القضاء (al-qada'): The performance of a similar obligation (mithl) to make up for a missed original obligation (e.g., praying zuhr after its time).
الكامل (al-kamil): Performance that fulfills all conditions and rights of the commanded act, e.g., prayer on time with congregation and all sunnahs.
القاصر (al-qasir): Performance that fulfills only the bare minimum, missing some rights (e.g., prayer on time but without congregation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the definition of 'ada' (performance)?
A) Delivering a similar obligation to the due recipient
B) Delivering the very obligation to its due recipient
C) Performing any act of worship
D) Making up a missed prayer

Key Takeaway
Ada' delivers the exact obligation; qada' delivers a similar obligation; both discharge the duty, but completeness of ada' depends on fulfilling all rights.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Definitions of Ada and Qada and Types of Ada
Defines أداء and قضاء, then explains كامل and قاصر with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between أداء (ada) and قضاء (qada) by applying the Hanafi usul definitions, and classify a given act of worship or transaction as complete or deficient ada.

Core Idea
Ada delivers the very obligation; qada delivers its equivalent; complete ada fulfills all rights; deficient ada still fulfills the essence.

This lesson unpacks two foundational terms in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: الأداء (ada) and القضاء (qada). These concepts are essential for understanding how obligations are discharged, whether in worship or transactions. The passage also introduces the subdivision of ada into complete (كامل) and deficient (قاصر), with concrete examples from prayer, circumambulation, and sales. By the end, you will be able to apply these definitions to new scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Learn the primary definitions
Note the precise Arabic of each definition: ada is 'delivering the very obligation (ayn al-wajib) to its entitled one'; qada is 'delivering the equivalent (mithl) of the obligation to its entitled one'. Understand the key difference between 'ayn and mithl.
2
Understand the condition 'to its entitled one'
The author added 'to its entitled one' to complete the definition. Why is this phrase essential? Consider: paying a debt to a wrong person does not count as ada. This condition ensures the delivery reaches the rightful party.
3
Explore the two types of ada
Complete ada (كامل) delivers the obligation with all its prescribed rights fulfilled. Deficient ada (قاصر) delivers the very obligation but with a deficiency in its description. Identify what 'rights' refer to – e.g., performing prayer in congregation with full tranquility.
4
Examine the examples
For each given example (prayer with congregation, circumambulation with wudu, returning a sold item soundly, returning a usurped item as taken), determine whether it illustrates complete or deficient ada. Note that some examples may be relative complete (كامل إضافي) if only some rights are fulfilled.
5
Note the ikhtilaf on ta'dil al-arkan
The passage mentions that ta'dil al-arkan (tranquility in bowing, prostrations, etc.) is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad but fard according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. How does this affect the classification of a prayer without tranquility? In the Hanafi view, it is deficient ada (valid but incomplete); in the Shafi'i view, it is invalid.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فالأداء: عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه. والقضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه.
ثم الأداء نوعان: ۱- كامل ۲ وقاصر.
―
فصل في الأداء والقضاء
فالكامل: مثل أداء الصلاة في وقتها بالجماعة، أو الطواف متوضياً، وتسليم المبيع سليماً كما اقتضاه العقدُ إلى المشتري، وتسليم الغاصب العين المغصوبة كما غصبها. أداؤه وتفويضه عن مالكها وحكم هذا النوع أن يُحكم بالخروج عن العهدة به. بخروج المأمور
تسليم عين الواجب إلخ تسليم عين الواجب والمثل في الأفعال والأعراض إيجادها والإتيان بها، فإن العبادة حق الله تعالى، فالعبد يؤديها ويسلمها إليه ولم يعتبر التقييد بالوقت ليعم أداء الزكاة والأمانات والمنذورات والكفارات، والمراد بالواجب ههنا : ما يعم الفرض أيضاً. إلى مستحقه إنما زاد هذا اللفظ مع أنه متروك في عبارة كثير من المشايخ؛ لأنه من تمام حقيقة المحدود؛ إذ التسليم لابد من تمامه وتمامه بوجود المسلم إليه كيف وإنما المأمور به إذا سلم دراهم دين إلى غير رب الدين لا يكون ذلك التسليم أداء كذا في بعض الحواشي. والقضاء إلخ : أي القضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب لا عينه أي تسليم ذلك الواجب الذي وجب أولاً في غير ذلك الوقت، وكان ينبغي أن يقيده بقوله: "من عنده" ليخرج أداء الظهر أي ظهر اليوم عن ظهر أمسه؛ لأنه ليس من عنده بل عنده بل كلاهما الله تعالى، وإنما لم يقيده بشهرة أمره وكونه مدلولاً عليه بالالتزام كذا في "نور الأنوار". فالكامل إلخ هو أداء المأمور به على وجه شرع عليه مع إيفاء جميع حقوقه، ولو استوفى بعض حقوقه دون بعض فهو كامل ذلك الوجه قاصر من هذا الوجه كأداء الصلاة بالجماعة إذا أديت في وقت مكروه، أو بإمامة من الفاسق، وبترك واجب، أو سنة من داخلها أو خارجها، فالكامل المطلق ما لا يترك فيه حق من حقوق الأداء وغيره عن النقصانات كلها والكامل الإضافي ما استوفى فيه بعضها دون بعض وهو يجامع القاصر. أداء الصَّلاة: المراد بها الصلاة المكتوبة؛ لأن الجماعة فيما عداها صفة قصور بمنزلة الإصبع الزائدة، فلو أريد بها مطلق الصلاة فلم يطابق المثال بالمثل كما لا يخفى بالجماعة: فإن الصلاة بالجماعة قد فضلت على صلاة المنفرد بخمس وعشرين درجة كما نطق به الحديث. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ٩٤] أو الطواف إلخ: لقوله عليه: "الطواف بالبيت صلاة، والصلاة بدون الطهارة لا تجوز، لكنه يجزئ بدون الطهارة أيضاً؛ لإطلاق النص، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلْيَطُوفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ الْعَتيق

البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في الأداء والقضاء
وعلى هذا قلنا: الغاصب إذا باع المغصوب من المالك أو رَهَنه عنده، أو وَهَب له وسلَّمه المالك الغاصب إليه، يخرج عن العهدة ويكون ذلك أداء لحقه، ويلغو ما صرح به من البيع والهبة. ولو غَصَبَ طعاماً فأَطْعَمَه مالكه وهو لا يدري أنه طعامه، أو غَصَبَ ثوباً فأَلْبَسَه مالكه وهو لا يدري أنه ثوبه يكون ذلك أداء الحقه، والمشتري في البيع الفاسد لو أعار المبيع من البائع أو رَهَنه عنده، أو آجَرَه منه، أو باعه منه، أو وَهَبه له وسلّمه يكون ذلك أداء المبيع لحقه ويلغو ما صرح به من البيع والهبة ونحوه. وأمَّا الأداء القاصر: فهو تسليم عين الواجب مع النقصان في صفته نحو الصلاة بدون تعديل الأركان، أو الطواف محدثاً، وردّ المبيع مشغولاً بالدين أو بالجناية، ورد المغصوب أداء لحقه: هذا إذا لم يحدث فيه ما يقطع حق المالك، فأما إذا حدث فيه ما يقطع حقه بأن كان دقيقاً فخبزه فأطعمه، أو لحماً فشواه ثم أطعمه لا يبرأ عن الضمان بالاتفاق؛ لأنه ملك بهذه التصرفات كذا في "المعدن". في البيع الفاسد : البيوع أنواع صحيح وهو المشروع بأصله ووصفه وباطل وهو ضده، وهو لا يفيد الملك بوجه، وفاسد: وهو المشروع بأصله دون وصفه ويفيد الملك إذا اتصل به القبض، ومثال البيع الفاسد: بيع السمك في الماء، وبيع المجهول. [حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ١١٣] اعلم أن البيع الفاسد كالبيع بالخمر والخنزير، والبيع بشرط لا يقتضيه العقد فيه منفعة لأحد العاقدين أو المعقود عليه وهو من أهل الاستحقاق كما إذا باع عبداً بشرط أن يعتقه المشتري أو يدبره أو يكاتبه، أو أمة على أن يستولدها المشتري، فإذا قبض المبيع المشتري في البيع الفاسد يكون المبيع مضموناً في يده، ولكل واحد عن المتعاقدين فسخه دفعاً للفساد، ويجب على المشتري رد المبيع إلى البائع، فإذا أعار المشتري المبيع من البائع، أو رهنه المشتري عند البائع أو أعطى المشتري المبيع للبائع بالأجرة، أو وهب المشتري المبيع للبائع، وقبض البائع يكون ذلك أداء الحقه دون تسليم عين الواجب هذا ملخص الكتب. بدون تعديل إلخ تعديل الأركان :هو الطمأنية في الركوع والسجدتين والقومة بعد الركوع، والجلسة بين السجدتين في ظاهر الرواية، وهو أي: التعديل واجب عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحم الله، فإذا تركه جازت الصلاة النقصان بفوات الوصف، وعند أبي يوسف والشافعي حملها فرض، وبسطه في الفروع. = مع

The First Inquiry concerning the Book of Allah.
So al-Ada: it is an expression for delivering the very obligation to its entitled one. And al-Qada: it is an expression for delivering the equivalent of the obligation to its entitled one.
Then al-Ada is of two types: 1- complete and 2- deficient.
―
Section on al-Ada and al-Qada
So the complete: like performing prayer in its time with congregation, or circumambulating in wudu, and delivering the sold item soundly as the contract required to the buyer, and the usurper delivering the usurped item as he usurped it. His delivering and entrusting it from its owner. And the ruling of this type is that it is judged that liability is discharged by it. By the exit of the commanded.
"Delivering the very obligation etc.": delivering the very obligation and the equivalent in actions and accidents is creating them and performing them, for worship is the right of Allah Almighty, so the servant performs it and delivers it to Him, and restriction by time was not considered so that it includes the delivery of zakat, trusts, vows, and expiations. And what is meant by al-wajib here: that which includes al-fard as well. "To its entitled one": he added this word even though it is omitted in the expression of many shaykhs; because it is part of the completeness of the reality of the defined; since delivery must be complete and its completion is by the existence of the one delivered to. Indeed, if the commanded one delivers dirhams of debt to someone other than the creditor, that delivery is not ada. So mentioned in some footnotes.
"And al-Qada etc.": i.e. al-Qada is an expression for delivering the equivalent of the obligation, not the very obligation, i.e. delivering that obligation which was first obligatory at a time other than that time. And he should have restricted it by his saying "from himself" to exclude performing the zuhr of today from yesterday's zuhr; because it is not from himself but with himself, but both are by Allah Almighty. And he did not restrict it due to the fame of its matter and its being indicated by implication, as in "Nur al-Anwar". "So the complete etc." is performing the commanded in the manner prescribed with fulfilling all its rights. If he fulfills some of its rights without others, then it is complete from that aspect and deficient from this aspect, like performing prayer with congregation if performed at a disliked time, or with an imam who is a fasiq, and leaving an obligatory or sunnah act from within or outside it. So the absolutely complete is that in which no right from the rights of performance and others is left regarding all deficiencies, and the relative complete is that in which some of them are fulfilled without others, and it can coexist with the deficient.
"Performing prayer": what is meant is the obligatory prayer; because congregation in other than it is a quality of deficiency like an extra finger. If absolute prayer were meant, then the example would not match the example, as is not hidden. "With congregation": for the prayer with congregation is superior to the prayer of an individual by twenty-five degrees as stated in the hadith. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p.94]
"Or circumambulating etc.": because of his saying (peace be upon him): "Circumambulation of the House is prayer, and prayer without purification is not permissible." But it is valid without purification due to the unrestrictedness of the text, which is His statement: "And let them circumambulate the Ancient House" [Quran 22:29].

[PAGE_102]
The First Inquiry concerning the Book of Allah
Section on al-Ada and al-Qada
And based on this we said: if the usurper sells the usurped item to the owner, or pawns it with him, or gives it as a gift and the owner delivers it to him (the usurper), he is discharged from liability and that is ada of his right, and what he explicitly stated of sale and gift is void. And if he usurps food and feeds it to its owner without the owner knowing it is his food, or usurps a garment and clothes its owner without the owner knowing it is his garment, that is ada of his right. And the buyer in a void (fasid) sale, if he lends the sold item to the seller, or pawns it with him, or leases it to him, or sells it to him, or gives it as a gift to him and delivers it, that is ada of his right and what he explicitly stated of sale and gift and the like is void.
"As for the deficient ada: it is delivering the very obligation with a deficiency in its description, like prayer without straightening the pillars, or circumambulating without ablution, and returning the sold item encumbered by a debt or by a crime, and returning the usurped item."
"Ada of his right": this is if he did not do something that cuts off the owner's right. But if he did something that cuts off his right, as if it was flour and he baked it and fed it, or meat and he roasted it then fed it, he is not freed from liability by consensus, because he owned it through these dispositions. So in "al-Ma'din".
"In the fasid sale": sales are of types: sound (sahih) which is legislated in its foundation and description, void (batil) which is its opposite and does not confer ownership at all, and fasid which is legislated in its foundation but not in its description and confers ownership if possession is taken. And examples of fasid sale: selling fish in water, and selling the unknown. [Hashiyah of Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi: p.113] Know that the fasid sale is like selling for wine or pig, and selling with a condition that does not require the contract in which there is benefit for one of the two contracting parties or the object of contract while he is eligible, such as if he sells a slave on condition that the buyer frees him or makes him a mudabbar or a mukatib, or a female slave on condition that the buyer seeks to impregnate her. Then if the buyer takes possession of the sold item in a fasid sale, the sold item is held as a trust in his hand, and each of the two contracting parties may rescind it to remove the defect, and the buyer must return the sold item to the seller. So if the buyer lends the sold item to the seller, or pawns it with the seller, or gives the sold item to the seller for rent, or gives the sold item to the seller as a gift, and the seller takes possession, that is ada of his right, but not delivering the very obligation. This is the summary of the books.
"Without straightening etc.": straightening the pillars (ta'dil al-arkan) is tranquility (tumaninah) in bowing, the two prostrations, the standing after bowing, and the sitting between the two prostrations in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). And it (ta'dil) is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). So if he leaves it, the prayer is valid with deficiency due to the loss of the description. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, it is fard in prayer, as elaborated in the furu'.

.....
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a definition section from the Hanafi usul work 'Usul al-Shashi'. It first defines the two key terms: الأداء (ada) and القضاء (qada). Ada is defined as 'delivering the very obligation (ayn al-wajib) to its entitled one', while qada is 'delivering the equivalent (mithl) of the obligation to its entitled one'. The author then clarifies that 'wajib' here includes both fard and wajib, and the addition of 'to its entitled one' is essential to complete the definition. The passage then divides ada into two types: complete (كامل) and deficient (قاصر). Complete ada is delivering the obligation with all its rights fulfilled, such as praying in congregation at its proper time. It also discusses when a usurper or a buyer in a fasid sale returns the item to the owner, and that counts as ada. Deficient ada is delivering the obligation with a deficiency in its description, like praying without tranquility (ta'dil al-arkan). The commentary explains that ta'dil al-arkan is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but a fard according to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i. The passage also includes discussions on the sale of fish in water and other fasid sales. The commentary references works like 'Nur al-Anwar' and 'Umdat al-Hawashi'.

Key Terms
الأداء (al-ada): Delivering the very obligation (ayn al-wajib) to its entitled one
القضاء (al-qada): Delivering the equivalent (mithl) of the obligation to its entitled one
الأداء الكامل (al-ada al-kamil): Performing the obligation with all its prescribed rights and conditions fulfilled
الأداء القاصر (al-ada al-qasir): Delivering the very obligation but with a deficiency in its description or some rights omitted

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of القضاء (qada)?
A) تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه
B) تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه
C) تسليم الواجب مع النقصان في صفته
D) تسليم الواجب بجميع حقوقه

Key Takeaway
The distinction between ada (exact obligation) and qada (equivalent) is fundamental; complete ada fulfills all rights, while deficient ada still discharges the essence.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Deficient Performance (Ada Qasir) and Compensation with Similar
Definition and ruling of deficient performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for deficient performance and apply it to new scenarios involving compensation with a similar.

Core Idea
A deficient performance remains valid but requires compensation with a similar if possible; otherwise, the sin remains.

This lesson introduces a key Hanafi usul principle: not every imperfection in performing an obligation invalidates it. Instead, the law distinguishes between the validity of the act and the need to compensate for any deficiency. By understanding this, you will grasp how the school balances fulfilling obligations with practical realities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of deficient performance (ada qasir)
Recognize that ada qasir refers to an act that fulfills the essential obligation but is lacking in some quality or description.
The three examples in the passage illustrate this: blood money encumbered, item with debt, counterfeit coins.
2
Understand the rule of compensation with a similar (jabr bil mithl)
If the deficiency can be compensated by providing something similar (mithl) in value or kind, then compensation is required.
The text says 'إن أمكن جبر النقصان بالمثل ينجبر به'.
3
Apply the consequence when compensation is impossible
If no similar exists, the deficiency is overlooked in terms of the obligation, but the person remains sinful for the imperfection.
The phrase 'وإلا يسقط حكم النقصان إلا في الإثم' indicates this.
4
Distinguish from invalid performance
This ruling applies only to deficient performance that still meets the essential requirements. A completely invalid act (batil) requires full repetition, not compensation.
The passage does not discuss batil, but the ruling presupposes the act is valid in essence.

Source Text

البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في الأداء والقضاء
مباحُ الدم بالقتل، أو مشغولاً بالدين، أو الجناية بسبب عند الغاصب، وأداء الزيوف مكان الجياد إذا لم يَعْلَم الدائن ذلك.
وحكمُ هذا النوع أنه إن أمكن جبرُ النقصان بالمثل ينجَبَرُ به وإلا يَسقط حكم النقصان النقصان وإن لم يكن جبره بالمثل
إلا في الإثم.
The First Research: On the Book of Allah. Chapter on Performance and Recompense. The blood money [paid] due to killing, or an item encumbered with debt, or a crime [committed] against the possessor, and the payment of counterfeit coins in place of good ones when the creditor is unaware of that. The ruling of this type is that if it is possible to compensate the deficiency with a similar, it is compensated thereby; otherwise, the ruling of the deficiency falls away, and it is not compensated with a similar except in sin.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage opens a chapter on 'ada' (performance) and 'qada' (recompense), part of the discussion on legal obligations. The author lists three examples of deficient performance: paying blood money that is encumbered, returning a stolen item that has become encumbered with debt, and paying counterfeit coins to a creditor who is unaware. The central rule is that if the deficiency can be made up by providing a 'mithl' (similar in value or kind), then it must be done. If no similar exists—like when a qualitative deficiency cannot be remedied—then the obligation is still considered fulfilled in terms of the original duty, but the person remains sinful for the deficiency. This rule is foundational in Hanafi usul for understanding how imperfect performance affects liability.

Key Terms
أداء قاصر (adā' qāṣir): A performance that fulfills the essential obligation but is deficient in some quality or description.
المثل (al-mithl): A similar thing that can compensate for the deficiency, either in kind or as legally determined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what happens if a deficiency in performance cannot be compensated with a similar?
A) The entire performance becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The deficiency is ignored and the performance is considered perfect.
C) The deficiency is not compensated with a similar, but the sin remains.
D) The deficiency is automatically compensated by an alternative prescribed by law.

Key Takeaway
A deficient performance is valid but requires compensation with a similar if possible; otherwise, the deficiency is remitted but sin remains.

Complete and Deficient Qada: The Hanafi Framework of Compensation
Defines types of compensation and fungible goods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define and distinguish between complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir) qada, and classify goods as mithli (fungible) or qimi (non-fungible) according to Hanafi law.

Core Idea
Compensation is either by delivering a like in form and meaning (mithl) or by value (qima) when exact substitution fails.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi framework of compensation (qada). The text from Usul al-Shashi defines two types of qada and provides the criteria for distinguishing fungibles (mithli) from non-fungibles (qimi). Understanding these categories is essential for determining the correct mode of compensation in cases of usurpation or destruction.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of qada
State the two types: kamil (complete) involves delivering a like in both form and meaning; qasir (deficient) involves delivering value which matches in meaning only. Identify examples from the text (wheat vs. goat).
2
Define mithli (fungible)
Explain that mithli is a good that has a like in the market without appreciable price difference. The text provides three categories: measured, weighed, and closely similar countable items.
3
Differentiate mithli from qimi
Qimi goods have no like; value must be paid. Examples: animals and clothes. Understand the rationale: drastic variation among individuals precludes exact similarity.
4
Apply the definitions to case scenarios
Given a specific good, decide if it is mithli or qimi and determine the appropriate compensation: like (mithl) for fungibles, value (qima) for non-fungibles.

Source Text

البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في الأداء والقضاء
ويتفرع من هذا: مسألة المضمونات، ولذا قال لو ظهر العبد المغصوب بعد ما أَخَذَ المالك ضمائه من الغاصب كان العبد ملكاً للمالك، والواجب على المالك ردُّ ما أخذ من قيمة العبد.
وأما القضاء فنوعان - كامل - وقاصر.
فالكامل منه: تسليم مثل الواجب صورةً ومعنى، كمَنْ غصب قفيز حنطة فاستهلكها ضمنَ قفيز حنطة، ويكون المؤدى مثلاً للأول صورةً ومعنى، وكذلك الحكم في جميع المثليات. وأمَّا القاصرُ: فهو ما لا يماثلُ الواجب صورةً ويماثلُ معنى، كمن غصب شاةٌ فَهَلَكَتْ ضمن قيمتها والقيمَةُ مثل الشاة من حيث المعنى لا من حيث الصورة.
= المغصوبة الهالكة الثابت بذمة القاضي - الواجب بظاهر الرواية؛ لأنها رويت عن الإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني برواية الثقات عنه، فهي إما متواترة أو مشهورة. [الشافي: ص ١٤٨] ويتفرع من هذا : أي مما تقدم من أن المغصوب إذا صنع فيه الغاصب وتغير تغيراً فاحشاً يعتبر صنعته ويجعل المغصوب كالهالك حتى يزول عنه ملك المالك ويدخل في ملك الغاصب عندنا خلافاً للشافعي. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ۱۰۰] مسألة المضمونات، فإن المغصوب إذا تغير تغيراً فاحشاً يجب على الغاصب قيمته عندنا، وضمان المغصوب عنده.
في جميع المثليات تعريف المثلي: كل ما يوجد له مثل في الأسواق بلا تفاوت يعتد به، أي: لا يختلف لسببه الثمن فهو مثلي، وما ليس كذلك فقيمي. [حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ۱۱۹] وهي المكيلات كالحنطة والشعير وغيرهما، والموزونات كالذهب والفضة ونحوهما، والعدديات المتقاربة كالجوز والبيض؛ لقلة التفاوت بين أفرادها، وأما غير المثليات فمثل الحيوانات والثياب؛ فإن ثوباً لا يماثل ثوباً من جميع الوجوه، ولهذا يتفاوتان قيمةً لا محالة، وكذلك الحيوان، فلذا وجبت القيمة عند هلاك العين في غير المثلي؛ لتعذر رعاية المماثلة صورة ومعنى للتفاوت الفاحش بين أمثالها، وأما القيمة فهو مثل معنى لا تفاوت فيه أصلاً فكانت أولى كذا في "المعدن". ضمن قيمتها: أي قيمة الشاة؛ لأن حق المستحق في الصورة والمعنى جميعاً، إلا أن حقه في الصورة قد فات للعجز عن القضاء، فبقي حقه في المعنى وهي القيمة والقيمة إلخ: لأنها تعادل الشاة في المالية وتقوم مقامها، ولذا سميت قيمة.

البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في الأداء والقضاء
والأصل في القضاء الكامل.
وعلى هذا قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله: إذا غصب مثلياً فهَلَكَ في يده انقطع ذلك عن أيدي الناس ضمن قيمته يومَ الخصومة؛ لأن العجز عن تسليم المثل الكامل إنما يظهر عند الخصومة، فأما قبل الخصومة فلا؛ لتصور حصول المثل من كل وجه.
فأما ما لا مثل له لا صورةً ولا معنى لا يمكن إيجاب القضاء فيه بالمثل.
ولهذا المعنى قلنا: إن المنافِعَ لا تضمن بالإتلاف؛ لأن إيجاب الضمان بالمثل متعذر.
الكامل: أي الأداء بالمثل صورة ومعنى، فإن فيه رعاية حق المستحق صورة ومعنى. قال أبو حنيفة إلخ: وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله: يضمن قيمته يوم الغصب؛ لأنه هو الموجب للضمان والخصومة، فاعتبار قيمة المضمون وقت تحقق الضمان أولى من اعتباره وقت الخصومة، وقال محمد رحمه الله: يضمن قيمته يوم الانقطاع عن أيدي الناس؛ لأن الواجب هو المثل وإنما يصار إلى القيمة عند العجز عنه، والعجز إنما يتحقق عند الانقطاع عن أيدي الناس كذا في "المعدن".
لا يمكن إيجاب إلخ: يعني إنما وجب الضمان بالمثل الكامل أو بالقاصر فيما له مثل أو له قيمة، وأما ما لا قيمة له فلا يضمن إلا بالإثم؛ لأنه لا مثل له صورة ولا معنى، إلا أن يرد الشرع بالمثل له صورة كما ذكر بعد هذه المسائل كذا في "الفصول". ولهذا المعنى: أي لأجل أن ما لا مثل له لا صورة ولا معنى لا يمكن إيجاب القضاء فيه كذا في "الفصول". قلنا إلخ هذا المسألة مختلف فيها، فعندنا لا تضمن إلا أن ينقص باستعماله، فيغرم النقصان، وقال الشافعي رحمه الله: يضمنها، فيجب أجر المثل وبه قال أحمد، وقال مالك: إن سكن الدار مثلاً يجب أجر المثل، وإن عطلها فلا شيء عليه. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ۱۰۱]
لا تضمن بالإتلاف وصورة إتلاف المنافع: أن يستعمل الأعيان المغصوبة بأن يستخدم العبد ويركب الدابة المغصوبة ويسكن البيت فإنه لا يجب ضمانها على المتلف لا بمثلها ولا بقيمتها؛ لأن إيجاب الضمان بمثلها من المنافع متعذر؛ لأن المنافع تتفاوت تفاوتاً كثيراً على حسب تفاوت أعيانها، فإن منفعة عبد مثلاً لا تماثل منفعة عبد آخر؛ للتفاوت بين المنفعتين كذا في بعض شروح "المنار". متعذر : لأن المنافع تتفاوت تفاوتاً كثيراً على حسب تفاوت أعيانها، فإن منفعة عبد مثلاً لا يماثل منفعة عبد آخر؛ للتفاوت بين المنفعتين كذا في "المعدن".
First investigation in the Book of Allah. Chapter on Performance and Compensation. And from this branches: the issue of guaranteed objects. Hence he said: If the usurped slave appears after the owner has taken his guarantee from the usurper, the slave is the property of the owner, and the owner must return what he took of the slave's value. As for compensation, it is of two types - complete and deficient. The complete is: delivering a substitute for the obligatory in form and meaning, like one who usurps a bushel of wheat and consumes it, he guarantees a bushel of wheat, and the delivered substitute is a like for the first in form and meaning. Similarly the ruling for all fungibles. As for the deficient: it is that which does not match the obligatory in form but matches in meaning, like one who usurps a goat and it perishes, he guarantees its value, and the value is like the goat in meaning but not in form. [The obligatory is fixed by the judge's liability] by apparent transmission; because it is transmitted from Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani through reliable chains, so it is either mutawatir or mashhur. [al-Shafi: p. 148] And from this branches: from what preceded that if a usurped object is transformed by the usurper with a drastic change, his action is considered and the usurped object becomes like perished until the owner's ownership is removed and it enters into the usurper's ownership according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 100] Issue of guaranteed objects: when the usurped object changes drastically, the usurper must pay its value according to us, and the guarantee of the object is with him. In all fungibles: definition of fungible: everything for which a like can be found in the markets without appreciable difference, i.e., the price does not vary due to it, it is fungible; what is not so is non-fungible. [Hashiyah of Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi: p. 119] They are measured goods like wheat and barley etc., weighed goods like gold and silver etc., and closely similar countable goods like walnuts and eggs due to little variation among their units. As for non-fungibles, such as animals and clothes; for a garment does not resemble another garment in all respects, hence they inevitably differ in value, likewise animals. Therefore value is obligated at the destruction of the object in non-fungibles due to the impossibility of observing similarity in form and meaning because of the drastic difference among their likes. As for value, it is a like in meaning with no difference at all, so it is more appropriate. [Al-Ma'din] 'He guarantees its value': i.e., the value of the goat; because the claimant's right is in both form and meaning, except that his right in form has been lost due to inability to compensate, so his right in meaning remains, which is the value. 'And the value etc.': because it equals the goat in monetary value and stands in its place, hence it is called value. [PAGE_109] First investigation in the Book of Allah. Chapter on Performance and Compensation. The principle in complete compensation. Based on this, Abu Hanifa said: If someone usurps a fungible and it perishes in his hand and becomes scarce among people, he guarantees its value on the day of lawsuit; because inability to deliver the complete like only appears at the time of lawsuit. Before lawsuit, it is not so due to the possibility of obtaining the like in every aspect. As for that which has no like either in form or meaning, it is not possible to impose compensation with a like. For this meaning we said: Benefits are not guaranteed by destruction; because imposing guarantee with a like is impossible. 'Complete': i.e., performance with a like in form and meaning, for it observes the claimant's right in form and meaning. Abu Hanifa said etc.: Abu Yusuf said: He guarantees its value on the day of usurpation; because that is what necessitates guarantee and lawsuit, so considering the value of the guaranteed object at the time guarantee is realized is more appropriate than considering it at the time of lawsuit. Muhammad said: He guarantees its value on the day of scarcity among people; because the obligatory is the like, and value is resorted to only at inability, and inability is realized at the time of scarcity among people. [Al-Ma'din] 'It is not possible to impose etc.': meaning that guarantee is obligated either with a complete like or a deficient one for that which has a like or a value. But for that which has no value, it is not guaranteed except by sin; because it has no like in form or meaning, unless the law brings a like for it in form as mentioned after these issues. [Al-Fusul] 'For this meaning': i.e., because that which has no like in form or meaning cannot have compensation imposed. [Al-Fusul] 'We said etc.' This issue is disputed; according to us, [benefits] are not guaranteed unless there is decrease from use, then he pays the decrease. Al-Shafi'i said: He guarantees them, so the equivalent wage is obligatory; Ahmad said the same. Malik said: If he resides in the house for example, the equivalent rent is obligatory; if he leaves it idle, nothing is due. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 101] 'Not guaranteed by destruction' and the form of destroying benefits: That the usurped objects are used by employing the slave, riding the usurped animal, and residing in the house. Then no guarantee is obligatory on the destroyer neither by its like nor by its value; because imposing guarantee with a like of benefits is impossible because benefits vary greatly according to the variation of their objects. For the benefit of a slave, for example, does not resemble the benefit of another slave due to the difference between the two benefits. [Al-Ma'din]
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi discusses two types of compensation (qada) in Hanafi law: complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). Complete compensation involves delivering a substitute that matches the original in both form and meaning, like paying a bushel of wheat for a bushel of wheat. Deficient compensation applies when exact substitution is impossible, such as when a goat is destroyed; here the value is paid, which matches the original in meaning (monetary value) but not in form.

The text then defines fungible (mithli) goods: those for which exact substitutes exist in the market without appreciable variation in price. Examples include measured items (wheat, barley), weighed items (gold, silver), and closely similar countable items (walnuts, eggs). Non-fungible (qimi) items like animals and clothes have individual variation, so value is paid upon destruction.

A key ruling by Abu Hanifa: for fungibles lost, value is assessed at the time of the lawsuit because inability to deliver the exact like becomes apparent then. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ: Abu Yusuf considers the day of usurpation, Muhammad the day the item becomes scarce.

Finally, benefits (manafi) of usurped property are not compensable according to Abu Hanifa, because benefits cannot be exactly replicated. This opposes al-Shafi'i, who requires payment of the equivalent wage. The Hanafi view is that unless the property is diminished by use, no compensation is due for mere use.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada): Compensation: delivering a substitute for a destroyed or consumed object.
المثلي (al-mithli): A good for which a like exists in the market without appreciable price difference.
القيمي (al-qimi): A good that does not have a like; compensation is by value.
المنافع (al-manafi): Benefits or usufruct of an object, such as the service of a slave or use of a house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definitions in this lesson, which of the following is an example of qasir (deficient) qada?
A) Delivering a bushel of wheat for a bushel of wheat
B) Paying the market value of a destroyed goat
C) Returning the exact same goat alive
D) Delivering a more expensive goat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes delivering a like (mithl) in form and meaning; value is secondary when like is impossible.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Time of Valuation for Lost Fungibles and the Non-Compensability of Benefits
Presents intra-Hanafi dispute on valuation timing and inter-madhhab dispute on benefits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the time of valuation for lost fungibles and explain why benefits (manafi) are not compensable under Hanafi law.

Core Idea
The time for valuing a lost fungible varies among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad; benefits are not compensable because they cannot be replicated exactly.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi debate on when to value a lost fungible and the broader principle that benefits (manafi) are not independently compensable. The text recounts the views of the three leading Hanafi imams and the disagreement with al-Shafi'i on the guarantee of usufruct.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions on valuation timing
Abu Hanifa: value at time of lawsuit. Abu Yusuf: value at time of usurpation. Muhammad: value at time of scarcity (when the like becomes unavailable). Understand the rationale behind each.
2
Understand the rationale behind each position
Abu Hanifa: inability to deliver the like appears only at lawsuit. Abu Yusuf: liability arises at usurpation, so value at that time. Muhammad: value is only a fallback when the like is unavailable, so scarcity time.
3
Analyze the ruling on benefits (manafi)
Hanafi: benefits are not compensable by like or value; only compensatory if the property is diminished by use. Shafi'i: benefits are compensable by equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl). Malik's intermediate view: compensable only if actually used.
4
Apply the principles to a case
Given a scenario (e.g., wheat usurped and destroyed, price fluctuates), determine which valuation time applies under each imam's view. Also, if a house is occupied without permission, determine if rent is due under Hanafi vs. Shafi'i.

البحث الأول في كتاب الله
فصل في الأداء والقضاء
ويتفرع من هذا: مسألة المضمونات، ولذا قال لو ظهر العبد المغصوب بعد ما أَخَذَ المالك ضمائه من الغاصب كان العبد ملكاً للمالك، والواجب على المالك ردُّ ما أخذ من قيمة العبد.
وأما القضاء فنوعان - كامل - وقاصر.
فالكامل منه: تسليم مثل الواجب صورةً ومعنى، كمَنْ غصب قفيز حنطة فاستهلكها ضمنَ قفيز حنطة، ويكون المؤدى مثلاً للأول صورةً ومعنى، وكذلك الحكم في جميع المثليات. وأمَّا القاصرُ: فهو ما لا يماثلُ الواجب صورةً ويماثلُ معنى، كمن غصب شاةٌ فَهَلَكَتْ ضمن قيمتها والقيمَةُ مثل الشاة من حيث المعنى لا من حيث الصورة.
= المغصوبة الهالكة الثابت بذمة القاضي - الواجب بظاهر الرواية؛ لأنها رويت عن الإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني برواية الثقات عنه، فهي إما متواترة أو مشهورة. [الشافي: ص ١٤٨] ويتفرع من هذا : أي مما تقدم من أن المغصوب إذا صنع فيه الغاصب وتغير تغيراً فاحشاً يعتبر صنعته ويجعل المغصوب كالهالك حتى يزول عنه ملك المالك ويدخل في ملك الغاصب عندنا خلافاً للشافعي. [عمدة الحواشي: ص ۱۰۰] مسألة المضمونات، فإن المغصوب إذا تغير تغيراً فاحشاً يجب على الغاصب قيمته عندنا، وضمان المغصوب عنده.

'And the value etc.': because it equals the goat in monetary value and stands in its place, hence it is called value. [PAGE_109] First investigation in the Book of Allah. Chapter on Performance and Compensation. The principle in complete compensation. Based on this, Abu Hanifa said: If someone usurps a fungible and it perishes in his hand and becomes scarce among people, he guarantees its value on the day of lawsuit; because inability to deliver the complete like only appears at the time of lawsuit. Before lawsuit, it is not so due to the possibility of obtaining the like in every aspect. As for that which has no like either in form or meaning, it is not possible to impose compensation with a like. For this meaning we said: Benefits are not guaranteed by destruction; because imposing guarantee with a like is impossible. 'Complete': i.e., performance with a like in form and meaning, for it observes the claimant's right in form and meaning. Abu Hanifa said etc.: Abu Yusuf said: He guarantees its value on the day of usurpation; because that is what necessitates guarantee and lawsuit, so considering the value of the guaranteed object at the time guarantee is realized is more appropriate than considering it at the time of lawsuit. Muhammad said: He guarantees its value on the day of scarcity among people; because the obligatory is the like, and value is resorted to only at inability, and inability is realized at the time of scarcity among people. [Al-Ma'din] 'It is not possible to impose etc.': meaning that guarantee is obligated either with a complete like or a deficient one for that which has a like or a value. But for that which has no value, it is not guaranteed except by sin; because it has no like in form or meaning, unless the law brings a like for it in form as mentioned after these issues. [Al-Fusul] 'For this meaning': i.e., because that which has no like in form or meaning cannot have compensation imposed. [Al-Fusul] 'We said etc.' This issue is disputed; according to us, [benefits] are not guaranteed unless there is decrease from use, then he pays the decrease. Al-Shafi'i said: He guarantees them, so the equivalent wage is obligatory; Ahmad said the same. Malik said: If he resides in the house for example, the equivalent rent is obligatory; if he leaves it idle, nothing is due. [Umdat al-Hawashi: p. 101] 'Not guaranteed by destruction' and the form of destroying benefits: That the usurped objects are used by employing the slave, riding the usurped animal, and residing in the house. Then no guarantee is obligatory on the destroyer neither by its like nor by its value; because imposing guarantee with a like of benefits is impossible because benefits vary greatly according to the variation of their objects. For the benefit of a slave, for example, does not resemble the benefit of another slave due to the difference between the two benefits. [Al-Ma'din]
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi discusses two types of compensation (qada) in Hanafi law: complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). Complete compensation involves delivering a substitute that matches the original in both form and meaning, like paying a bushel of wheat for a bushel of wheat. Deficient compensation applies when exact substitution is impossible, such as when a goat is destroyed; here the value is paid, which matches the original in meaning (monetary value) but not in form.

The text then defines fungible (mithli) goods: those for which exact substitutes exist in the market without appreciable variation in price. Examples include measured items (wheat, barley), weighed items (gold, silver), and closely similar countable items (walnuts, eggs). Non-fungible (qimi) items like animals and clothes have individual variation, so value is paid upon destruction.

A key ruling by Abu Hanifa: for fungibles lost, value is assessed at the time of the lawsuit because inability to deliver the exact like becomes apparent then. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani differ: Abu Yusuf considers the day of usurpation, Muhammad the day the item becomes scarce.

Finally, benefits (manafi) of usurped property are not compensable according to Abu Hanifa, because benefits cannot be exactly replicated. This opposes al-Shafi'i, who requires payment of the equivalent wage. The Hanafi view is that unless the property is diminished by use, no compensation is due for mere use.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada): Compensation: delivering a substitute for a destroyed or consumed object.
المثلي (al-mithli): A good for which a like exists in the market without appreciable price difference.
القيمي (al-qimi): A good that does not have a like; compensation is by value.
المنافع (al-manafi): Benefits or usufruct of an object, such as the service of a slave or use of a house.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which Hanafi imam assesses the value of a lost fungible at the time of scarcity?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) All three

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's nuanced approach to valuation timing reflects the principle that the primary obligation is to deliver the like (mithl); value is only a fallback when the like is unavailable.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
