The Four Types of Rights (Huquq) in Hanafi Usul
Defines four types of rights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of rights according to Hanafi usul and identify the presence or absence of ilzam in each.

Core Idea
Rights are classified by owner and binding (ilzam), determining evidentiary requirements.

In Hanafi usul, legal rights are not monolithic; they are divided into four categories based on whether they belong purely to Allah or to the human slave, and whether they involve a binding obligation (ilzam). This classification is foundational because it dictates the conditions under which a single narrator's report (khabar al-wahid) is accepted as proof. In this lesson, we will learn the precise definition of each category and see examples that anchor them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary owners of rights
Rights belong either to Allah exclusively (haqq Allah) or to the slave exclusively (haqq al-'abd). This is the first distinction.
2
Further divide the slave's rights by ilzam
The slave's right can have pure ilzam, no ilzam, or ilzam from one aspect. This yields three subcategories.
3
Memorize the four categories with their parallels
Each type has a specific parallel (e.g., type 1: acts of worship; type 2: disputes; type 3: transactions; type 4: dismissal/interdiction).
4
Connect to the purpose
This classification sets the stage for rules of evidence (khabar al-wahid). Understand that the presence or absence of ilzam directly affects the strictness of evidentiary conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الثاني في سنة رسول الله
-۱- خالص حق الله تعالى ما ليس بعقوبة.
-٢- وخالص حق العبد ما فيه إلزام محض.
-٣- وخالص حقه ما ليس فيه إلزام.
٤- وخالص حقه ما فيه إلزام من وجه.

فصل في حجية خبر الواحد
أما الأول فيقبل فيه خبر الواحد، فإن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل شهادة الأعرابي في هلال رَمَضَان.
ما ليس بعقوبة: وإنما قيد به؛ لأن ما هو عقوبة من حقوق الله تعالى لا يقبل فيه خبر الواحد عند الكرخي، وإليه ذهب فخر الإسلام، وشمس الأئمة السرخسي، وكذا الماتن له؛ وذلك لأن مبنى الحدود على الإسقاط بالشبهات، فلا يجوز إثباتها بخبر الواحد كما لا يجوز بالقياس، وأما إثباتها بالبينات فيجوز بالنص الموجب للعلم على خلاف القياس، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا﴾ الآية، وقد انعقد الإجماع على ذلك. أما الأول وهو ما كان خالص حق الله ما ليس بعقوبة. فيقبل فيه خبر الواحد إلخ فمثل عامة الشرائع من الصلاة والصوم، والوضوء والعشر، وصدقة الفطر يقبل في كلها خبر الواحد على ما قلنا من شرائطه من الإسلام والعدالة والعقل والضبط عند الجماهير، وزعم بعض العلماء أنه لا يقبل خبر الواحد دليل لا قوة فيه، فجاز أن يعمل فيما ليس فيه قوة وهو الفرع، وللجمهور أن المقصود من العبادات هو العمل أصلاً كانت أو فرعاً، فيجب العمل فيها بالدلائل الموجبة للعمل، ويؤيده أنه عليه قبل شهادة الأعرابي في هلال رمضان كذا في "الفصول". خبر الواحد: مطلقاً من غير اشتراط عدد ولا تعيين لفظ الشهادة والولاية بالحرية. [عمدة الحواشي: ص فإن رسول الله إلخ لأن الثابت بها حق الله تعالى على عباده خالصاً وهو الصوم، حيث قال الله جل شأنه: ﴿كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامُ﴾ الآية، ولهذا لم تشترط فيه الحرية، ولفظ الشهادة فيه مخالف لمرضي فخر الإسلام، حيث ذكر في "أصوله" : أن الشهادة بهلال رمضان من النوع الثالث، وهو خالص حق العبد ما ليس فيه إلزام؛ لأنه جاء أعرابي إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : إني رأيت الهلال، فقال: أتشهد أن لا إله إلا الله؟ قال: نعم، قال: أتشهد أن محمداً رسول الله؟ قال: نعم، قال: "يا بلال أذن في الناس فليصوموا غداً". أخرجه أبو داود في باب في شهادة الواحد على رؤية هلال رمضان، رقم: ٢٣٤٠، والنسائي في باب قبول شهادة الرجل الواحد على هلال شهر رمضان، رقم: ۲۱۱۳، وابن ماجه في باب ما جاء في الشهادة على رؤية الهلال رقم ١٦٥٢ عن ابن عباس.

وأما الثاني: فيشترط فيه العدد والعدالة.
ونظيره: "المنازعات".

وأما الثالث: فيقبَلُ فيه خبَرُ الواحد عدلاً كان أو فاسقاً.
ونظيره: "المعاملات".

وأما الرابع: فيشترط فيه إما العدَدُ أو العدالة عند أبي حنيفة ونظيره : العَزْلُ والحَجْرُ.

فصل في حجية خبر الواحد
شه
خبره غير ملزم للصوم بل الملزم هو النص، وأجيب بأن المصنف محله فيه تابع شمس الأئمة السرخسي * والصحيح ذلك، فإن العدالة شرط في الشهادة بهلال رمضان وخبر الفاسق مقبول في النوع الثالث كما سيأتي كذا في "المعدن". وأما الثاني وهو ما كان خالص حق العبد ما فيه إلزام محض.
المنازعات كالبيوع والأشربة والأملاك المرسلة بأن ادعى أحد على آخر أنه باع هذا العبد أو اشترى ذلك، أو أن ألفاً عليه، فإنه يشترط فيه العدد والعدالة، والأولى بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا شَهيدين﴾ الآية، والثاني: بقوله عز اسمه: ﴿وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوَيْ عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ﴾، ولأن التزوير والتلبيس والحيل في الخصومات أكثر، فشرط زيادة العدد ولفظ الشهادة تقليلاً لها، وصيانة للحقوق المعصومة بقدر الوسع والإمكان ولأن المنازعة قائمة بين اثنين بخبرين متعارضين من الدعوى والإنكار، فلم يقع الفصل والرجحان بجنسه من الخبر بل بخبر ظهرت له مزية على غيره من يمين أو شهادة :أي: أقوال اثنين أو أكثر كذا في "المعدن".
فيقبل فيه خبَرُ إلخ: فإنه عليه السلام كان يقبل الهدية من العادل والفاسق بإخبارهما بأنها هدية؛ لأن الضرورة دعت إلى قبول خبر كل مميز، فإن الإنسان قلما يجد المجتمع بشرائط الشهادة كلها ولا دليل للسامع غير هذا الخبر، فتسقط الشرائط سوى التمييز للضرورة بخلاف خبره عليه السلام، فإنه لا ضرورة إلى قبول خبر الفاسق فمه؛ لكثرة الرواة العدول وحكم الله تعالى في تلك الحادثة يمكن معرفته بدليل آخر أي: القياس كذا في "المعدن". ونظيره : العزل والحجر أي: عزل الوكيل وحجر المأذون، فإن فيها إلزاماً من حيث أنه يلزمهما ألف ويبطل عملهما في المستقبل، وليس بإلزام من حيث أن الموكل والمولى يتصرف في حقه بالفسخ كما يتصرف في حقه بالتوكيل والإذن، فشرطنا فيهما العدد والعدالة؛ لكونهما بين المنزلتين كذا في "المعدن".
عن
التصرف
The second investigation: concerning the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah. -1- Pure right of Allah Almighty that is not a punishment. -2- Pure right of the slave that contains a pure binding (ilzam). -3- Pure right of the slave that contains no binding. -4- Pure right of the slave that contains binding from one aspect. Chapter on the authority of khabar al-wahid. As for the first, khabar al-wahid is accepted in it, for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of the Bedouin regarding the crescent of Ramadan. 'That is not a punishment': It is only restricted by that because what is a punishment from the rights of Allah Almighty is not accepted by khabar al-wahid according to al-Karkhi, and Fakhr al-Islam, Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, and likewise the author (al-Shashi) went to that; that is because the basis of hudud is on dropping due to doubts, so it is not permissible to establish them by khabar al-wahid just as it is not permissible by qiyas. As for establishing them by clear proofs (bayyinat), it is permissible by the text that necessitates knowledge, contrary to qiyas, and that is His saying: 'And call to witness...' (the verse), and consensus has been established on that. As for the first, which is pure right of Allah that is not a punishment, khabar al-wahid is accepted in it, etc. So like the general legislations such as prayer, fasting, wudu, 'ushr, and sadaqat al-fitr, khabar al-wahid is accepted in all of them according to the conditions we mentioned of Islam, justice, intellect, and retention according to the majority. Some scholars claimed that khabar al-wahid is not accepted because it is a proof with no strength, so it is permissible to act on it in what has no strength, which is the branch. And the majority holds that the purpose of acts of worship is action, whether original or branch, so it is obligatory to act on proofs that necessitate action. It is supported that he (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of the Bedouin regarding the crescent of Ramadan. This is from 'al-Fusul'. Khabar al-wahid: absolutely without condition of number nor specification of the word of testimony and trusteeship with freedom. [from 'Umdat al-Hawashi] 'For the Messenger of Allah etc.' because what is established by it is a pure right of Allah Almighty upon His slaves, which is fasting, where Allah the Exalted said: 'Fasting is prescribed for you' (the verse), and for this reason freedom was not required, and the word of testimony in it is contrary to the opinion of Fakhr al-Islam, where he mentioned in his 'Usul' that testimony for the crescent of Ramadan is of the third type, which is the pure right of the slave that has no binding; because a Bedouin came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: I saw the crescent. He said: Do you testify that there is no god but Allah? He said: Yes. He said: Do you testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah? He said: Yes. He said: 'O Bilal, announce to the people that they should fast tomorrow.' Reported by Abu Dawud in the chapter on the testimony of one person on seeing the crescent of Ramadan, no. 2340, and al-Nasa'i in the chapter on accepting the testimony of one man on the crescent of the month of Ramadan, no. 2113, and Ibn Majah in the chapter on what has come regarding testimony on seeing the crescent, no. 1652 from Ibn Abbas. As for the second, number and justice are required in it. Its parallel: 'disputes'. As for the third, khabar al-wahid is accepted in it whether the reporter is just or corrupt. Its parallel: 'transactions'. As for the fourth, either number or justice is required according to Abu Hanifa. Its parallel: 'dismissal and interdiction'. Chapter on the authority of khabar al-wahid. ... His report is not binding for the fast, rather the binding is the text. And it was answered that the author's position follows Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, and the correct is that, for justice is a condition in testimony for the crescent of Ramadan, and the report of a corrupt person is accepted in the third type as will come. This is from 'al-Ma'dan'. As for the second, which is the pure right of the slave that contains a pure binding. Disputes such as sales, drinks, and absolute properties, when one claims against another that he sold this slave or bought that, or that a thousand is owed by him, then number and justice are required. The first by His saying: 'And call to witness two witnesses' (the verse), and the second by His saying 'And call to witness two just persons from among you' (the verse). And because forgery, deception, and tricks are more in disputes, so the increase in number and the word of testimony were required to reduce them and to safeguard protected rights as much as possible. And because the dispute exists between two parties with two conflicting reports of claim and denial, so the decision and preponderance are not by the genus of the report but by a report that has an advantage over others from oath or testimony: i.e., statements of two or more. This is from 'al-Ma'dan'. 'So khabar al-wahid is accepted in it etc.' For he (peace be upon him) used to accept a gift from the just and the corrupt by their informing that it is a gift, because necessity called for accepting the report of every discerning person, for a person rarely finds someone who meets all the conditions of testimony, and the listener has no proof other than this report, so the conditions drop except discernment due to necessity, unlike his (peace be upon him) report, for there is no necessity to accept the report of a corrupt person because there are many upright narrators and the ruling of Allah regarding that incident can be known by another proof, i.e., analogy. This is from 'al-Ma'dan'. And its parallel: dismissal and interdiction, i.e., dismissal of an agent and interdiction of a permitted (slave/child), for in them there is binding in that it obligates them to something and makes their future actions invalid, but there is no binding in that the principal and guardian act in their right by revocation just as they act in their right by agency and permission. So we required number and justice in them because they are between the two statuses. This is from 'al-Ma'dan'. Regarding... the disposal...
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from al-Shashi's Usul presents a foundational classification in Hanafi jurisprudence: the division of rights (huquq) into four categories based on their nature (whether they belong purely to Allah, purely to the slave/human, or mixed) and whether they involve a binding obligation (ilzam). This classification determines the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid (a report from a single narrator) as evidence. The author first enumerates the four types: (1) pure right of Allah that is not a punishment (e.g., acts of worship like prayer, fasting, zakat), (2) pure right of the slave that contains a pure binding (e.g., claims in disputes involving property), (3) pure right of the slave that contains no binding (e.g., gifts and transactions), and (4) pure right of the slave that contains binding from one aspect (e.g., dismissal of an agent or interdiction). Then he applies the rule for khabar al-wahid: For type 1, khabar al-wahid is accepted with the conditions of Islam, justice, intellect, and retention according to the majority. There is a dispute regarding hudud (punishments) which are also pure rights of Allah but involve punishment; according to al-Karkhi, Fakhr al-Islam, al-Sarakhsi, and the author, khabar al-wahid is not accepted for hudud because they are established on a basis of dropping by doubts, and they require definitive proof. However, the acceptance of khabar al-wahid for non-punitive rights of Allah is supported by the Prophet's acceptance of a single Bedouin's testimony regarding the sighting of the crescent of Ramadan. For type 2, number (two witnesses) and justice are required, as in disputes over property, based on Quranic verses. For type 3, khabar al-wahid is accepted even from a corrupt person due to necessity, as in accepting gifts. For type 4, either number or justice is required according to Abu Hanifa, as in cases of dismissal or interdiction where there is binding from one aspect. The passage also includes a discussion of a different opinion regarding the crescent testimony, classifying it as type 3 (right of slave with no binding) by Fakhr al-Islam, but the author follows al-Sarakhsi, maintaining that justice is still required for the crescent testimony. The key point is that the evidentiary value of a single report varies according to the nature of the right involved.

Key Terms
خالص حق الله (khalis haqq Allah): A right that belongs purely to Allah with no share for the slave, such as acts of worship.
خالص حق العبد (khalis haqq al-'abd): A right that belongs purely to the slave (human) with no share for Allah, such as property claims.
إلزام (ilzam): A binding obligation that compels the person to act or forbear.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by a single narrator that does not reach the level of tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following correctly describes 'خالص حق العبد ما فيه إلزام محض'?
A) Right of the slave with no binding
B) Right of the slave with pure binding
C) Right of Allah with punishment
D) Right of Allah without punishment

Key Takeaway
The fourfold classification of rights (huquq) determines the evidentiary rigor required for accepting a single reporter's testimony.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Conditions for Accepting Khabar al-Wahid by Type of Right
Applies acceptance conditions for khabar al-wahid to each type of right.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the correct conditions (number, justice, etc.) for accepting khabar al-wahid in each of the four categories, and explain the exception for hudud.

Core Idea
Khabar al-wahid is accepted in all but hudud; required conditions vary: number+justice for binding disputes, none for non-binding transactions, and either number or justice for mixed-binding.

Once the four categories of rights are understood, the next step is to apply the evidentiary rules for accepting a single narrator's report (khabar al-wahid). This passage details the specific conditions—whether number, justice, or both are required—for each category. It also addresses a crucial exception: punishments (hudud) that are pure rights of Allah are not established by khabar al-wahid due to the principle of dropping doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories and their acceptance rule
For each type, what is required: number, justice, both, or none? Review the text's explicit statements.
2
Note the exception for hudud
Pure rights of Allah that are punishments are excluded from acceptance of khabar al-wahid because hudud require certainty.
3
Understand the rationale for each rule
Why does necessity allow corrupt narrators for transactions? Why do disputes require more? The text provides reasons.
4
Apply to the crescent testimony case
See how the authors differ on the classification of the Bedouin's report and the implications for conditions.
5
Synthesize the overall pattern
The stricter the binding, the stricter the evidence. Pure ilzam requires number+justice; no ilzam requires none; ilzam min wajh requires either number or justice.

البحث الثاني في سنة رسول الله
-۱- خالص حق الله تعالى ما ليس بعقوبة.
-٢- وخالص حق العبد ما فيه إلزام محض.
-٣- وخالص حقه ما ليس فيه إلزام.
٤- وخالص حقه ما فيه إلزام من وجه.

فصل في حجية خبر الواحد
أما الأول فيقبل فيه خبر الواحد، فإن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل شهادة الأعرابي في هلال رَمَضَان.
ما ليس بعقوبة: وإنما قيد به؛ لأن ما هو عقوبة من حقوق الله تعالى لا يقبل فيه خبر الواحد عند الكرخي، وإليه ذهب فخر الإسلام، وشمس الأئمة السرخسي، وكذا الماتن له؛ وذلك لأن مبنى الحدود على الإسقاط بالشبهات، فلا يجوز إثباتها بخبر الواحد كما لا يجوز بالقياس، وأما إثباتها بالبينات فيجوز بالنص الموجب للعلم على خلاف القياس، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا﴾ الآية، وقد انعقد الإجماع على ذلك. أما الأول وهو ما كان خالص حق الله ما ليس بعقوبة. فيقبل فيه خبر الواحد إلخ فمثل عامة الشرائع من الصلاة والصوم، والوضوء والعشر، وصدقة الفطر يقبل في كلها خبر الواحد على ما قلنا من شرائطه من الإسلام والعدالة والعقل والضبط عند الجماهير، وزعم بعض العلماء أنه لا يقبل خبر الواحد دليل لا قوة فيه، فجاز أن يعمل فيما ليس فيه قوة وهو الفرع، وللجمهور أن المقصود من العبادات هو العمل أصلاً كانت أو فرعاً، فيجب العمل فيها بالدلائل الموجبة للعمل، ويؤيده أنه عليه قبل شهادة الأعرابي في هلال رمضان كذا في "الفصول". خبر الواحد: مطلقاً من غير اشتراط عدد ولا تعيين لفظ الشهادة والولاية بالحرية. [عمدة الحواشي: ص فإن رسول الله إلخ لأن الثابت بها حق الله تعالى على عباده خالصاً وهو الصوم، حيث قال الله جل شأنه: ﴿كُتِبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الصِّيَامُ﴾ الآية، ولهذا لم تشترط فيه الحرية، ولفظ الشهادة فيه مخالف لمرضي فخر الإسلام، حيث ذكر في "أصوله" : أن الشهادة بهلال رمضان من النوع الثالث، وهو خالص حق العبد ما ليس فيه إلزام؛ لأنه جاء أعرابي إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : إني رأيت الهلال، فقال: أتشهد أن لا إله إلا الله؟ قال: نعم، قال: أتشهد أن محمداً رسول الله؟ قال: نعم، قال: "يا بلال أذن في الناس فليصوموا غداً". أخرجه أبو داود في باب في شهادة الواحد على رؤية هلال رمضان، رقم: ٢٣٤٠، والنسائي في باب قبول شهادة الرجل الواحد على هلال شهر رمضان، رقم: ۲۱۱۳، وابن ماجه في باب ما جاء في الشهادة على رؤية الهلال رقم ١٦٥٢ عن ابن عباس.

وأما الثاني: فيشترط فيه العدد والعدالة.
ونظيره: "المنازعات".

وأما الثالث: فيقبَلُ فيه خبَرُ الواحد عدلاً كان أو فاسقاً.
ونظيره: "المعاملات".

وأما الرابع: فيشترط فيه إما العدَدُ أو العدالة عند أبي حنيفة ونظيره : العَزْلُ والحَجْرُ.

فصل في حجية خبر الواحد
شه
خبره غير ملزم للصوم بل الملزم هو النص، وأجيب بأن المصنف محله فيه تابع شمس الأئمة السرخسي * والصحيح ذلك، فإن العدالة شرط في الشهادة بهلال رمضان وخبر الفاسق مقبول في النوع الثالث كما سيأتي كذا في "المعدن". وأما الثاني وهو ما كان خالص حق العبد ما فيه إلزام محض.
المنازعات كالبيوع والأشربة والأملاك المرسلة بأن ادعى أحد على آخر أنه باع هذا العبد أو اشترى ذلك، أو أن ألفاً عليه، فإنه يشترط فيه العدد والعدالة، والأولى بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُوا شَهيدين﴾ الآية، والثاني: بقوله عز اسمه: ﴿وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوَيْ عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ﴾، ولأن التزوير والتلبيس والحيل في الخصومات أكثر، فشرط زيادة العدد ولفظ الشهادة تقليلاً لها، وصيانة للحقوق المعصومة بقدر الوسع والإمكان ولأن المنازعة قائمة بين اثنين بخبرين متعارضين من الدعوى والإنكار، فلم يقع الفصل والرجحان بجنسه من الخبر بل بخبر ظهرت له مزية على غيره من يمين أو شهادة :أي: أقوال اثنين أو أكثر كذا في "المعدن".
فيقبل فيه خبَرُ إلخ: فإنه عليه السلام كان يقبل الهدية من العادل والفاسق بإخبارهما بأنها هدية؛ لأن الضرورة دعت إلى قبول خبر كل مميز، فإن الإنسان قلما يجد المجتمع بشرائط الشهادة كلها ولا دليل للسامع غير هذا الخبر، فتسقط الشرائط سوى التمييز للضرورة بخلاف خبره عليه السلام، فإنه لا ضرورة إلى قبول خبر الفاسق فمه؛ لكثرة الرواة العدول وحكم الله تعالى في تلك الحادثة يمكن معرفته بدليل آخر أي: القياس كذا في "المعدن". ونظيره : العزل والحجر أي: عزل الوكيل وحجر المأذون، فإن فيها إلزاماً من حيث أنه يلزمهما ألف ويبطل عملهما في المستقبل، وليس بإلزام من حيث أن الموكل والمولى يتصرف في حقه بالفسخ كما يتصرف في حقه بالتوكيل والإذن، فشرطنا فيهما العدد والعدالة؛ لكونهما بين المنزلتين كذا في "المعدن".
عن
التصرف
The second investigation: concerning the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah. -1- Pure right of Allah Almighty that is not a punishment. -2- Pure right of the slave that contains a pure binding (ilzam). -3- Pure right of the slave that contains no binding. -4- Pure right of the slave that contains binding from one aspect. Chapter on the authority of khabar al-wahid. As for the first, khabar al-wahid is accepted in it, for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of the Bedouin regarding the crescent of Ramadan. 'That is not a punishment': It is only restricted by that because what is a punishment from the rights of Allah Almighty is not accepted by khabar al-wahid according to al-Karkhi, and Fakhr al-Islam, Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, and likewise the author (al-Shashi) went to that; that is because the basis of hudud is on dropping due to doubts, so it is not permissible to establish them by khabar al-wahid just as it is not permissible by qiyas. As for establishing them by clear proofs (bayyinat), it is permissible by the text that necessitates knowledge, contrary to qiyas, and that is His saying: 'And call to witness...' (the verse), and consensus has been established on that. As for the first, which is pure right of Allah that is not a punishment, khabar al-wahid is accepted in it, etc. So like the general legislations such as prayer, fasting, wudu, 'ushr, and sadaqat al-fitr, khabar al-wahid is accepted in all of them according to the conditions we mentioned of Islam, justice, intellect, and retention according to the majority. Some scholars claimed that khabar al-wahid is not accepted because it is a proof with no strength, so it is permissible to act on it in what has no strength, which is the branch. And the majority holds that the purpose of acts of worship is action, whether original or branch, so it is obligatory to act on proofs that necessitate action. It is supported that he (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of the Bedouin regarding the crescent of Ramadan. This is from 'al-Fusul'. Khabar al-wahid: absolutely without condition of number nor specification of the word of testimony and trusteeship with freedom. [from 'Umdat al-Hawashi] 'For the Messenger of Allah etc.' because what is established by it is a pure right of Allah Almighty upon His slaves, which is fasting, where Allah the Exalted said: 'Fasting is prescribed for you' (the verse), and for this reason freedom was not required, and the word of testimony in it is contrary to the opinion of Fakhr al-Islam, where he mentioned in his 'Usul' that testimony for the crescent of Ramadan is of the third type, which is the pure right of the slave that has no binding; because a Bedouin came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: I saw the crescent. He said: Do you testify that there is no god but Allah? He said: Yes. He said: Do you testify that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah? He said: Yes. He said: 'O Bilal, announce to the people that they should fast tomorrow.' Reported by Abu Dawud in the chapter on the testimony of one person on seeing the crescent of Ramadan, no. 2340, and al-Nasa'i in the chapter on accepting the testimony of one man on the crescent of the month of Ramadan, no. 2113, and Ibn Majah in the chapter on what has come regarding testimony on seeing the crescent, no. 1652 from Ibn Abbas. As for the second, number and justice are required in it. Its parallel: 'disputes'. As for the third, khabar al-wahid is accepted in it whether the reporter is just or corrupt. Its parallel: 'transactions'. As for the fourth, either number or justice is required according to Abu Hanifa. Its parallel: 'dismissal and interdiction'. Chapter on the authority of khabar al-wahid. ... His report is not binding for the fast, rather the binding is the text. And it was answered that the author's position follows Shams al-A'immah al-Sarakhsi, and the correct is that, for justice is a condition in testimony for the crescent of Ramadan, and the report of a corrupt person is accepted in the third type as will come. This is from 'al-Ma'dan'. As for the second, which is the pure right of the slave that contains a pure binding. Disputes such as sales, drinks, and absolute properties, when one claims against another that he sold this slave or bought that, or that a thousand is owed by him, then number and justice are required. The first by His saying: 'And call to witness two witnesses' (the verse), and the second by His saying 'And call to witness two just persons from among you' (the verse). And because forgery, deception, and tricks are more in disputes, so the increase in number and the word of testimony were required to reduce them and to safeguard protected rights as much as possible. And because the dispute exists between two parties with two conflicting reports of claim and denial, so the decision and preponderance are not by the genus of the report but by a report that has an advantage over others from oath or testimony: i.e., statements of two or more. This is from 'al-Ma'dan'. 'So khabar al-wahid is accepted in it etc.' For he (peace be upon him) used to accept a gift from the just and the corrupt by their informing that it is a gift, because necessity called for accepting the report of every discerning person, for a person rarely finds someone who meets all the conditions of testimony, and the listener has no proof other than this report, so the conditions drop except discernment due to necessity, unlike his (peace be upon him) report, for there is no necessity to accept the report of a corrupt person because there are many upright narrators and the ruling of Allah regarding that incident can be known by another proof, i.e., analogy. This is from 'al-Ma'dan'. And its parallel: dismissal and interdiction, i.e., dismissal of an agent and interdiction of a permitted (slave/child), for in them there is binding in that it obligates them to something and makes their future actions invalid, but there is no binding in that the principal and guardian act in their right by revocation just as they act in their right by agency and permission. So we required number and justice in them because they are between the two statuses. This is from 'al-Ma'dan'. Regarding... the disposal...
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from al-Shashi's Usul presents a foundational classification in Hanafi jurisprudence: the division of rights (huquq) into four categories based on their nature (whether they belong purely to Allah, purely to the slave/human, or mixed) and whether they involve a binding obligation (ilzam). This classification determines the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid (a report from a single narrator) as evidence. The author first enumerates the four types: (1) pure right of Allah that is not a punishment (e.g., acts of worship like prayer, fasting, zakat), (2) pure right of the slave that contains a pure binding (e.g., claims in disputes involving property), (3) pure right of the slave that contains no binding (e.g., gifts and transactions), and (4) pure right of the slave that contains binding from one aspect (e.g., dismissal of an agent or interdiction). Then he applies the rule for khabar al-wahid: For type 1, khabar al-wahid is accepted with the conditions of Islam, justice, intellect, and retention according to the majority. There is a dispute regarding hudud (punishments) which are also pure rights of Allah but involve punishment; according to al-Karkhi, Fakhr al-Islam, al-Sarakhsi, and the author, khabar al-wahid is not accepted for hudud because they are established on a basis of dropping by doubts, and they require definitive proof. However, the acceptance of khabar al-wahid for non-punitive rights of Allah is supported by the Prophet's acceptance of a single Bedouin's testimony regarding the sighting of the crescent of Ramadan. For type 2, number (two witnesses) and justice are required, as in disputes over property, based on Quranic verses. For type 3, khabar al-wahid is accepted even from a corrupt person due to necessity, as in accepting gifts. For type 4, either number or justice is required according to Abu Hanifa, as in cases of dismissal or interdiction where there is binding from one aspect. The passage also includes a discussion of a different opinion regarding the crescent testimony, classifying it as type 3 (right of slave with no binding) by Fakhr al-Islam, but the author follows al-Sarakhsi, maintaining that justice is still required for the crescent testimony. The key point is that the evidentiary value of a single report varies according to the nature of the right involved.

Key Terms
خالص حق الله (khalis haqq Allah): A right that belongs purely to Allah with no share for the slave, such as acts of worship.
خالص حق العبد (khalis haqq al-'abd): A right that belongs purely to the slave (human) with no share for Allah, such as property claims.
إلزام (ilzam): A binding obligation that compels the person to act or forbear.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report transmitted by a single narrator that does not reach the level of tawatur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the basis for not accepting khabar al-wahid in hudud?
A) Hudud are not part of sharia
B) Hudud require certainty, and khabar al-wahid is zanni
C) The Quran forbids using khabar al-wahid in hudud
D) Hudud can be established by qiyas

Key Takeaway
The conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid vary by type of right and the presence of binding or punishment.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Strength of Shubha: Locus vs. Opinion
Compares shubha in locus vs. opinion using father/son slave-girl example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shubha fi al-mahal (locus) and shubha fi al-zann (opinion) and apply the Hanafi rule that shubha fi al-mahal drops the hadd penalty regardless of the actor's belief.

Core Idea
Shubha in the locus is stronger; a textual basis overrides personal belief.

In Hanafi penal law, not all doubts are equal. Some arise from the act itself due to a textual indication (shubha in the locus), while others stem from the individual's mistaken opinion (shubha in opinion). This passage from Usul al-Shashi explains why the first type is sufficient to drop the hadd penalty, even if the actor believed the act was forbidden. The example of a father with his son's slave-girl illustrates the principle.

Guided Path
1
Define shubha and its two types
From the passage, identify the two categories: shubha fi al-mahal (shubhat al-fi'l/al-ishtibah) and shubha fi al-zann (shubhat al-dalil/al-hukmiyyah). Note their definitions.
Shubha fi al-mahal arises from a textual source, while shubha fi al-zann is based on personal opinion.
2
Analyze the hadith proof
Examine the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father' (أنت ومالك لأبيك). Understand how this creates a semblance of ownership without actual ownership, generating shubha in the locus.
The hadith is zanni in transmission and indication, but sufficient for shubha.
3
Apply to the father's case
Apply the hadith: The father's intercourse with his son's slave-girl is not punished by hadd because the shubha of ownership exists in the act itself, regardless of his personal belief of prohibition.
The text says even if he said 'I knew it was forbidden,' the hadd is dropped.
4
Contrast with shubha in opinion
Consider the second example where both a man and a woman claim shubha. The woman's shubha is in the locus (she thought it permissible due to a text?), but the man's shubha is also considered. Understand that when both exist, the textual one dominates.
The text says if the woman claims she thought it halal, her hadd drops, and the man's drops due to partnership.
5
State the Hanafi rule
Conclude: Shubha fi al-mahal is stronger and drops hadd even if the actor believed the act was haram. The effective factor is the legal proof, not the actor's opinion.
This is the key takeaway for usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى اعتبار أن العمل بالرأي دون العمل بالنص قلنا: إن الشبهة بالمحل أقوى من الشبهة في الظن حتى سَقَطَ اعتبار ظنّ العبد في الفصل الأول.
لاستناده إلى الرأي والظن وهو الشبه في المحل
ومثاله: فيما إذا وطئ جارية ابنه لا يُحَدِّ، وإن قال: علمت أنها على حرام، ويثبت نَسَبُ الولد منه؛ لأن شبهة الملك لا تثبتُ بالنص في مال الابن قال علي: "أنت ومالكَ لأبيك" * فسقط اعتبار ظنه في الحل والحرمة في ذلك.
أن الأب قد
إن الشبهة بالمحل إلخ أي بالفعل، وتسمى شبهة الاشتبهاه؛ لأنها كانت نشأت من الظن فيكون لها ثلاثة أسماء: شبهة الاشتباه، وشبهة الفعل، وشبهة الظن.
اعلم أن الشبهة ما يشبه الثابت أي: الحق وليس بثابت وهي تكون شبهة بالفعل وتسمى شبهة اشتبهاه وهي المرادة بالشبهة في الظن، وذلك أن يظن الإنسان ما ليس بدليل الحل والحرمة دليلا في كل واحد منهما، وقد تكون شبهة في الحل وتسمى شبهة الدليل والشبهة الحكمية، وهي يوجد الدليل الشرعي النافي للحل والحرمة مع تخلف حكمه لمانع اتصل به فیورث هذا الدليل شبهة في حل ما ليس بحلال أو عكسه وهذا النوع من الشبهة لا يتوقف تحققه على ظن الجاني واعتقاده، بخلاف القسم الأول، فإذا تحقق كلاهما :أي كلا الشبهتان، فلابد من أن يكون القسم الثاني من الشبهة في المحل لنشوه عن النص أقوى من الأول؛ لاستناده إلى الرأي والظن، ولهذا كان الحد ساقطاً لشبهة المحل وإن كان على خلاف ظنه كذا في 'المعدن'. في الظن لاستناده إلى الرأي والظن.
فتدبر
ومثاله : أي مثال ما كانت الشبهة في المحل وفي الظن، ومثال سقوط ظن العبد فيما إذا كانت الشبهة في وعدم سقوط ظنه فيما إذا كانت الشبهة في الظن كذا في 'المعدن'. أنها عليّ حرامٌ أي إذا قال الرجل: إنها علي حرام، وقالت جارية الابن ظننت أنه يحل لي لا يحد واحد منهما ، أما المرأة؛ فلدعوى الشبهة، وأما الرجل؛ فلأن الزنا يقوم بهما، فإذا سقط الحد عن المرأة سقط عن الرجل مكان الشركة.
لأبيك: فإن اللام للملك، فظاهر الحديث يدل على أن للأب حق التملك في مال ولده إلا أن حقيقة ثبوت الملك له ساقط بالإجماع و بالنصوص، فتصير شبهة دائرة وإن ظن الحرمة؛ لأن المؤثر في الإسقاط هو الدليل الشرعي، وذلك لا يتفاوت بين معتقد الحل والحرمة كذا في 'المعدن'.
* أخرجه أبو داود رقم: ٣٥٣٠ ، باب في الرجل يأكل من مال ولده وابن ماجه باب ما للرجل من مال ولده، رقم: ۲۲۹۲ عن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده.
And upon the consideration that acting by opinion without acting by text, we said: Indeed, shubha (doubt) arising from the locus (mahal) is stronger than shubha in the opinion (zann), to the extent that the consideration of the slave's opinion in the first case falls away. Because it is based on opinion and conjecture, and it is shubha in the locus. Its example: When a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl, he is not subjected to the hadd penalty, even if he said: 'I knew it was forbidden.' And the lineage of the child is established from him, because the shubha of ownership does not become established by a text concerning the son's property. 'Ali said: 'You and your property belong to your father.' So the consideration of his opinion regarding permissibility and prohibition in that matter fell away. That the father... Indeed, shubha in the locus, etc., meaning in the act, and it is called shubha of confusion (shubhat al-ishtibah), because it arose from opinion. Thus it has three names: shubha of confusion, shubha of the act, and shubha of opinion. Know that shubha is what resembles the established (i.e., truth) but is not established. It may be shubha in the act, called shubha of confusion, which is intended by shubha in the opinion, such that a person thinks something that is not a proof of permissibility or prohibition to be a proof in each of them. And it may be shubha in the ruling, called shubha of the proof and shubha of the legal ruling, which is where there exists a legal proof negating permissibility or prohibition but its ruling is delayed due to a connected impediment, so this proof gives rise to a shubha in the permissibility of what is not permissible or vice versa. This type of shubha does not depend for its realization on the criminal's opinion and belief, unlike the first type. So when both types are realized (i.e., both shubhas), then necessarily the second type, which is shubha in the locus because it arises from the text, is stronger than the first, because it is based on opinion and conjecture. For this reason, the hadd penalty is dropped due to shubha in the locus, even if it was contrary to his opinion. Thus in al-Ma'din. ... Reflect. And its example: an example of where there is shubha in the locus and in the opinion, and an example of the fall of the slave's opinion when the shubha is in the locus and the non-fall of his opinion when the shubha is in the opinion, as in al-Ma'din. 'She is forbidden to me' – meaning if a man says: 'She is forbidden to me,' and the son's slave-girl says: 'I thought it was permissible for me,' then neither is subjected to the hadd penalty. As for the woman, due to her claim of shubha; as for the man, because zina is committed by both partners, so if the hadd falls from the woman, it falls from the man as well due to partnership. 'To your father' – the lam here indicates ownership, so the apparent meaning of the hadith indicates that the father has the right of ownership over his son's property, except that the actual establishment of ownership is not valid by consensus and by texts, so a shubha persists. Even if he thought it forbidden, because the effective factor in dropping the penalty is the legal proof, which does not vary between the one who believes it permissible or forbidden. Thus in al-Ma'din. *Narrated by Abu Dawud no. 3530, chapter on a man eating from his son's wealth; Ibn Majah no. 2292, chapter on what a man may have from his son's wealth, from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the Hanafi theory of shubha (legal doubt) in penal law. It distinguishes two types: shubha in the act/locus (shubhat fi al-mahal) and shubha in the opinion (shubha fi al-zann). The first arises from a legitimate textual indication (like a hadith or general principle) that creates a semblance of legality, even if the act is actually unlawful. The second is merely the actor's personal mistaken belief. The author rules that the first type is stronger and is sufficient to drop the hadd penalty, even if the actor believed the act was forbidden. The example: a father who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl. Even if he knew it was forbidden, the hadd is not applied because of the shubha of ownership derived from the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father.' This hadith, though not establishing actual ownership, creates a doubt (shubha) in the locus (the act). The text also provides a second example where both a man and a woman claim shubha, and the hadd is dropped for both due to partnership. The commentary emphasizes that the drop of penalty is due to the presence of a textual basis, not the individual's belief.

Key Terms
الشبهة (al-shubha): A legal doubt that resembles the truth but is not actually true; it prevents the application of corporal punishments.
الشبهة في المحل (shubhat fi al-mahal): Shubha arising from the act itself due to a textual indication that suggests legality, even if the act is actually unlawful.
الشبهة في الظن (shubhat fi al-zann): Shubha based on the actor's personal mistaken opinion, lacking a textual basis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the father with his son's slave-girl, why is the hadd penalty not applied, even though the father knew it was forbidden?
A) Because the father did not actually commit adultery.
B) Because the son's slave-girl consented.
C) Because the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father' creates a shubha in the act (locus).
D) Because the father's belief of forbiddance nullified the penalty.

Key Takeaway
Shubha fi al-mahal, grounded in a textual source, is stronger than shubha fi al-zann and drops hadd regardless of the actor's belief.

The Binding Effect of Taharri: Confirmed by Action, Not Reversed by Subsequent Ijtihad
Explains rule that first taharri is confirmed by action and cannot be invalidated by a second

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that a ruling established by valid ijtihad and acted upon cannot be invalidated by a subsequent contrary ijtihad, and distinguish between cases where the subject matter admits of transfer (like qibla) and where it does not (like garment purity).

Core Idea
A ruling confirmed by action is binding; only if the subject matter is mutable can a second ijtihad replace it like naskh.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi lays out a key Hanafi principle: once a mujtahid performs an act based on his best judgment (taharri), that act is legally valid and cannot be undone by a later change of mind. However, this rule has an exception when the subject of the ruling is something that can change over time, such as the direction of prayer (qibla). Understanding this distinction is essential for correct ijtihad and fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: the case of two garments (where one is prayed in after taharri) and the case of qibla direction (where one prays facing one direction after taharri).
The garment case is the default; the qibla case is the exception.
2
Extract the ruling for each scenario
For the garments, the first taharri is confirmed by action, so the second taharri cannot be used for Asr. For qibla, if taharri later indicates a different direction, the prayer can be performed facing the new direction.
The ruling for qibla is that the second opinion is permissible, like naskh.
3
Locate the distinguishing factor
The difference is whether the subject matter admits of transfer (intiqal) or not. The garment's purity status is fixed; the qibla direction can change (as it did from Bayt al-Maqdis to Kaaba).
Intiqal is the key concept: if transfer is possible, a second ijtihad can override the first.
4
State the principle
A ruling established by valid ijtihad and acted upon is binding and cannot be invalidated by a later ijtihad, unless the subject matter is mutable, in which case the second ijtihad is treated like naskh.
This principle ensures stability in rulings while allowing for change where the Shariah itself allows it.

Source Text

التحري بأداء الصلاة فيه
وهذا بخلاف ما إذا تَحرَّى في القبلة ثم تبدَّل رأيه، ووَقَعَ تحريه على جهة أخرى توجه إليه؛ لأن القبلةَ مما يحتمل الانتقال فأمكن نقل الحكم بمنزلة نسخ النص، وعلى هذا مسائل "الجامع الكبير" في تكبيرات العيد وتبدل رأي العيد كما عُرف.

وهذا بخلاف إلخ: جواب سوال مقدر وهو أن المصلي لو تحرى عند اشتباه القبلة وصلى إلى جهة ثم تبدل رأيه ووقع تحريه على جهة أخرى، فإنه يصلي في المستقبل إلى هذه الجهة، وهذا يخالف ما ذكرنا من أنه إذا تحرى وتأكد تحريه بالعمل لا ينتقض بمجرد الرأي فتدبر.

مما يحتمل الانتقال: من جهة إلى جهة حتى انتقل من بيت المقدس إلى الكعبة الشريفة، ومن عين الكعبة إلى جهتها في حق الغائب عن الكعبة فاحتملت نقل الحكم والتحول بالتحري الثاني أيضاً، وكلامنها فيما لا يحتمله كمسألة الثوب، فإن النجاسة متى انحلت في الثوب لا يحتمل الانتقال إلى محل آخر. مسائل الجامع الكبير" وهي المسائل التي ذكرها الإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني محله في باب صلاة العيدين. Chapter on explaining the duty of the mujtahid. The third research on consensus and its explanation: Regarding when one investigates between two garments and prays Zuhr with one of them, then his investigation at Asr time falls on the other garment, it is not permissible for him to pray Asr with the other; because the first (garment) became confirmed by action, so it is not invalidated by mere investigation. And for this reason, i.e., because when the first is confirmed by action, it is not abrogated by the second. We say: When a ruling has passed by ijtihad, then another ijtihad appears that contradicts it, the first is not abrogated by it. As in al-Fusul. Because the qibla etc.: This is a start in explaining the difference between the garment issue and the Kaaba. And the summary of the explanation: That in what does not admit of transfer and succession, if action according to ijtihad in the future contrary to the first were allowed, it would lead to validating every qiyas; because we have shown that when he investigates and acts and makes investigation a proof necessarily, the action becomes correct and true. So if we allow action with the other, that would also be correct, and the other investigation is a proof, and in it is permitting multiplicity of truths, which is invalid. Unlike what admits of transfer and succession, because if action with the other were allowed in it, that would be like a ruling of abrogation to the other ruling, and each of them would be correct and true, and there is no multiplicity of truths because the first has become abrogated. As in al-Fusul. What admits of transfer: from one direction to another, as it transferred from Bayt al-Maqdis to the noble Kaaba, and from the very Kaaba to its direction for the one absent from the Kaaba. So it admitted the transfer of ruling and transformation by the second investigation as well. And each of them is in what does not admit of it, like the garment issue, because when impurity is removed from the garment, it does not admit of transfer to another place. Issues of al-Jami' al-Kabir: these are the issues that Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani mentioned in their place in the chapter of Eid prayer. [al-Shafi: p. 249]
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul principle that once a ruling is established by valid ijtihad (taharri) and acted upon, it cannot be overridden by a subsequent contrary ijtihad. It compares two cases: the case of two garments (where the impurity is fixed) and the case of qibla (which admits of change). The key distinction is whether the subject matter admits of transfer (intiqal) or not. For mutable matters like qibla, a second ijtihad can replace the first like naskh, but for immutable matters like a specific garment that was determined pure, the first ijtihad is confirmed and cannot be undone. This is the Hanafi position based on the principle that a ruling that has been acted upon is established as correct. The passage also references the issue of Eid takbirs from al-Jami' al-Kabir, where a change of opinion among the Sahaba is treated as permissible for future acts but does not invalidate past acts. All examples follow Hanafi usul methodology.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharri): Effort to determine the correct ruling or object when the original is uncertain, e.g., choosing between two suspected garments or discerning qibla direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the first action was performed and the garment's status is fixed by the act.
C) Because the qibla does not change.
D) Because the mujtahid is not allowed to change his mind.

Key Takeaway
The first valid ijtihad acted upon is binding and cannot be overturned by a later ijtihad, except when the subject matter admits of transfer like qibla.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Cause, Effective Reason, and Condition of the Ruling
Definition of core uṣūl terms and critique of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sabab, illa, and shart, and apply the concepts of naqḍ and mu‘āraḍah to evaluate a qiyas argument.

Core Idea
The ruling is attached by its cause, established by its effective reason, and found when its condition is present.

This short but dense chapter from al-Shāshī’s Uṣūl lays the foundation for understanding how rulings (aḥkām) are linked to their occasions (asbāb), intrinsic reasons (ilal), and prerequisites (shurūṭ). It also introduces two critical objections used in qiyas debates: naqḍ (contradiction) and mu‘āraḍah (counterargument). Mastering these distinctions is essential for correctly deriving and defending rulings within the Hanafī tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three key terms
From the opening sentence, extract the definitions of sabab, illa, and shart. Note how the ruling relates to each: attachment (ta‘alluq) to sabab, establishment (thubūt) by illa, and existence (wujūd) at shart.
These three relationships are the backbone of uṣūl al-fiqh for connecting rulings to their bases.
2
Differentiate sabab from illa
Sabab is the extrinsic occasion (e.g., entry of prayer time for prayer obligation), while illa is the intrinsic attribute that justifies the ruling (e.g., intoxication for wine prohibition). Understand how they work together.
The Hanafī school strictly distinguishes these, unlike some other schools.
3
Understand naqḍ (contradiction) as a qiyas objection
Naqḍ occurs when the claimed illa exists but the ruling is absent. The text uses the example: wuḍū’ is purification (illa) requiring intention, but washing a garment is also purification without intention – this is a naqḍ of the illa. Analyze the Hanafī response redefining the illa as ‘legal purification’.
Hanafīs accept naqḍ only if no preventer (māni‘) exists.
4
Distinguish mu‘āraḍah from naqḍ
Mu‘āraḍah is when the opponent brings an independent proof that contradicts the ruling outright, rather than exposing an inconsistency in the illa. Recognize the difference: naqḍ attacks the illa, mu‘āraḍah attacks the ruling via a separate dalīl.
The text contrasts tanāquḍ (contradiction invalidating the proof) with ta‘āruḍ (conflict preventing establishment).
5
Apply the concepts to the wuḍū’ example
Trace the full Hanafī argument: The Shāfi‘ī claimant says wuḍū’ requires intention because it is purification (like tayammum). The Hanafī responds by naqḍ: washing a garment is purification without intention. Then the illa is refined to ‘legal purification’ (ṭahārah ḥukmiyyah), which is not rationally discernible and thus requires intention. Notice how this defends the Hanafī position.
This example illustrates how naqḍ leads to refinement of the illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في سبب الحكم وعلته وشرطه:
الحكم يُتعلق بسببه، ويثبت بعلته، ويوجد عند شرطه.
الحكم
وأما النقض: فهو وجود العلة وتخلف الحكم عنه سواء كان لمانع أو لغيره عند من لم يجوز التخصيص أي: تخصيص العلة، فالتخصيص مناقضة عندهم، وعند من جوزه هو تخلف الحكم عما ادعاه المعلل علة لا لمنانع، مثاله: ما يقال: الوضوء طهارة فيشترط فيه النية كالتيمم والجامع أن كلاً منهما عبادة ولا عبادة بدون النية، قلنا: ينقض بغسل الثوب والإناء لوجود العلة وهي الطهارة مع تخلف الحكم وهو اشتراط النية؛ لأنه لم يشترط النية فيهما فتدبر كذا قيل ما يقال إلخ القائلون هم أهل الطرد من الشافعية. [الشافي: ص ۲۸۲] قلنا : فعاد المعلل فارقاً بتغيير العلة إلى أن العلة ليست ما فهمتم حتى تقولوا: يلزم تخلف الحكم عن علة في طهارة الثوب، بل العلة عندنا هو الطهارة الحكمية وهي غير معقولة، فيحتاج فيها إلى النية، وأجاب عنه الحنفية بأن تنجس البدن بخروج النجاسة أمر معقول نعم الاقتصاء على الأعضاء الأربعة مع وجوب تطهير البدن كله غير معقول قد جوز لدفع الحرج، فإذا تنجس البدن والماء مطهر لطبيعة المطهر شرعاً أيضاً، فيتطهر به ويزيل النجاسة بلا حاجة إلى النية بخلاف التيمم، فإن التراب ملوث لا مطهر. وأمّا المعارَضَةُ : [الفرق بين التعارض والمتعارض أن التناقض يوجب بطلان نفس الدليل، والتعارض يمنع ثبوت الحكم من غير أن يتعرض الدليل] وهي أن يأتي السائل بدليل آخر ينفي حكم دليل المعلل بأن يقول للمعلل: ما ذكرت من الدليل وإن دل على الحكم، لكن عندنا من الدليل ما ينفيه. [حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ٢٤٤] الحكم إلخ لما تم البحث من دلائل الشرع وهو الأصول الأربعة، فاعلم أن ما ثبت بهذه الدلائل من الأحكام يتعلق بأسبابها وشروطها وعللها، فلابد من بيانها، وهذا الفصل لبيان ذلك، فإن الحكم يتعلق بسببه؛ لأنه يفضي -
Chapter on the cause (sabab) of the ruling, its effective reason (illa), and its condition (shart). The ruling is attached to its cause, established by its effective reason, and found when its condition is present. As for al-naqḍ (contradiction), it is the existence of the effective reason but with the ruling absent from it, either due to a preventer or otherwise, according to those who do not allow takhsīṣ (specification) of the illa. So takhsīṣ is a contradiction in their view. According to those who allow it, it is the absence of the ruling from what the mu‘allil claimed as an illa without a preventer. Example: It is said: Wuḍū’ is purification, so intention is necessary for it, like tayammum, and the common link is that both are acts of worship and no worship is valid without intention. We said: This is contradicted (yanquḍ) by washing a garment and a vessel, because the illa (purification) exists with the ruling (necessity of intention) absent; for intention is not required in them. So ponder. Thus it is said, etc. The proponents are the proponents of ṭard (rejection) among the Shāfi‘īs. [Al-Shāfī: p. 282] We said: So the mu‘allil returns as a distinguisher by changing the illa to that the illa is not what you understood so that you would say: the absence of the ruling from an illa in the purification of a garment necessarily follows. Rather, according to us, the illa is legal purification (ṭahārah ḥukmiyyah) which is not rationally discernible, so it requires intention. The Hanafīs answered that the body becoming impure by the exit of filth is a rational matter; indeed, restricting (washing) to four limbs while the entire body needed purification is not rational, but it is allowed to avoid hardship. So when the body is impure, water is a purifier by nature and also legally, so one purifies with it and removes impurity without need for intention, unlike tayammum, because soil is polluting, not purifying. As for al-mu‘āraḍah (counterargument): [The difference between ta‘āruḍ (conflict) and muta‘āriḍ (conflicting proofs) is that tanāquḍ (contradiction) necessitates the invalidity of the proof itself, while ta‘āruḍ prevents the establishment of the ruling without attacking the proof.] It is that the questioner brings another proof that negates the ruling of the mu‘allil's proof, by saying to the mu‘allil: Your proof, even if it indicates the ruling, we have a proof that negates it. [Ḥāshiyat al-Shaykh Akram al-Nadwī: p. 244] The ruling etc. Since the research on the sources of Sharī‘ah—the four principles—is completed, know that what is established by these proofs of rulings is attached to their causes, conditions, and effective reasons, so it is necessary to explain them, and this chapter is for explaining that. Indeed, the ruling is attached to its cause because it leads to...
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This is a short but foundational chapter from al-Shāshī's Uṣūl defining the key terms: sabab (cause), illa (effective reason), and shart (condition). The opening sentence—'The ruling is attached to its cause, established by its effective reason, and found when its condition is present'—encapsulates the entire theory. The sabab is the extrinsic occasion for the ruling (e.g., the entrance of prayer time for the obligation of prayer), the illa is the intrinsic attribute that brings about the ruling (e.g., intoxication for prohibition of wine), and the shart is a prerequisite for the ruling (e.g., ritual purity for prayer). The text then delves into the concept of naqḍ (contradiction), which is when the claimed illa exists but the ruling is absent. This is a critical objection in qiyas. The example given: whoever claims that wuḍū’ requires intention because it is purification and all acts of worship require intention is contradicted by washing a garment, where purification occurs without intention. The Hanafī response refines the illa to 'legal purification' (ṭahārah ḥukmiyyah), which is not rationally discernible and thus requires intention. Then mu‘āraḍah (counterargument) is defined as bringing an alternative proof that negates the ruling. The chapter concludes by emphasizing that after establishing rulings from the four sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma‘, Qiyas), their connection to causes, conditions, and effective reasons must be understood. This lesson is a memorization anchor for the definitions of sabab, illa, and shart.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): The cause (occasion) to which the ruling is attached; e.g., the entrance of prayer time is the sabab for the obligation of prayer.
العلة (al-‘illa): The effective reason that establishes the ruling; an attribute that is appropriate (munāsib) for the ruling and upon which the ruling is built.
الشرط (al-shart): The condition at whose existence the ruling is found; without it the ruling does not exist, though it may still be attached to its sabab and illa.
النقض (al-naqḍ): An objection in qiyās where the claimed illa exists but the ruling is absent, indicating the illa is invalid.
المعارضة (al-mu‘āraḍah): An objection in qiyās where the questioner brings an independent proof that contradicts the ruling of the proponent's proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the ruling (hukm) and its cause (sabab)?
A) The ruling is established by its cause.
B) The ruling is attached to its cause.
C) The ruling exists when its cause is present.
D) The ruling is derived from its cause by analogy.

Key Takeaway
The ruling is attached to its sabab, established by its illa, and exists at its shart – these three distinctions are fundamental to deriving and defending rulings in the Hanafī school.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Four Categories of Hukm Attribution
Defining the four categories related to hukm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sabab, ‘illah, shart, and ‘alāmah by applying the Hanafi usul definitions to given scenarios.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a ruling is attributed primarily to its ‘illah; sabab, shart, and ‘alāmah are secondary with distinct functions.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi provides the foundational definitions of four key terms in Hanafi legal theory. Understanding these categories is essential for tracing how rulings are derived from proofs. The text lays out a logical division and a hierarchy of attribution, culminating in a practical rule for assigning a ruling to its appropriate category.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the Logical Division
The text divides the factors to which a ruling is attached into four categories using a binary tree. Identify the criteria: effective vs. non-effective, existence of ruling with it, and sign vs. non-sign.
The division ensures mutual exclusivity and completeness.
2
Differentiate Ifḍā’ and Iqtiḍā’
Sabab has ifḍā’ (efficacy) without iqtiḍā’ (necessitation); ‘illah has both. Understand that sabab leads to the ruling through an intermediary (the ‘illah), while ‘illah directly requires the ruling.
Example: opening a stable door (sabab) leads to the animal's exit (illah) which causes liability (ruling).
3
Learn the Hierarchy of Attribution
The text states: attribute the ruling first to the ‘illah; if impossible, to the cause of the ‘illah; then to the pure sabab; then to the shart. Memorize this sequence and the examples given.
This hierarchy is a key Hanafi principle for constructing qiyas.
4
Apply Definitions to Examples
Using the stable door example and the examples of ‘asr prayer, fitr charity, and supererogatory prayers, classify the factor as sabab, ‘illah, shart, or ‘alāmah. Justify your classification with the definitions.
Pay attention to whether the factor directly effects the ruling or only signals it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحكم إلخ لما تم البحث من دلائل الشرع وهو الأصول الأربعة، فاعلم أن ما ثبت بهذه الدلائل من الأحكام يتعلق بأسبابها وشروطها وعللها، فلابد من بيانها، وهذا الفصل لبيان ذلك، فإن الحكم يتعلق بسببه؛ لأنه يفضي - إلى إليه ويتوصل به إلى الحكم، ويثبت الحكم بعلته؛ لأنها مؤثرة في الحكم والحكم يوجد عند وجود الحكم بعلة؛ لأنها مؤثرة في الحكم، والحكم يوجد عند وجود الشرط، فالسبب ما يكون طريقا ووسيلة إلى المسبب، والحكم بواسطة بين الحكم والسبب كالطريق، فإن معناه اللغوي الطريق، واستعمل في الشرع بمعنى الطريق أيضاً كذا في "الفصول". يُتعلَّقُ بسببه: اعلم أن ما يتعلق به الأحكام أربعة: السبب والعلة والشرط، والعلامة، ووجه الحصر على هذه الأربعة: أن ما يتعلق به الأحكام إما مؤثر في الحكم ووجوده ظاهراً أو لا يكون، فالأول هو "العلة"، والثاني إما يوجد الحكم عنده أم لا ، فالأول هو الشرط"، والثاني إما أن يكون علماً على وجود الحكم أو لا، فالأول "العلامة" والثاني هو "السبب"، وإلا أن يحمل دليل الحصر على الاستقرار.
أن
هو
إلى الشيء إلخ والحاصل أن ما فيه افضاء لا اقتضاء هو "السبب" وما فيه اقتضاء للحكم أيضاً بذاته أي: ما يقتضيه بطبعه هو "العلة"، وما ليس فيه افضاء ولا اقتضاء بل لوجوده دخل في تحقق الحكم بأنه منوط به وموقوف عليه هو "الشرط"، وما ليس له دخل أيضاً بل مجرد تعريف وكشف هو "العلامة والإمارة"، والأصل في إضافة الحكم أن يضاف إلى "علة" كصلاة العصر، وإذا تعذرت فإلى "علة "العلة" كالسوق والقود، وعند التعذر فإلى "السبب المحض، وعند التعذر فإلى "الشرط" كصدقة الفطر وحجة الإسلام، وقد يضاف إلى غيرها كصلاة التسبيح، وصلاة الإستخارة، وصلاة القضاء والنفل فافهم. من الدابة إلخ وهي خروج الدابة، وخروج الطير، وذهاب العبد، فكان كل واحد من الفتح والحل سبباً، والخروج والذهاب علة له كذا في "المعدن".
The ruling, etc. Since the discussion of the proofs of the Shari‘ah, which are the four principles, has been completed, know that the rulings established by these proofs are attached to their causes (asbāb), conditions (shurūṭ), and effective causes (‘ilal). So it is necessary to explain them, and this chapter is for explaining that. For the ruling is attached to its cause, because it leads to it and through it one reaches the ruling. The ruling is established by its effective cause, because it is effective in the ruling. The ruling exists at the existence of the condition. Thus, the cause (sabab) is that which is a path and means to the effect (musabbab), and the ruling is through an intermediary between the ruling and the cause, like a road, for its linguistic meaning is road, and it is used in the Shari‘ah also in the sense of road. This is as in 'al-Fuṣūl'. It is attached to its cause: Know that the things to which rulings are attached are four: the cause (sabab), the effective cause (‘illah), the condition (sharṭ), and the sign (‘alāmah). The reason for restricting to these four is that what rulings are attached to is either effective in the ruling and its existence is apparent, or not. The first is the 'effective cause’. The second is either that the ruling exists with it or not, so the first is the 'condition', and the second is either a sign of the existence of the ruling or not, so the first is the 'sign' and the second is the 'cause' – unless we interpret the proof of restriction as based on consideration. The summary is that which has efficacy without necessitation is the 'cause'; that which also has necessitation of the ruling by itself, i.e., what necessitates it by its nature, is the 'effective cause'; that which has neither efficacy nor necessitation, but its existence has an effect in the realization of the ruling in that it is contingent on it and dependent on it, is the 'condition'; and that which also has no effect, but is merely a marker and disclosure, is the 'sign and indicator'. The principle in attributing a ruling is that it is attributed to the 'effective cause', like the ‘aṣr prayer; if that is not possible, then to the 'cause of the cause' like the market and retaliation; if not possible, then to the 'pure cause'; if not possible, then to the 'condition', like the charity of fitr and the pilgrimage of Islam. And it may be attributed to others, like the prayer of tasbīḥ, the prayer of istikhārah, the prayer of qaḍā’ and nafil. So understand. From the animal etc., which are the exiting of the animal, the exiting of the bird, and the going away of the slave. So each of opening and untying is a cause, and the exiting and going away is the effective cause of it. This is as in 'al-Ma‘din'.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is a definitional lesson in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, explaining the four categories that rulings are attached to: sabab (cause), ‘illah (effective cause), shart (condition), and ‘alāmah (sign). The author begins by stating that after discussing the four proofs (Qur’an, Sunnah, Ijma‘, Qiyas), it is necessary to explain the factors related to the rulings themselves. The ruling is attached to its sabab because the sabab is a means to the ruling through an intermediary (the ‘illah). The sabab is defined as a path with an intermediary, analogous to a road that leads to a destination through walking. The ‘illah is directly effective (mu’aththir) in the ruling. The condition (sharṭ) is something on which the existence of the ruling depends, but it does not cause the ruling. The sign (‘alāmah) is merely an indicator of the ruling without having any causal role. The text then provides a systematic breakdown: things that rulings are attached to are either effective in the ruling (that is the ‘illah) or not effective. If not effective, either the ruling exists with it (that is the sharṭ) or it does not. If it does not, either it is a sign of the ruling (that is the ‘alāmah) or it is not; but since it must be something, the only remaining category is the sabab. This is a logical division. The passage also gives the rule for attributing a ruling: primarily to the ‘illah, then to the ‘illah of the ‘illah, then to the pure sabab, then to the sharṭ. Examples: ‘asr prayer is attributed to the sun’s decline (which is the ‘illah? Actually the example is unclear but the text shows hierarchy). Examples of other attributions are given. The example of opening a stable door: the opening is the sabab, the animal’s exit is the ‘illah, and the loss (tلف) is the ruling. This illustrates the sabab-‘illah distinction.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): That which is a path and means to the ruling via an intermediary; it has efficacy (ifḍā’) without direct necessitation (iqtiḍā’).
العلة (al-‘illah): That which is directly effective (mu’aththir) in the ruling and necessitates it by its nature (iqtiḍā’).
الشرط (al-sharṭ): Something on which the existence of the ruling depends but which does not cause the ruling; the ruling exists when it is present.
العلامة (al-‘alāmah): A marker that indicates the ruling without having any causal relationship; purely a sign.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary factor to which a ruling is attributed, according to the text?
A) The sign (‘alāmah)
B) The condition (sharṭ)
C) The effective cause (‘illah)
D) The cause (sabab)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, rulings are attached to four categories: sabab (indirect cause), ‘illah (direct cause), shart (condition), and ‘alāmah (sign), with the ‘illah being the primary attributor.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
6 min
The Hanafi Concept of Sabab: Cause as a Sign
Defines causes as signs that make obligations known.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi concept of sabab as a sign (amara) that reveals a legal obligation and distinguish it from the efficient cause (illa).

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a cause (sabab) is a sign revealing obligation, not its efficient cause.

The passage from Al-Shashi's Usul tackles a foundational distinction: how do we know when an obligation is due? The Hanafi answer: through signs (asbab) appointed by the Lawgiver. This lesson unpacks that concept using the example of prayer time, showing that the entry of time is the sabab, not the verbal command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of sabab
Locate the sentence where the author explains what sabab means in this context. Look for terms like 'amara', 'ma'rif', 'kashf'.
The passage explicitly says: 'فالسبب في الشرع عبارة عما يكون طريقاً لمعرفة المطلوب لا موجبا له'.
2
Distinguish sabab from illa
The author stresses that sabab here is not the efficient cause (illa) that necessitates the ruling, but a sign that reveals the obligation. Note the contrast: 'سَبَبًا لوجوبها... لا بمعنى مؤثرات'.
Also: 'والمراد ههنا بالأسباب العلل' but then clarifies that the mashayikh chose sabab because it is more general.
3
Examine the prayer time example
The passage uses prayer and time as the primary example. Show how time acts as a sabab: it indicates that the obligation is now due. Note the proof: the address only comes after time.
Reference the Quranic verse: 'أقم الصلاة لدلوك الشمس'.
4
Address the role of the address (khitab)
Understand how the khitab relates to sabab. The khitab commands performance but does not create the obligation itself; the obligation is already there with the cause. This answers a potential objection.
The text says: 'والخطاب مثبت لوجوب الأداء ومعرّف للعبد سبب الوجوب قبله'.
5
Conclude with the broader principle
Generalize: in Hanafi usul, causes are signs (amarat) that make rulings known. This affects how we derive rulings and understand the relationship between time, address, and obligation.
The passage also discusses how the first part of time suffices, otherwise prayer couldn't be performed at the beginning.
