فصل في أسباب الأحكام الشرعية:
الأحكام الشرعية تتعلّق بأسبابها؛ وذلك لأن الوجوب غيب عنا فلابد من علامة يَعْرِفُ العبد بها وجوب الحكم، وبهذا الاعتبار أضيف الأحكام إلى الأسباب. فسبب وجوب الصلاة "الوقت" بدليل أن الخطاب بأداء الصلاة لا يتوجه قبل دخول الوقت، وإنما يتوجه بعد دخول الوقت، فلا يكون سبباً : لأن من شأن علاقة العلية أن يكون العلة مقتضية لوجود المعلول ومجامعتها معه ضرورة وجوب مجامعة العلة والمعلول والموجب وأن للعلة اختصاص بالمعلول وجوداً لا عدماً، ولا يتوهم أن المعد مناف للمعلول يجب رفعه وزواله عند وجوده؛ لأن الكلام في العلة الأصولية لا الحكمية فتدبر كذا في "الحصول". تتعلق إلخ: وذلك؛ لأن الوجوب إما هو بإيجابه تعالى وإيجابه وإن كان معلوماً لنا بالشرع، لكن تعلقاته المتجددة في انحاء الطلب بانصرامات الأزمنة خافية عنها، فإنه لا يعلم لنا في أي وقت تعلق الطلب فلابد ههنا من مراسم ومعالم وأمارات على خصوص انحاء الطلبات، فالأوقات لما كانت ظروفاً لتجدد نعمه، ومنه وموقفة لنا عليها معرفة لها اعتبرت في عامة الأحكام أسباباً وعللاً لوجوبها كما في الصلاة والصيام، فتعرض المصنف لبيان انحاء الأسباب والأحكام الشرعية الثابتة بالكتاب والسنة والإجماع والقياس، وبهذا علم أن الأسباب ههنا بمعنى أمارات ومعرفات كاشفة عن الأحكام لا بمعنى مؤثرات فالسبب الحقيقي لنفس الوجوب هو الإيجاب القديم وهو الحقيقية له تعالى وناب منابه الأسباب الظاهرة كالأوقات، والسبب الحقيقي لوجوب الأداء هو تعلق الطلب من الشارع، وسببه الظاهري صيغة الأمر اللفظية الحادثة كذا في "الحصول". وذلك لأن الوجوب: بإيجاب الله تعالى، وإيجابه تعالى الصلاة مثلاً في اليوم أو في الليلة لا يعلم متى يكون، فلو لم تكن الأسباب التي وضعت لها يشق معرفتها على العباد، ثم المراد ههنا بالأسباب العلل؛ لأن السبب في الشرع عبارة عما يكون طريقاً لمعرفة المطلوب لا موجباً له لكن المشائخ اختاروا لفظ السبب؛ لأنه أعم. قبل دخول الوقت وإليه أشير بقوله تعالى: ﴿أَقِمِ الصَّلاةَ لِدُلُوكِ الشَّمْسِ إِلَى غَسَقِ اللَّيْلِ﴾، والأصل في اللام هو للتعليل، ولو حمل على الوقت نظراً إلى قوله: ﴿فَسُبْحَانَ اللهِ حِينَ تُمْسُونَ وَحِينَ تُصْبِحُونَ﴾ الآية، فلا يضرنان؛ لأن التوقيت لا ينافي التعليل بناء على ما حققنا أنه السبب الظاهري، وأنه في الأصل من الظروف، وهذا القول
والخطابُ مُثبت لوجوب الأداء ومعرّفٌ للعبد سَبَبَ الوجوب قبله، وهذا كقولنا: "أدِّ ثَمَنَ المبيع، وأدِّ نَفَقَةَ المنكوحة"، ولا موجودَ يُعرفه العبد ههنا إلا دخول الوقت، فتبين أن الوجوب يثبتُ بدخول الوقت، ولأن الوجوب ثابت على من لا يتناوله الخطاب كالنائم والمغمى عليه ولا وجوب قبل الوقت فكان ثابتاً بدخول الوقت.
وبهذا ظهر أن الجزء الأول سبب للوجوب،
من أنه المصنف له أيضاً يشير إلى أن الوقت إنما هو معرف، وإنما السبب وهو توجه الخطاب بناء على لا يتوجه الخطاب قبل دخول الوقت، فالدوران دل على كونه سبباً لكنه بمعنى المعرف والامارة، فلا يضر أنكم كيف قلتم بالعلل الطردية كذا قال مولانا محمد حسن السنبهلي في "حصول الحواشي". والخطاب إلخ: جواب سوال وهو: أنه لما كان نفس الوجوب ثابتاً بالسبب وهو الوقت، فما فائدة الخطاب، فأجاب بقوله : والخطاب مثبت إلخ كذا في "المعدن". قبله : أي قبل وجوب الأداء، وهو ينفصل عن نفس الوجوب؛ لأن الخطاب يثبت بالأمر، ونفس الوجوب ثابت بالسبب وهو الوقت والسبب غير الأمر، فإن السبب يثبت به نفس الوجوب، والخطاب بالأمر يتوجه بعد ذلك السبب، ويعرف سبب الوجوب وهو الوقت قبله أي قبل وجوب الأداء كذا في "المعدن".
أد ثمن المبيع إلخ فإنه يجب الثمن بالبيع والنفقة بالنكاح، ويجب أداؤهما عند المطالبة كقولنا: "أد"، وبه يعرف أن الوجوب يثبت بالسبب أي الوقت سابقا على وجوب الأداء بالخطاب المتوجه بعد الوقت؛ لأن الوجوب أي وجوب الصلاة ثابت في حق من لا يتناوله الخطاب لكونه غير فاهم الخطاب كالنائم والمغمى عليه، غير زائد على يوم وليلة حتى أمر بالقضاء بعد الانتباه والإفاقة، والقضاء لا يجب إلا بدلاً عن الفائت، فعرفنا أن الوجوب ثابت في حقهما، ألا ترى أن الحائض لا يجب عليها القضاء؛ لما أنه لا يجب عليه الأداء كذا في "الفصول". كالنائم والمغمى عليه فإنهما في هذه الحالة غير صالحين لفهم الخطاب، ولا توجه إلا بفهمه، وإليه أشير في قوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تَقْرَبُوا الصَّلاةَ وَأَنْتُمْ سُكَارَى حَتَّى تَعْلَمُوا مَا تَقُولُونَ﴾ الآية، وفي حديث عائشة : "رفع القلم عن ثلاثة عن النائم حتى يستيقظ، وعن الصبي حتى يكبر، وعن المجنون حتى يعقل أو يفيق"، فعلم منه أن الوجوب في حقهما مضاف إلى السبب، ولا يمكن إضافته إلى الخطاب؛ لعدم توجه الخطاب كذا في "الحصول". الجزء الأول إلخ: فلا يتوقف الوجوب على كل الوقت؛ إذ لو كان كذلك لما يثبت الوجوب إلا بعد مضي الوقت فلا يصح إتيان الصلاة في الوقت للزوم تقدم المسبب على السبب، وهو لا يجوز كذا في "الفصول".
Chapter on the causes of legal rulings: Legal rulings are connected to their causes; because obligation is hidden from us, so there must be a sign by which the servant recognizes the obligation of the ruling. By this consideration, rulings are attributed to causes. So the cause of the obligation of prayer is 'time', evidenced by the fact that the address to perform prayer is not directed before the entry of time, but only after the entry of time. So it is not a cause (in the sense of efficient cause) because the nature of causality requires that the cause necessitates the existence of the effect and coexists with it necessarily, and that the cause has a specific relation to the effect in existence not non-existence. And one should not imagine that the absence of the cause is contrary to the effect requiring its removal and disappearance upon its existence, because we are speaking about the usuli cause, not the legal cause. This is from 'al-Husul'. 'Tata'allaq' etc.: because obligation is by His command, and His command, although known to us through revelation, its renewed attachments in aspects of request with the passing of times are hidden from us. So there must be here signs and markers and indicators for the specific aspects of requests. Times, since they are containers for the renewal of His blessings and are a means for us to know them, are considered in the majority of rulings as causes (asbab) and effective causes (ilal) for obligation, as in prayer and fasting. So the author intended to explain the types of causes and the legal rulings established by the Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. Through this it is known that causes here mean signs and identifiers that reveal the rulings, not in the sense of effectors. So the real cause for the obligation itself is the eternal command, which is truly from Him, and the apparent causes like times take its place. The real cause for the obligation of performance is the attachment of the request from the Lawgiver, and its apparent cause is the verbal command form that occurs. This is from 'al-Husul'. And that because obligation is by Allah's command, and His command for prayer for example in the day or night is not known when it occurs. So if there were no causes that are set for them, their knowledge would be difficult for the servants. Then what is meant here by causes is the effective causes (ilal); because the cause in Shari'ah is what is a path to know the required, not what necessitates it. But the mashayikh chose the word 'sabab' because it is more general. Before the entry of time, and to it is indicated by His saying: 'Establish prayer at the decline of the sun until the darkness of the night' and the original in the lam is for causation. If it is interpreted as time considering His saying: 'So glorify Allah when you enter the evening and when you enter the morning' the verse, it does not harm. Because timing does not contradict causation based on what we have verified that it is the apparent cause and that it is originally from containers. And this statement. And the address (khitab) establishes the obligation of performance and defines for the servant the cause of obligation before it. This is like our saying: 'Pay the price of the sold item, and pay the maintenance of the wife'. And there is nothing here that the servant knows except the entry of time, so it is clear that obligation is established by the entry of time. And because obligation is established upon one whom the address does not reach, like the sleeping and the unconscious, and there is no obligation before time, so it is established by the entry of time. By this it becomes apparent that the first part is a cause for obligation. From that the author also indicates that time is only a definer, and the cause is actually the direction of the address, based on that the address is not directed before the entry of time. So the co-existence (idara) indicates that it is a cause, but in the sense of a definer and sign. So it does not harm that you claimed with the purely definitional causes. This is what Mawlana Muhammad Hasan al-Sanhali said in 'Husul al-Hawashi'. And the address etc. is an answer to a question: that when the obligation itself is established by the cause which is time, what is the benefit of the address? So he answered by saying: the address establishes etc. This is from 'al-Ma'din'. Before it: i.e., before the obligation of performance, and it is separate from the obligation itself. Because the address is established by the command, and the obligation itself is established by the cause which is time, and the cause is other than the command. For the cause establishes the obligation itself, and the address by the command is directed after that cause, and it defines the cause of obligation which is time before it, i.e., before the obligation of performance. This is from 'al-Ma'din'. 'Pay the price of the sold item' etc.: for the price is obligatory by the sale, and the maintenance by marriage, and their payment is obligatory upon demand, like our saying: 'Pay'. By this it is known that obligation is established by the cause, i.e., time, prior to the obligation of performance by the address directed after time. Because obligation, i.e., the obligation of prayer, is established in the right of one whom the address does not reach because he is not understanding the address, like the sleeping and the unconscious, not exceeding a day and night, such that he is commanded to make up after waking and regaining consciousness. And make-up is only obligatory as a substitute for what was missed. So we know that obligation is established in their right. Do you not see that the menstruating woman is not obligated to make up because performance is not obligatory upon her? This is from 'al-Fusul'. Like the sleeping and the unconscious: for they in this state are not fit to understand the address, and it is only directed with understanding. To this is indicated in His saying: 'Do not approach prayer while you are intoxicated until you know what you are saying' the verse, and in the hadith of Aisha: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he grows up, and from the insane until he comes to his senses or recovers'. From this it is known that obligation in their right is attributed to the cause, and cannot be attributed to the address because the address is not directed. This is from 'al-Husul'. 'The first part' etc.: so obligation does not depend on the entire time; for if it were so, obligation would not be established until after the passage of time, and then performing prayer during the time would be invalid because it would necessitate the caused preceding the cause, which is not permissible. This is from 'al-Fusul'.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a chapter from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh text defining the concept of 'sabab' (cause) as it relates to legal rulings. The author explains that obligations (wajibat) are hidden from us; we only know them through signs. These signs are called 'asbab' (causes). The primary example is the obligation of prayer, whose cause is the entry of time. The text clarifies that this is an apparent cause (sabab zahiri), not the actual cause (illa haqiqiyya), which is Allah's eternal command. The commentary distinguishes between the cause that establishes the obligation itself (the entry of time) and the address (khitab) that commands performance. It addresses a potential objection: if time is the cause, what is the role of the command? The command defines the cause and obligates performance, but the obligation itself is already established by the time. The text further supports this by noting that the obligation applies even to those who cannot hear the command (e.g., sleeping, unconscious), proving the cause is the time, not the address. Additionally, the first part of the time is sufficient to establish the obligation, otherwise prayer could not be performed at the beginning of the time. The discussion is rooted in Quranic verses and hadith, emphasizing that causes are signs (amarat) that reveal rulings, not efficient causes.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): In this text, a sign (amara) that makes a ruling known, not the efficient cause.
العلامة (al-amara): Sign or indicator that reveals the obligation.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Legal obligation established by the Shari'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of prayer?
A) The verbal command (khitab) to pray
B) The entry of time (dukhul al-waqt)
C) The intention of the person
D) The ability to perform

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a cause (sabab) is a sign that reveals an obligation, not its efficient cause; the entry of time is the sabab for prayer.

The Cause of Obligation: Entry of Time vs. Divine Address
Explaining that time is the cause of obligation, not the address

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cause (sabab) of the obligation of prayer and explain why the divine address (khitab) is not the cause, applying the Hanafi definition of sabab.

Core Idea
The entry of time, not the divine address, is the cause of prayer's obligation.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, distinguishing between the cause (sabab) of a ruling and the divine address (khitab) is foundational. This passage from Usul al-Shashi clarifies that for prayer, the cause is the entry of time, not the command itself. Understanding this mechanism is essential for correctly determining when obligations arise and how to handle cases where capacity changes during the time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
The passage claims that the cause (sabab) of the obligation of prayer is the entry of time (dukhul al-waqt), not the divine address (khitab). The khitab only makes known the cause and commands performance after the cause exists.
2
Analyze the Proof via the Sleeper and Unconscious
The author argues that obligation is established on those whom the address does not reach, such as the sleeper and unconscious person. Since they are not addressed, their obligation must be due to the time itself.
This proof is based on the hadith 'The pen is lifted from three: the sleeper until he wakes, the child until he becomes adult, and the insane until he recovers.'
3
Understand the Sequential Causality
The cause operates sequentially: the first part of the time is the initial cause. If one does not perform in that part, the cause transfers to the next part, and so on, until the last part where the obligation becomes fixed.
4
Apply to Cases of Changing Capacity
Consider the status of the servant in the last part of the time. If a child becomes adult, a disbeliever converts, or a menstruating woman becomes pure in that last part, the prayer becomes obligatory on them. This shows obligation is tied to the time, not to a prior state.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle of considering the end of the time for obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أسباب الأحكام الشرعية
والخطابُ مُثبت لوجوب الأداء ومعرّفٌ للعبد سَبَبَ الوجوب قبله، وهذا كقولنا: "أدِّ ثَمَنَ المبيع، وأدِّ نَفَقَةَ المنكوحة"، ولا موجودَ يُعرفه العبد ههنا إلا دخول الوقت، فتبين أن الوجوب في الصلاة يثبتُ بدخول الوقت، ولأن الوجوب ثابت على من لا يتناوله الخطاب كالنائم والمغمى عليه ولا وجوب قبل الوقت فكان ثابتاً بدخول الوقت.
وبهذا ظهر أن الجزء الأول سبب للوجوب، ثم بعد ذلك طريقان: أحدهما: نقل السببية من الجزء الأول إلى الثاني إذا لم يؤد في الجزء الأول، ثم إلى الثالث والرابع إلى أن ينتهي إلى آخر الوقت، فيتقرر الوجوب حينئذ، ويُعتبر حال العبد في ذلك الجزء الآخر من أجزاء الوقت وبيان اعتبار حال العبد فيه: أنه لو كان صبيا في أول الوقت بالغاً في ذلك الجزء الآخر من الوقت، أو كان كافراً في أول الوقت مسلماً في ذلك الجزء أو كانت حائضاً أو نُفَساءَ في أول الوقت طاهرةً في ذلك الجزء وجبت الصلاة. وعلى هذا جميع صور حدوث الأهلية في آخر الوقت.

Chapter on the causes of legal rulings. The address (khitab) establishes the obligation of performance and makes known to the servant the cause of obligation before it. This is like our saying: 'Pay the price of the sold item, and pay the maintenance of the married woman.' There is nothing known to the servant here except the entry of time, so it becomes clear that the obligation in prayer is established by the entry of time. And because the obligation is established upon those whom the address does not reach, like the sleeper and the unconscious, and there is no obligation before the time, so it is established by the entry of time. And by this it is apparent that the first part (al-juz' al-awwal) is the cause of obligation. Then after that there are two ways: one: transferring the causality from the first part to the second if he did not perform in the first part, then to the third and fourth until it ends at the last part of the time, then the obligation becomes settled at that point, and the status of the servant in that last part is considered. Regarding the consideration of the servant's status in it: if he was a child at the beginning of the time and reached puberty in that last part of the time, or was a disbeliever at the beginning and became Muslim in that part, or was menstruating or postpartum at the beginning and became pure in that part, then the prayer becomes obligatory. And upon this are all cases of capacity arising at the end of the time.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi is a key discussion on the definition and operation of causes (asbab) in Hanafi legal theory. The author opens by clarifying the relationship between the divine address (khitab) and the cause (sabab) of obligation. He explains that the khitab does not create the obligation; rather, it informs the servant of the cause and commands performance after the cause exists. For prayer, the cause is the entry of time (dukhul al-waqt). Evidence for this is that obligation is proven for the sleeper and unconscious person, who are not addressed, yet they are obligated; this obligation cannot be from the khitab, so it must be from the time. The first part of the time is thus the cause of obligation. Next, the author explains the mechanism if one delays prayer: the cause transfers sequentially to subsequent parts of the time until the last part, when the obligation becomes fixed. At that final part, the legal capacity (ahliyyah) of the person is considered: if a child becomes pubescent, a disbeliever accepts Islam, or a menstruating woman becomes pure in that last part, the prayer becomes obligatory on them. This shows that the obligation is tied to the cause (time) and not to a previous state. The passage exemplifies Hanafi causal reasoning (ta'lil) and the importance of time as a cause (sabab) in worship.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): That which is made by the Lawgiver a sign (amarah) for the existence of a ruling; here, the entry of time is the cause for the obligation of prayer.
خطاب (khitab): The divine address (command) that communicates the ruling to the servant; it informs of the cause and commands performance after the cause exists.
وجوب (wujub): The legal obligation that becomes binding upon the mukallaf; here, the obligation of prayer upon entry of time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Determining Prayer Obligation Based on Status at the End of Time
Ruling on prayer obligation when traveler/resident status changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that the end of the prayer time determines the obligation, distinguishing between travel status and exempting conditions.

Core Idea
The end of the prayer time, not the beginning, decides the number of rak'ahs and obligation.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi illustrates a key principle: the attribute at the end of the prayer time governs the completeness of the obligation. Whether a person begins as a traveler or resident, it is the status at the moment the time ends that determines if he prays two or four rak'ahs. Similarly, the occurrence of an exempting condition at any point during the time drops the obligation entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two distinct cases: (1) if an exempting condition (menstruation, postnatal bleeding, continuous insanity, prolonged unconsciousness) occurs during the time, prayer is dropped; (2) if travel status changes, the number of rak'ahs is based on the end of the time.
2
Extract the underlying principle
Both rulings demonstrate that the condition at the end of the time is decisive. This is the usul principle: the final moment of the prayer time determines the obligation's completion or concession.
3
Apply the principle to travel
If a person is a traveler at the beginning and a resident at the end, he prays the full prayer (e.g., four rak'ahs for Zuhr). If he is a resident at the beginning and a traveler at the end, he prays the traveler's prayer (two rak'ahs).
This applies only to prayers that allow qasr: Zuhr, Asr, Isha.
4
Consider exemptions
If an exempting condition occurs at any point during the time (even at the very end), the prayer obligation for that time is completely dropped. There is no requirement to make it up.
The exemption covers the entire time once it occurs.
5
Note the usul rule
This passage is a clear example of the usul rule that the hukm (legal obligation) attaches to the last part of the time for obligations that span the entire time. It is a principle of takyif al-waqt (characterizing the moment).
This rule is specific to Hanafi usul; other schools may apply a different principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى العكس بأن يحدث حيض أو أنفاس أو جنون مستوعب أو إغماء ممتد في ذلك الجزء سقطت عنه الصلاة. ولو كان مسافراً في أول الوقت مقيماً في آخره يصلي أربعاً، ولو كان مقيماً في أول الوقت مسافراً في آخره يصلي ركعتين.
And on the contrary: if menstruation, post-natal bleeding, continuous insanity, or prolonged unconsciousness occurs in that part, the prayer is dropped from him. And if he was a traveler at the beginning of the time and a resident at its end, he prays four; and if he was a resident at the beginning of the time and a traveler at its end, he prays two rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents two rules from Hanafi fiqh regarding the effect of a change in personal status during prayer time. The first rule states that if a state negating the obligation of prayer (menstruation, post-natal bleeding, continuous insanity covering the entire part, or prolonged unconsciousness) occurs, the prayer obligation is dropped entirely. The second rule concerns travel: if a person begins the time as a traveler and becomes a resident before the end, he must pray the full four rak'ahs (since residency applies at the end). Conversely, if he begins as a resident and becomes a traveler, he prays two rak'ahs, because the traveler's concession applies. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that the attribute of the end part of the time determines the completeness or deficiency of the obligation.

Key Terms
مسافر (musāfir): A traveler who meets the conditions for qasr (shortening prayer).
مقيم (muqīm): A resident who is not traveling.
حيض (hayḍ): Menstruation, one of the exempting conditions that drops prayer obligation.
نفاس (nifās): Post-natal bleeding, exempting condition.
جنون مستوعب (junūn mustaw'ib): Continuous insanity covering the entire part of the time.
إغماء ممتد (ighmā' mumtadd): Prolonged unconsciousness covering the entire part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Cause of Zakah and Expediting Payment
Defining the cause of zakah and explaining the ruling on expediting payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the cause of zakah is ownership of nisab to determine the validity of expediting payment before the year completes.

Core Idea
The cause of zakah is ownership, not the year; expediting is permissible once the cause exists.

In Hanafi usul, understanding the cause (sabab) of an obligation is critical for determining when the obligation becomes due. This passage clarifies that the cause of zakah is ownership of nisab, and the passing of the year is merely a condition. It also introduces a key dalil from the hadith of al-Abbas, which permits expediting payment before the year ends.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine what ruling the passage is addressing: the obligation of zakah and the permissibility of paying before the year completes.
2
Extract the cause (sabab)
Locate the explicit statement: 'sabab wujub al-zakah milk al-nisab al-nami.' This is the core of the analysis.
Note the distinction between real growth (trade) and legal growth (year).
3
Analyze the dalil
Examine the hadith of al-Abbas: the Prophet permitted expediting, indicating that the obligation is triggered by ownership, not the year.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so Hanafi usul treats it as operative but not qati.
4
Apply the usul principle
In Hanafi usul, when the cause exists, the effect can be brought forward (al-sabab idha wujid jaza al-ta'jil). This is the basis for expediting.
This principle distinguishes zakah from hajj where the cause (the House) is unique and non-repeating.
5
Differentiate from other ibadat
Understand why zakah repeats annually while hajj does not: the cause in zakah (nisab) can be considered renewed each year, unlike the Kaaba.
The passage uses this to highlight the nature of the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسَبَبُ وجوب الزكاة ملك النصاب النامي حقيقة أو حكماً، وباعتبار وجوب السبب جاز التعجيل في باب الأداء.
ملك النصاب إلخ أي نمواً حقيقياً بالتجارة، أو حكماً بحولان الحول؛ لأن به يتمكن من استنماء المال على الكمال؛ لأن الحول يشتمل على الفصول الأربعة، وبهذا ظهر الفرق بين الزكاة والحج من أن الزكاة تجب مكرراً بحولان الحول دون الحج؛ لأن النصاب الواحد باعتبار النماء يتكرر حكماً، والبيت لا يتكرر أصلاً لا حقيقة وهو ظاهر، ولا تقديراً؛ لأن حرمة البيت أمر واحد مستمر وهي مدة كاملة لاستنماء كل جنس من المال كالنقد والسائم وغيرهما، فأقيم مقام النماء لعدم الإطلاع على حقيقة النماء، أو التقصير في الاستنماء، وإنما كان المال سبباً للزكاة؛ لأنها مضاف إليه يقال: زكاة المال، فكان وجود النصاب وهو المال المقدر سبباً فافهم كذا في "الفصول". جاز التعجيلُ إلخ: يعني إذا ملك نصاباً جاز أن يؤدي الزكاة قبل حولان الحول؛ لوجود المسبب بعد وجود السبب.

And the cause of obligation of zakah is ownership of productive nisab, in reality or legally; and due to the obligation of the cause, expediting in payment is permissible. (Explanation: real growth through trade, or legal growth through the passing of the year; because through it one is able to fully develop the wealth; because the year includes the four seasons. And through this the difference between zakah and hajj appears: zakah is repeated annually while hajj is not, because the single nisab is considered repeatedly due to growth, whereas the House (Kaaba) is not repeated at all, not in reality nor in estimation. Because the sanctity of the House is one continuous thing, and the complete period for developing each type of wealth like currency and grazing animals is the year, so it stands in place of growth due to difficulty in knowing actual growth or neglect in developing. And wealth is the cause of zakah because it is added to it: 'zakah of wealth', so the existence of nisab which is the specified wealth is the cause. (Expediting: meaning if one owns nisab, it is permissible to pay zakah before the year passes because the effect exists after the existence of the cause.) (Expediting: know that the permissibility of expediting charity (i.e. zakah) before the completion of the year is reported in the hadith of Ali that al-Abbas asked the Prophet to expedite his charity before it was due and he permitted that.)

Commentary
This passage defines the cause of zakah as ownership of nisab that is productive (either by trade or by the passage of a full year). The commentary explains that the year serves as a proxy for growth. It distinguishes zakah from hajj by noting that zakah repeats due to the recurring nature of the cause (nisab potentially grows each year), while hajj does not. It also discusses the permissibility of paying zakah before the year completes (ta'jil) based on a hadith about Al-Abbas. This is a standard Hanafi position: expediting is allowed because the cause (ownership of nisab) already exists.

Key Terms
ملك النصاب النامي (milk al-nisab al-nami): Ownership of a minimum threshold of wealth that is capable of growth, either through trade or through the passage of a year.

Identifying the Cause of Hajj and Deriving Non-Repetition
Stating the cause of hajj as the House and explaining non-repetition via hadith and usul principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sabab (cause) of hajj according to Hanafi usul and derive that the obligation is not repeated by applying the principle that an absolute command does not imply repetition.

Core Idea
The singular cause of hajj makes it once-in-a-lifetime; the absolute command confirms non-repetition.

In this lesson, we examine a classical usul text that tackles a key question: why is hajj obligatory only once in a lifetime? The answer lies in identifying the correct cause (sabab) and understanding how a prophetic command operates in Hanafi legal theory. You will learn to differentiate between a cause and a condition, and see how the same principle applies elsewhere.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Claim
The passage states that the cause of hajj is the House (al-bayt). Look for the construct 'hajj al-bayt' and note that the cause is singular.
2
Examine the Evidence
The hadith 'Inna Allaha qad farada 'alaykum al-hajj fahujju' provides the basis. Also the usul principle: al-amr al-mutlaq la yufidu al-takrar.
3
Analyze the Alternative View
A possibility is that the cause is the servant's servitude, with the House and istita'ah as conditions. The author shows this also leads to non-repetition.
4
Explore the Consequence
If the cause were only the House, hajj would be fard kifaya (like funeral prayer) due to unity of cause. This is avoided by the chosen view.
5
Distinguish from Zakah
Performing hajj before istita'ah suffices because the cause (the House) exists; for zakah, performing before nisab does not count because the cause (nisab) is absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسَبَبُ وجوب الحج "البيت" لإضافته إلى البيت، وعدم تكرار الوظيفة في العمر.
عدم تعدد وجوبها
وعلى هذا لو حج قبل وجود الاستطاعة ينوب ذلك عن حجة الإسلام لوجود السبب،
وبه فارَقَ أداء الزكاة قبل وجود النصاب لعدم السبب.

And the cause of obligation of hajj is 'the House' due to its addition to the House, and the non-repetition of the duty in a lifetime. (Non-multiplicity of its obligation). Based on this, if one performs hajj before having istita'ah, it suffices for the hajj of Islam because the cause exists. (And non-repetition of the duty: because hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime, and this is established by the words of the Prophet: 'Indeed Allah has obligated hajj upon you, so perform hajj.' And because an absolute command does not necessitate repetition. On this view also, repetition is not required due to the unity of the servant's servitude. If the cause were the House, then hajj would be a communal obligation fulfilled by some, like funeral prayer, due to the unity of the cause.

Commentary
This passage discusses the cause of hajj. The primary cause is the House (Kaaba) as indicated by the construct phrase 'hajj al-bayt'. Because the cause is one (the House), hajj is obligatory only once in a lifetime. The commentary considers an alternative view that the cause is the servant's state of servitude, but in both cases non-repetition is logical. It also addresses whether hajj performed without istita'ah counts, and distinguishes from zakah. The passage includes a hadith and usul principle about absolute commands.

Key Terms
البيت (al-bayt): The Kaaba, considered as the cause (sabab) for the obligation of hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is hajj not repeated annually like zakah?
A) Because the command is absolute and does not imply repetition.
B) Because the cause (the House) is one and does not multiply.
C) Both A and B.
D) Because the year is not a condition for hajj.

Key Takeaway
Hajj is wajib once because its cause (the House) is singular and the absolute command from the Prophet does not imply repetition.

Cause of Obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr
Defining the cause of sadaqat al-fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cause (sabab) of sadaqat al-fitr according to Hanafi usul and derive the ruling from the hadith proof.

Core Idea
The sabab of sadaqat al-fitr is the dependent person, proven by the command 'Pay for those you support'.

This lesson examines the cause (sabab) of sadaqat al-fitr as defined by Hanafi usul. The passage from Usul al-Shashi identifies the cause as 'ra's yamoonuh' (a dependent person) and supports it with a hadith. Understanding this cause is essential to determine on whose behalf fitr must be paid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
Read the first line: 'The cause of sadaqat al-fitr is a head one supports.' This is the sabab: the dependent person.
2
Locate the dalil
The text quotes the hadith 'Addu 'amman tamununah'. Note that this is a prophetic command, classified as Sunnah ahad (zanni al-thubut).
The hadith is not from the Quran but from the Sunnah, which in Hanafi usul can establish obligation if the command is clear.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'Addu' (pay) is a direct imperative. In Hanafi usul, the default for an imperative is obligation (wujub). The phrase 'amman tamununah' (for those you support) indicates that the cause is the existence of a dependent.
The word 'cause' (sabab) is a term of art in usul: something that makes the ruling applicable.
4
Apply to a scenario
If a person has a wife and two children, each dependent is a separate cause for fitr. The payer must pay fitr for each head.
This highlights the practical consequence: the number of fitr payments equals the number of dependents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسبب وجوب صدقة الفطر رأس يَمُونه ويلي عليه.
يَمُونه : لقوله عليها: "أدوا عمن تمونونه" أي تحملوا هذه المؤنة عمن وجبت عليكم مؤنته.
And the cause of obligation of sadaqat al-fitr is a head that one supports and is in charge of. (Yamoonuh: according to his (the Prophet's) saying: 'Pay for those you support', i.e., bear this expense for those whose maintenance is obligatory upon you.)
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage states the cause of sadaqat al-fitr (zakat al-fitr). It is the dependent person (ra's) whom one supports (yamoonuh). The proof is the hadith instructing to pay for those one supports. This means every person for whom a Muslim is responsible for maintenance (e.g., family members, slaves) is a cause for paying fitr.

Key Terms
رأس يَمُونه (ra's yamoonuh): A person (head) whose maintenance is the responsibility of the payer.
سبب (sabab): The cause or legal trigger that makes a ruling applicable; here, the existence of a dependent person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The sighting of the moon of Shawwal.
B) The person one supports.
C) The wealth one possesses.
D) The passing of Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
The cause (sabab) of sadaqat al-fitr is the dependent person (ra's yamoonuh), as proven by the command to pay for those one supports.

Asbab al-Ahkam: Identifying Causes of Legal Obligations
Listing and explaining the causes of various obligatory acts with a dispute on wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sabab, identify the cause for each major obligatory act (zakat, hajj, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, kharaj, wudu, ghusl), and apply the principle of ta'jil using the sabab framework.

Core Idea
The cause (sabab) triggers obligation; its presence permits early performance, and its nature determines repetition.

This lesson from Usul al-Shashi introduces the Hanafi concept of legal cause (sabab) by listing the causes of several obligatory acts. Understanding sabab is fundamental to Hanafi usul because it distinguishes a trigger from a condition or preventer. The passage also explores a key dispute: is the cause of wudu prayer or ritual impurity? We will work through each example to see how the Hanafi school justifies its positions.

Guided Path
1
Define sabab in Hanafi usul
Sabab is the cause that necessitates a legal obligation when it exists. It is distinct from shart (condition) and mani' (preventer).
2
Identify the sabab for each obligatory act
From the passage: zakat -> ownership of productive nisab; hajj -> the Ka'ba (or the servant in terms of servitude); sadaqat al-fitr -> a dependent head; 'ushr -> productive land; kharaj -> land suitable for cultivation; ghusl -> menstruation, postpartum bleeding, janabah; wudu (Hanafi view) -> prayer.
Note that for hajj, the text suggests the true cause is the existence of the servant to avoid making hajj a collective duty.
3
Analyze the legal implications
Because the sabab of zakat exists before the year ends, ta'jil (acceleration) is permitted. The sabab of hajj (the Ka'ba) does not repeat, so hajj is obligatory only once. The sabab of sadaqat al-fitr (a dependent head) allows ta'jil before Eid day.
4
Examine the wudu dispute
Two views: (1) Hanafi view: sabab of wudu is prayer; (2) Opposing view: sabab is hadath. The Hanafi refutation argues that hadath removes purity, thus cannot lead to it; wudu is required only when one intends to pray.
5
Complete the proof chain for wudu
Using the source text, identify the textual category and apply Hanafi usul principles to derive the ruling. Fill in the missing steps in the proof_chain below.

Source Text

The Fourth Research: On Qiyas. Chapter on the Causes of Legal Rulings. The cause of the obligation of zakat is ownership of a productive nisab, actually or constructively, and by considering the obligation of the cause, acceleration (ta'jil) is permitted in performance. The cause of the obligation of hajj is 'the House' (al-Bayt) due to its attribution to the House, and non-repetition of the duty in a lifetime. Non-multiplicity of its obligation. And upon this, if one performs hajj before the existence of istita'ah, it suffices for the hajj of Islam due to the existence of the cause. And by this it differs from performing zakat before the existence of the nisab due to the absence of the cause. The cause of the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr is a head (person) for whom one provides maintenance (yamunu) and upon whom one has authority (yali). 'Ownership of nisab etc.' meaning actual growth through trade, or constructively by the passing of the year; because by it one is able to fully grow the wealth; because the year includes the four seasons. By this the difference between zakat and hajj becomes clear: zakat is repeated with the passing of the year while hajj is not; because the single nisab is considered repeatedly growing constructively, while the House does not repeat at all neither actually—which is apparent—nor virtually; because the sanctity of the House is a single continuous matter, and it is a complete period for the growth of every type of wealth such as cash, grazing animals, and others. So it (the year) stands in place of growth due to the inability to ascertain the reality of growth, or due to negligence in growth. Rather, wealth is a cause for zakat because it is attributed to it: it is said 'zakat of wealth', so the existence of nisab, which is the specified wealth, is the cause. Understand this. Thus in 'al-Fusul'. 'Ta'jil is permitted' etc. means: if one owns a nisab, it is permissible to pay zakat before the passing of the year, due to the existence of the effect after the existence of the cause. And 'non-repetition of the duty': because hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime, and this is established by the Prophet's saying: 'Indeed Allah has made hajj obligatory upon you, so perform hajj.' And because an absolute command does not necessitate repetition. [al-Shafi: p. 299] There is what has preceded. And it is possible that the cause of its obligation is the existence of the slave (al-'abd) in terms of servitude. For after the House and istita'ah, both are conditions for its obligation, not the cause. And upon this also, repetition of the duty is not necessary due to the unity of the slave in terms of servitude. But if the cause were the House, then it would imply that hajj is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) discharged by the performance of some, like the funeral prayer, due to the unity of the cause, and the performance of its requirement by the performance of some, and no valid aspect can be imagined except by considering it as permissiveness. Thus in 'al-Husul'. 'Yamunu': due to his (the Prophet's) saying: 'Pay on behalf of those for whom you provide maintenance.' Meaning: bear this expense for those whose maintenance is obligatory upon you. 'Ta'jil is permitted': Know that the permissibility of expediting charity (i.e., zakat) before the completion of the year has been reported in the hadith of 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that al-'Abbas asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) regarding expediting his sadaqah before it became due, and he permitted him to do so. It was narrated by the four except al-Nasa'i, and also by al-Darimi, Ahmad, and 'Abd al-Razzaq. = [Page 243] Sadaqat al-Fitr. And by considering the cause, ta'jil is permitted so that it is permissible to pay it before the day of Fitr. 'al-Ra's' and the cause of the obligation of 'ushr is lands that are productive by actual yield (haqiqat al-ray'). The cause of the obligation of kharaj is lands suitable for cultivation, so they are constructively productive. And the cause of the obligation of wudu is prayer according to some scholars. For this reason, wudu is obligatory upon one for whom prayer is obligatory, and there is no wudu upon one for whom there is no prayer. And some said: its cause is hadath (ritual impurity), and the obligation of prayer is a condition. And it has been reported from Muhammad that he analyzed that textually. And the cause of the obligation of ghusl is menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and janabah (major impurity). 'Lands that are productive': because 'ushr is attributed to land: it is said 'ushr of the land' by actual yield: i.e., produce. So even if the owner neglects the 'ushr land, 'ushr is not obligatory even though it is suitable. Thus in 'al-Ma'din'. 'Hadath': And this is incorrect; because the cause of something is that which leads to that thing, and hadath removes and lifts purity, and that which removes and lifts cannot lead to it. So how can hadath be a cause for it? And what they said that obligation is repeated by the repetition of hadath is rejected; for it is repeated by the repetition of intending prayer. Do you not see that if hadath occurs after prayer, wudu is not obligatory unless one intends to stand for another prayer? And if hadath were the cause, it would be obligatory even if one does not intend another prayer. Thus it is clear that the obligation of wudu is by the repetition of intending prayer, not by the repetition of hadath. Understand this. Thus in 'al-Ma'din' and others.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi is a chapter on the causes (asbab) of legal obligations. It is a typical Hanafi usul discussion: for each religious duty, the author identifies its sabab (cause) and explains the rationale. The passage begins by stating that the cause of zakat is ownership of a nisab that is productive (nami)—either actually through trade or constructively by the passing of a lunar year. The key point is that because the cause is established (ownership of nisab), it becomes permissible to pay zakat before the year ends (ta'jil), unlike hajj where the cause (the Ka'ba) does not repeat, so hajj is only once in a lifetime. The author then discusses hajj: the Sabab is the House (al-Bayt), not istita'ah; istita'ah is a condition. He notes a potential problem: if the cause is one (the Ka'ba), then hajj would be a collective obligation like janazah prayer, but it is not; the solution is that the true cause is the existence of the servant (al-'abd) in terms of servitude, which is unique to each person, so the duty is individual. Next, the cause of sadaqat al-fitr: a head (person) that one provides maintenance for. The author supports this with the hadith 'Pay on behalf of those for whom you provide maintenance.' Then the causes of 'ushr and kharaj: 'ushr is caused by productive land (actual yield), kharaj by land suitable for cultivation (constructive productivity). Then a significant dispute on the cause of wudu: the majority (jumhur) and (apparently) some scholars say the cause is prayer itself; others (the text says 'al-ba'd'—some) say the cause is hadath. The author refutes the latter with rational argument: hadath removes purity, so it cannot be a cause; rather, wudu becomes wajib when one intends to pray. This is a classic Hanafi position. Lastly, the cause of ghusl is explicit: menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and janabah. Throughout, the author draws from earlier Hanafi works like al-Fusul, al-Husul, and al-Ma'din.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers a legal obligation; its existence necessitates the obligation.
ملك النصاب النامي (milk al-nisab al-nami): Ownership of a minimum amount of wealth that is productive (capable of growth) either actually or constructively.
تعجيل (ta'jil): Accelerating the payment of an obligation before its due time, permitted when the cause is present.
حدث (hadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wudu, according to the other opinion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is hajj not repeated in a lifetime?
A) Because the cause (the Ka'ba) does not repeat.
B) Because it is too burdensome.
C) Because the Prophet performed it once.
D) Because istita'ah cannot be repeated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi concept of sabab is central to usul: it triggers obligation, permits acceleration, and determines repetition; the wudu dispute illustrates how cause must be a leading factor, not a removal.

The Obstacle (Mani') in Hanafi Usul: Definition and Types
Opening definition and classification of obstacles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mani' according to Hanafi usul scholars and state the dispute regarding its primary divisions.

Core Idea
An obstacle (mani') blocks the legal ruling even when its cause is present.

You have learned about the cause (sabab) and condition (shart) that bring about a legal ruling. Now we turn to the obstacle (mani'): an existent attribute that, despite the presence of the cause, prevents the ruling from taking effect. This passage from Usul al-Shashi opens the chapter on obstacles, offering a definition by the usul scholars and noting a difference of opinion on how many primary types there are. Understanding this definition is key to applying the sabab-shart-mani' framework correctly.

Guided Path
1
Master the definition of al-mani'
Read the definition given: 'al-mani' huwa al-wasf al-wujudi al-zahir al-mundabit al-mu'arraf naqid al-hukm'. Identify each component: it must be an existent (not non-existence), apparent, regular, and it defines the opposite of the ruling.
This definition ensures the obstacle is a concrete, observable attribute.
2
Understand the effect of the obstacle
The definition states it 'prevents the ruling despite the existence of the cause' (yamna' al-hukm ma'a wujud al-sabab). Contrast this with a condition, which must be present for the ruling to apply; an obstacle cancels the ruling even when the cause is present.
Example: debt may prevent zakat obligation despite owning nisab.
3
Identify the classification dispute
The text quotes Qadi Imam Abu Zaid that obstacles are four types, but some books mention five. Note that the passage cuts off before listing them; the dispute itself is part of the lesson.
This is a memorization anchor: the number of primary divisions is debated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الموانع:
قال القاضي الإمام أبو زيد : الموانع أربعة أقسام:
= الموانع: اعلم أن المانع عند الأصوليين هو الوصف الوجودي الظاهر المنضبط المعرف نقيض الحكم، فإنه يمنع الحكم مع وجود السبب. [الشافي: ص ۳۰۲] أربعة والمذكور في بعض الكتب: أن الموانع خمسة: الأربعة منها =
Chapter on Obstacles: Qadi Imam Abu Zaid said: The obstacles are of four types. = Obstacles: Know that the obstacle according to usul scholars is the existent, apparent, regular attribute that defines the opposite of the ruling, for it prevents the ruling despite the existence of the cause. [al-Shafi: p. 302] Four, and it is mentioned in some books that the obstacles are five: four of them =
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This brief passage from Usul al-Shashi begins the chapter on obstacles (mawani'). It opens with a citation from Qadi Imam Abu Zaid (a Hanafi authority) that obstacles are of four types. Then the author provides a definition of al-mani' (the obstacle) from the usul scholars: it is an existent, apparent, well-defined attribute that is the opposite of the legal ruling; it prevents the ruling from applying even when the cause (sabab) is present. For example, if the cause for zakat (ownership of nisab) is present but an obstacle like debt (in some views) prevents the obligation. The text notes that some books mention five obstacles, but this passage is cut off before listing the types. This is a foundational usul concept: the triad of sabab, shart, and mani'.

Key Terms
مانع (mani'): An existent attribute that prevents the ruling despite the presence of the cause.
وصف وجودي (wasf wujudi): An attribute that exists (not a non-existence).
وصف ظاهر (wasf zahir): An attribute that is apparent or observable.
وصف منضبط (wasf mundabit): An attribute that is regular or consistent (not fluctuating).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in the passage, what does an obstacle (mani') do?
A) It invalidates the cause (sabab).
B) It prevents the ruling even though the cause is present.
C) It removes the condition (shart).
D) It creates a new cause.

Key Takeaway
An obstacle is an existent, apparent attribute that blocks the ruling even when its cause is fully present.

Linguistic Definition of Al-Fard and Types of Taqdir
Defines 'fard' linguistically as taqdir and classifies four types of taqdir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic meaning of al-fard as taqdir and identify the four types of Shariah estimations (taqdirat) with examples.

Core Idea
Fard means precise determination, not generic obligation—this shapes how Hanafi usul treats fixed rulings.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, the author opens the chapter on taklifi rulings by defining the key term 'fard'. Understanding that al-fard linguistically means al-taqdir (estimation) is essential because it reveals that Shariah obligations are precisely determined by the Lawgiver. The passage then enriches this by classifying four kinds of taqdir, showing how different rules (like hudud, khiyar, and travel) exhibit different degrees of fixity. This sets the stage for the Hanafi approach to obligatory acts.

Guided Path
1
Learn the linguistic definition
Memorize that al-fard in Arabic means taqdir (estimation). This is the starting point for understanding its Shariah usage.
The Shariah meaning builds on this: fard is a precisely determined obligation.
2
Connect to Shariah obligations
Understand that 'mafrudat al-shar'' are the fixed obligations that do not admit increase or decrease.
This distinguishes fard from wajib in Hanafi usul.
3
Memorize the four types of taqdir
List the four categories: (1) prevents both increase and decrease, (2) prevents neither, (3) prevents increase but not decrease, (4) prevents decrease but not increase.
Each type has a specific legal example.
4
Identify examples for each type
Associate each type with its given example: hudud for type 1, unknown future for type 2, khiyar al-shart for type 3, madd al-safar for type 4.
5
Reflect on implications for fiqh
Consider how the fixity of fard obligations impacts the derivation of rulings and the limits of human reasoning.
This is foundational for Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في أقسام الحكم التكليفي:
الفرض لغة: هو التقدير، ومفروضات الشرع مقدّراته بحيث لا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان.
اعلم أن التقديرات على أربعة أنواع: منها: ما يمنع الزيادة والنقصان وهو الحدود، ومنها ما لا يمنع الزيادة والنقصان كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا تَدْرِي نَفْسٌ مَاذَا تَكْسِبُ غدا﴾، ومنها: ما هو يمنع الزيادة دون النقصان وهو خيار الشرط عند أبي حنيفة له. ومنها: ما يمنع النقصان النقصان دون الزيادة كمدة السفر كذا قيل.
Chapter on the Divisions of Taklifi Ruling:
Al-Fard linguistically: it is al-taqdir (estimation), and the obligatory matters of the Shariah are its estimations such that they do not admit increase or decrease.
Know that estimations are of four types: Among them: what prevents increase and decrease, and that is the hudud (prescribed penalties). Among them: what does not prevent increase or decrease, as Allah the Exalted said: 'And no soul knows what it will earn tomorrow.' Among them: what prevents increase but not decrease, and that is the option of condition (khiyar al-shart) according to Abu Hanifa. And among them: what prevents decrease but not increase, like the duration of travel (madd al-safar), thus it is said.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This short passage introduces the chapter on the divisions of taklifi ruling (obligatory, recommended, etc.) by first defining the term 'fard' linguistically. The author states that fard in the Arabic language means taqdir (estimation, determination). Consequently, the obligatory acts (mafrudat) of the Shariah are described as 'estimations' (muqaddarat) that are fixed and do not admit increase or decrease—they are precisely defined by the Lawgiver. The passage then digresses to explain that taqdir in Shariah can be of four types: (1) What prevents both increase and decrease, like the hudud penalties which are fixed. (2) What prevents neither increase nor decrease, like knowledge of future events (only Allah knows). (3) What prevents increase but not decrease, exemplified by khiyar al-shart (option of condition) according to Abu Hanifa—the option period can be set but not extended beyond a certain maximum. (4) What prevents decrease but not increase, like the duration of travel that shortens prayers—it has a minimum but can be extended. This explanation clarifies that the term 'fard' is not simply 'obligatory' but has a technical meaning related to precise determination.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): Linguistically: taqdir (estimation). In Shariah: what is fixed without increase or decrease.
التقدير (al-taqdir): Estimation, determination; the act of setting a precise limit.
مفروضات الشرع (mafrudat al-shar'): The obligatory matters of the Shariah, which are precisely determined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the linguistic meaning of 'al-fard'?
A) Obligation
B) Estimation (taqdir)
C) Recommendation
D) Prohibition

Key Takeaway
Fard linguistically means taqdir, and the four types of taqdir highlight how Shariah provisions are fixed in varying degrees.

Distinguishing Farḍ and Wājib in Hanafi Usul
Defines farḍ and wājib linguistically and legally, and distinguishes them based on proof certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between farḍ and wājib based on the certainty of proof, and explain the practical implications for action and belief.

Core Idea
Farḍ requires both action and belief; wājib only action — separated by the certainty of the proof.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes a foundational distinction unique to the Hanafi school: the difference between farḍ and wājib. While many schools use these terms interchangeably, Hanafis build an entire taxonomy of obligations on the certainty (qaṭʿī) or ambiguity (ẓannī) of the proof. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping later rulings on prayer, zakat, and other acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate the sharʿī (legal) definitions of farḍ and wājib in the text. Note how each is defined by the type of proof: farḍ by a decisive proof (qaṭʿī) with no ambiguity, wājib by a proof containing some ambiguity (ẓannī).
2
Compare the proofs
Farḍ is established by a qaṭʿī proof (e.g., mutawātir texts); wājib is established by a ẓannī proof (e.g., solitary reports, interpreted verses). The passage lists examples of farḍ: faith, five prayers, fasting Ramadan, zakat, hajj.
ẓannī proofs can be ambiguous in transmission, meaning, or both.
3
Determine the legal effects
Farḍ requires both action (ʿamal) and belief (iʿtiqād); wājib requires only action. Denying a farḍ leads to kufr; denying a wājib does not.
This is the key practical consequence.
4
Understand the cross-madhhab dimension
The Shafiʿī school does not distinguish between farḍ and wājib, considering it a verbal dispute. The Hanafis maintain the distinction, affecting rulings like witr (wājib in Hanafi, farḍ in Shafiʿī).
The passage notes that Hanafis sometimes use the terms interchangeably in common speech but maintain the technical difference.
5
Apply to an example
Recognize that witr is wājib, not farḍ, in the Hanafi school. This means omitting it does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw).
This example illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرض لغة: هو التقدير، ومفروضات الشرع مقدراته بحيث لا يحتمل الزيادة والنقصان.
وفي الشرع: ما ثبت بدليل قطعي لا شبهة فيه.
وحكمه: لزوم العمل به والاعتقاد به.
الفرض حتى يكفر جاحده.
فصل في أقسام الحكم التكليفي
والوجوب هو السقوط يعني ما يسقط على العبد بلا اختيار منه، وقيل: هو من أي العبد الوجبة، وهو الاضطراب سُمِّي الواجب بذلك؛ لكونه مضطرباً بين الفرض والنفل.
الواجب: وفي الشرع وهو ما ثبت بدليل فيه شبهة، كالآية المؤولة، بدليل قطعي كالكتاب الغير المؤولة، والسنة المتواترة، وإجماع الصحابة له المنقول بالتواتر، وذلك مثل الإيمان، والصلوات الخمس، وصوم رمضان والزكاة والحج، فإنها تثبت بدلائل قطعية. [عمدة الحواشي: ص۲۳۹] والوجوب إلخ ولم يفرق الشافعي محله بينه وبين الفرض، والظاهر أنه نزاع لفظي كما بسط التفتازاني الله في "التلويح"، وإنما هو اختصام في إطلاق اللفظ، والحنفية أيضاً يطلقون أحدهما على الآخر كقولهم: الحج واجب والزكاة واجبة إلى غير ذلك من المواضع، والوجوب: هو السقوط، ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿إِذَا وَجَبَتْ جُنُوبُها أي: سقط على الأرض كذا في "الحصول".
لكونه مضطرباً إلخ فإن الوجوب شرعاً كان مضطرباً بين الفرض والنفل، فمن حيث أنه غير لازم الاعتقاد كالوتر عندنا يشابه النفل كذا في "الفصول". وهو ما ثبت أي ،لزومه، وإنما قيدنا بذلك؛ لئلا تدخل السنن والمستحبات والمباحات الثابتة بالدلائل الظنية. بدليل فيه إلخ : أي بدليل شرعي من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، القياس ظني جاء فيه الظنية لعروض شبهة في القطعي كالتأويل والتقييد والتخصيص في النصوص الكتابية، وكاحتمال كذب الراوي ووهمه ونسيانه في الأحاديث، وكذا في الإجماع، والمنقول بالآحاد، أو لتمكن الشهبة في صلبه وأصله كالقياس الاجتهادي والإجماع السكوتي، والدليل الظني قد يكون ظني الطريق والدلالة معاً كخبر الواحد المؤول ،والمختص، وقد يكون ظني الطريق دون الدلالة كخبر الواحد إذا كان نصاً في جواب المسألة قاطعاً فيه بلا احتمال خلافه، وقد يكون ظني الدلالة دون الطريق كالآية المؤولة والمخصصة، ثم هذا الحد يشتمل أدنى نوعي الفرض وهو "الفرض العملي؛ لأن في دليله شبهة ولذا يثبت بالآحاد أيضاً كقدر الناصية في الرأس، والقعدة الأخيرة في الصلاة وغير ذلك كثير، كوجوب الترتيب بين الفوائت، فارتفعت الاختلافات في أمثالها بثبوتها بالظني كذا في "الحصول".
مسح
Farḍ linguistically: it is estimation, and the ordained duties of the law are its estimations such that they do not admit increase or decrease. In law: what is established by a decisive proof without any ambiguity. Its ruling: obligation to act upon it and believe in it. Farḍ: its denier becomes an infidel. Chapter on the divisions of the obligating ruling. Wājib: its meaning is 'falling', i.e., what falls upon the servant without his choice. It is said: it is from 'wajaba' meaning 'to be agitated'; the obligatory is so named because it is agitated between farḍ and nafl. Wājib: In law, it is what is established by a proof containing some ambiguity, like an interpreted verse. (The previous sentence is incomplete.) By a decisive proof like the book that is not interpreted, the mutawātir sunna, and the consensus of the Companions transmitted by tawātur. Such as faith, the five prayers, fasting Ramadan, zakāh, and Hajj; these are established by decisive proofs. [ʿUmdat al-Ḥawāshī: p. 239] And wājib etc. Al-Shāfiʿī did not differentiate between it and farḍ, and apparently it is a verbal dispute as al-Taftāzānī elaborated in al-Talwīḥ. It is merely a dispute in terminology. The Ḥanafīs also sometimes use one term for the other, as they say: Hajj is wājib, zakāh is wājiba, etc. And wājib means 'falling', from Allah's saying: 'when their sides fall' meaning fall to the ground as in al-Ḥuṣūl. Because it is agitated etc. For wājib in law is agitated between farḍ and nafl, so insofar as it does not necessitate belief (like witr with us), it resembles nafl as in al-Fuṣūl. It is what is established (its bindingness), and we restrict it thus so as not to include sunan, mustaḥabbāt, and mubāḥāt that are established by speculative proofs. By a proof containing ambiguity, i.e., a legal proof from the Book, Sunna, Ijmāʿ, or qiyās that is speculative. Ambiguity occurs due to a doubt in the decisive, like interpretation, restriction, specification in scriptural texts, and the possibility of the narrator's lying, error, or forgetfulness in hadiths, and similarly in Ijmāʿ transmitted by āḥād, or because of doubt in the root of the proof itself, like ijtihādī qiyās and silent Ijmāʿ. The speculative proof may be speculative both in transmission and meaning, like an interpreted and specified solitary report; it may be speculative in transmission but not in meaning, like a solitary report that is a clear text on the issue; it may be speculative in meaning but not in transmission, like an interpreted and specified verse. Then this definition includes the lower of the two types of farḍ, which is 'practical farḍ'; because there is ambiguity in its proof, so it is also established by solitary reports, such as the amount of the forelock in wiping, the last sitting in prayer, and many others like the obligation of order among missed prayers; thus differences are removed in such matters by their establishment by speculative evidence. As in al-Ḥuṣūl. (Margin note: 'masḥ'?)
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a foundational usul definition section that clarifies the Hanafi distinction between farḍ and wājib. It begins with the linguistic meaning of farḍ (estimation) and then gives its sharʿī definition: something established by a qaṭʿī (definitive) proof free from any ambiguity. The ruling is that it must be acted upon and believed in, and its denier becomes a disbeliever. The text then moves to wājib, explaining its linguistic root (wajaba: to fall) and noting that it is called 'obligatory' because it oscillates between farḍ and nafl. Its sharʿī definition is that it is established by a proof that contains some shubha (ambiguity), such as an interpreted verse. The commentary clarifies that the Shafiʿī school does not distinguish between farḍ and wājib, considering the difference a mere verbal dispute. However, the Hanafīs maintain a distinction: farḍ requires both ʿamal (action) and iʿtiqād (belief), while wājib requires only action, not binding belief. The passage elaborates on types of ẓannī (speculative) proofs, showing that they can be speculative in transmission, meaning, or both. Importantly, it notes that the lower type of farḍ (farḍ ʿamalī) is established by ẓannī proofs (like solitary reports), even though farḍ in the higher sense requires qaṭʿī proof. Examples given include the amount of hair to wipe in wuḍūʾ and the last sitting in prayer. This explains many subsidiary fiqh rulings where obligations are established by ẓannī evidence.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-farḍ): Something established by a definitive proof (qaṭʿī) with no ambiguity, requiring both action and belief.
الواجب (al-wājib): Something established by a speculative proof (ẓannī) containing ambiguity, requiring action but not binding belief.
الحكم التكليفي (al-ḥukm al-taklīfī): Divine address requiring a Mukallaf to do something, refrain, or have a choice; farḍ and wājib are subcategories.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It requires both action and belief
B) It requires action but not binding belief
C) It is recommended but not obligated
D) It is only binding if proven by a definitive text

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between farḍ and wājib hinges on the certainty of the proof (qaṭʿī vs ẓannī), affecting both the obligation to believe and the consequence of denial.

The Hanafi Definition of Sunnah and Its Types
Defines sunnah, its rulings, and distinguishes its types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sunnah, distinguish between sunnah muakkadah and za'ida, and explain the ruling for abandoning each.

Core Idea
Sunnah is a commendable path; muakkadah sunnah demands action with blame for abandonment, za'ida is like nafl.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi defines the term 'sunnah' as understood in the Hanafi school and explains its legal classification. It clarifies that not all sunan are equal: some are emphatic (muakkadah) and carry a stronger obligation, while others are merely recommended (za'ida). Understanding this distinction is critical for correctly applying Hanafi fiqh rulings, especially in matters of worship where missing a muakkadah sunnah requires compensation or incurs blame.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition and Scope
Locate the Arabic definition of sunnah in the passage: 'الطريقة المسلوكة المرضية في باب الدين'. Note that it includes both the Prophet's and the Companions' practices.
The definition is broad, covering all commendable religious paths.
2
Analyze the Ruling (Hukm)
Find the statement on the ruling: one is required to revive it and deserves blame for leaving it without excuse. Understand that this applies to muakkadah sunnah, not za'ida.
The ruling includes blameworthiness (lai'mah) but not disbelief.
3
Distinguish Muakkadah vs. Za'ida
Notice the two types: muakkadah (emphatic) established by prophetic constancy and disapproval of abandonment; za'ida (non-emphatic) not constantly practiced. Their rulings differ.
The passage specifies that muakkadah has a ruling similar to wajib in practice.
4
Examine the Evidence (Dalil)
The hadith 'عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء' is cited. Recognize that it is ahad (zanni al-thubut), which affects the level of obligation.
The zanni nature prevents the ruling from reaching the level of fard.
5
Connect to Practical Examples
The passage mentions examples like witr, sadaqat al-fitr, and tarawih. Relate these to the types of sunnah.
Tarawih is considered sunnah because it was established by the caliphs, per the hadith.

And Sunnah: it is an expression for the followed commendable path in the matter of religion, whether it is from the Messenger of Allah or from the Companions. Ali said: 'Adhere to my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs after me, cling to it with your molar teeth.' Its ruling is like that of fard in action: it must be done, cannot be left, and the one who leaves it without excuse is sinful (fasiq) but not a disbeliever, due to the ambiguity preventing that. Sometimes obligation is established by the Prophet's continuous practice if it is accompanied by disapproval of the one who leaves it, as verified by al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam. The muakkadah sunnah excludes the non-emphatic sunan and nafl. 'Adhere to my Sunnah': narrated by Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi. From this hadith, many imams established the sunniyya of tarawih as it is the Sunnah of the three later Caliphs. Its ruling also: excuse like illness, forgetfulness, sleep, and travel as it is said it remains recommended (mandub) not muakkad. This ruling is for the muakkadah: deprivation of intercession for persistence in abandoning it. As for the non-emphatic sunan, their ruling is like nafl and mustahabb. What is meant by the absolute term is the sunan al-huda, i.e., the muakkadah, established by the Prophet's continuous practice, and occasional abandonment does not harm it.

Commentary
This passage defines 'sunnah' in Hanafi usul. It begins by noting that the correct from ahad reports has a certain ruling. Then it defines sunnah as a commendable path in religion, whether from the Prophet or the Companions, quoting the hadith of 'Ali about adhering to the Sunnah and the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Its ruling: one is required to revive it and is blameworthy for abandoning it without excuse. The commentary explains that the evidence for sunnah is zanni in transmission, and examples include specific practices like reciting al-Fatiha and a surah, witr, udhiyah, sadaqat al-fitr. In terms of action, its ruling is like fard (must be done, cannot be left), but the one who leaves it is not a disbeliever. The text distinguishes between muakkadah (emphatic) and non-emphatic sunan. Muakkadah sunan are established by the Prophet's continuous practice and disapproval of abandonment. Non-emphatic sunan have the ruling of nafl. The hadith evidence for sunniyya of tarawih is mentioned. The discussion includes that the person who abandons sunnah muakkadah without excuse becomes sinful and may be deprived of intercession. The passage clarifies that occasional abandonment does not harm the status of the sunnah.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): الطريقة المسلوكة المرضية في باب الدين (the commendable followed path in religion)
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): ما واظب عليه النبي مع التغليظ على تاركه (what the Prophet constantly practiced with censure for the abandoner)
سنة زائدة (sunnah za'ida): ما لم يواظب عليه النبي (what the Prophet did not constantly practice)

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
beginner
6 min
Definition and Ruling of Nafal
Defines nafal and clarifies its legal effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the linguistic and Shariah definitions of nafal and apply the ruling that nafal acts are rewarded but not punishable upon omission.

Core Idea
Nafal: increase over the obligatory; rewarded if done, no sin if left.

This passage introduces one of the key categories of acts in Hanafi usul: nafal. Understanding nafal distinguishes what is mandatory from what is voluntarily rewarded. The text builds the definition from the linguistic root (increase) and links it to spoils of war, then clarifies the legal ruling. We will dissect this definition step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic meaning
The author states that nafal linguistically means 'increase' (ziyadah). Spoils of war are called nafal because they are an increase over the primary goal of jihad (reward).
Linguistic meaning often illuminates the Shariah meaning.
2
Extract the Shariah definition
In Shariah, nafal is defined as 'an increase over the obligatory acts (fara'id and wajibat)' – i.e., acts of worship beyond what is required.
This definition excludes obligatory acts and includes all voluntary acts.
3
State the legal ruling
The ruling is: a person is rewarded (yuthabu) for performing nafal, and not punished (la yu'aqabu) for leaving it.
This is the core hukm: it distinguishes nafal from wajib (sin if left) and haram (sin if done).
4
Note the synonym
The text explicitly states that nafal and tatawwu' are synonyms (naziran). Both refer to voluntary acts of worship.
This avoids confusion with other terms like sunnah or mustahabb.
5
Differentiate from fard and wajib
Unlike fard (obligatory) and wajib (necessary), omission of nafal carries no sin. This is the key legal consequence.
In Hanafi usul, the five categories (fard, wajib, sunnah, nafal, haram, etc.) are distinguished by reward and punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنفل: عبارة عن الزيادة، والغنيمة تسمى نفلاً؛ لأنها زيادة على ما هو المقصود من وهو الثواب في الآخرة الجهاد، وفي الشرع عبارة عما هو زيادة على الفرائض والواجبات. أي عن عبادة وحكمه: أن يُثَابَ المرء على فعله ولا يُعاقب بتركه، والنفل والتطوع نظيران
And Nafal: it is an expression of increase. Spoils of war are called nafal because they are an increase over what is intended from jihad, which is reward in the Hereafter. In the Shariah, it is an expression of what is an increase over the obligatory acts (fara'id and wajibat), i.e., acts of worship. And its ruling: that a person is rewarded for doing it and not punished for leaving it. And nafal and tatawwu' are synonyms.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage defines 'Nafal' as any supererogatory act of worship beyond the obligatory. It notes that in linguistic usage, 'nafal' means increase, and spoils of war are called nafal because they are an additional gain beyond the primary objective of jihad (which is reward). The legal ruling is simple: one gets reward for performing nafal, but no punishment for leaving it. The text also confirms that 'nafal' and 'tatawwu'' are synonyms in Shariah, both referring to voluntary acts.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Increase; in Shariah, supererogatory acts of worship beyond the obligatory.
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Voluntary act of worship; synonym of nafal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of performing a nafal act?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is rewarded, and leaving it is punishable.
C) It is rewarded, and leaving it is not punishable.
D) It is discouraged.

Key Takeaway
Nafal acts are defined as voluntary worship beyond fard and wajib; they earn reward but no sin upon omission.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
